# Analysis of the sermon
*Source: KASHKOLE, Binder 6 (Ali ibn Abi Talib), Chapter 141. 25 topics. Language: ur.*<!-- section 1 (id=3577, raw_sort=1): عقل اور توحید -->There is a difference between intellect and reasoning. ** Intellect is the name of an 'infinite' potential that can fly beyond this mortal world, to the 'spiritual world', and can encompass the realities there. Reasoning, on the other hand, is a 'finite' force that moves from one subject to another using logic and works within the realm of mental conceptions. With the light of reason, man can see absolute realities, whereas through reasoning he can think only to some extent about these absolute realities. The power of reasoning is the servant of the intellect, and it is a resource, which the intellect uses according to its needs. 

Absolute reality is something that just is, e.g. Quran

### Intentions and Actions:

At the moment when the Battle of Jamal was about to begin, a Bedouin man came to Amir al-Mu'minin and said, "O Ali! **Do you say that God is one**? People stopped him, saying it wasn't the right time to ask the question. Maulana Ali told them all to leave him alone and let them ask, "Surely this man wants to know, we are fighting for him, so that people may know!" With this statement, he made clear the superiority of intention over action, and explained that knowing about the Absolute Truth and its monotheism is the purpose of every action, regardless of its outward appearance (acts of worship, tasbihat, war, etc.). And the fact is ⟪ar:توحید رب العزت،⟫that it has always been the intention of every outward act of Ali (a.s.). And your statement that "so that people know" is an argument that the real motivation ⟪ar:علم⟫for every intention, thought, thought, and movement is, whether it is a battlefield or a mosque. Therefore, the question of whether Allah is one is permissible at all times and in all places! In Ali's time, the three wars (⟪ar:جمل⟫, ⟪ar:نحروان⟫⟪ar:صفین⟫, ) were fought in response to this question. As the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings of Allaah be upon him) said, "O Ali! You will fight for the interpretation of the Qur'an as I have fought for the revelation of the Qur'an.

### Unity of Right:

At the same time, he delivered a wonderful sermon on the monotheism of Allah on the battlefield. He said to the Bedouin that it is not permissible to call Allah 'one' in the sense of number and counting, because He who has no parallel cannot be included in terms of number and counting. And not only that he cannot be called a partner because he ⟪ar:لا ثانی⟫exists, but that there can be no other like him.

That's it⟪ar:’الحق المبین‘⟫. Beyond everything in the universe, it is manifest to everything. At the same time, it is both inaccessible and inevitable. With this quote, you have made it clear to those who have insight that there should not be an assumption that He is 'one' God in comparison to many gods, but that He alone is the '⟪ar:الحق⟫real reality' and that everything else is just pretense and deception.

Notes ·
In Arabic, the word Ayat means sign or sign. And each sign points to the maker of that mark. For example, there are verses in the sand about the horse's footprints, the horse's existence and its presence in that place. Likewise, smoke is a verse for fire.  · In Arabic, the word Ayat means sign or sign. And each sign points to the maker of that mark. Everything is made for ⟪ar:’آیت‘⟫ the existence of 'Allah'; a sign and an argument that points to His ⟪ar:’ھو‘⟫ presence. And the same meaning of the word ⟪ar:تاویل⟫ is, 'the one who returns to the first'.  He is the First, He is the Last, He is the Outward One, He is the Inner, and all the outward abundance returns to ⟪ar:’وحدانیت‘⟫ Him One and the other⟪ar:’أحدیت‘⟫, as Allaah says (interpretation of the meaning):

> ⟪quran 41:53⟫
> ⟪ar:‏سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَتِنَا فِى ٱلأٓفَاقِ وَفِىٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ حَتَّىٰ يَتَبَيَّنَ لَهُمْ أَنَّهُ ٱلْحَقُّ ۗ أَوَلَمْ يَكْفِ بِرَبِّكَ أَنَّهُۥ عَلَىٰ كُلِّ شَىْءٍۢ شَهِيدٌ ‎⟫
> *&nbsp;We will show them Our Signs in the universe, and in their ownselves, until it becomes manifest to them that this (the Quran) is the truth. Is it not sufficient in regard to your Lord that He is a Witness over all things?*
> We will show them Our signs in the world and in their own souls until it becomes clear to them that it is the truth. Is it not sufficient that their Lord is a witness over all things?
> — **Quran 41:53 (inline widget)**

In this verse, Allaah has used the words "Verses" and "Afs" which are plural clauses. But for the truth, the singular and the symbol of knowledge (⟪ar:ال⟫) have been used, which indicates that the multiplicity of all the signs of the universe and the soul return to the one truth which is one!

There is an uneasiness and movement within the human being that leads us to the bliss of one-ness. The need to always strive for the bliss of oneness

Jung

### Qur'an and Interpretation:

For this reason, the Qur'an is one, but each verse has multiple interpretations.

Interpretation ·
Likewise, Ali is one, and the Imams of his descendants, who have become 'verses' for him, are many.  · Likewise, Ali is one, and the Imams of his descendants, who have become 'verses' for him, are many.
· Likewise, Ali is one, and the Imams of his descendants, who have become 'verses' for him, are many.

⟪ar:امام جعفر الصادق علیہ السلام⟫He said to one of his companions, "If I wish, I can tell you seventy interpretations of each verse of the Qur'an." ⟪ar:محمد مصطفی صلی اللہ علیہ و آلہ و سلم⟫Allah taught him the interpretation of the Qur'an, and then he taught Ali the same interpretation, and then the Messenger of Allah said, ⟪ar-quote:علی مع القرآن و القرآن مع العلی⟫ "Ali is with the Qur'an and the Qur'an is with Ali." Ali said to Hazrat Abbas, "If I tell you ⟪ar:سورۃ الفاتحۃ⟫the interpretation, seventy camels will be loaded with books."  Ali is the true interpreter of the Qur'an.

Interpretation ·
The Qur'an is a book written between two volumes. These two volumes are Muhammad and Ali, and all the pages in the middle refer to the Imams (a.s.) who are from their descendants.  · The Qur'an is a book written between two volumes. These two volumes are Muhammad and Ali, and all the pages in the middle refer to the Imams (a.s.) who are from their descendants.
· The Qur'an is a book written between two volumes. These two volumes are Muhammad and Ali, and all the pages in the middle refer to the Imams (a.s.) who are from their descendants.

### Reason, Revelation, Spirit:

Allah's revelation (the Book of the Qur'an) ⟪ar:’صامت‘⟫ is mute and does not speak in its own language. It needs an interpreter to explain its meaning (⟪ar:لا بُدَّ لَہُ مِن تَرجُماَن⟫). Likewise, to understand the divine messages (revelation), an interpreter or messenger is needed, which is 'intellect'. ⟪ar:وحی⟫The connection between them ⟪ar:عقل⟫is also evident ⟪ar-quote:رسول الرجل ترجمان عقلہ⟫ from the saying of the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings of Allaah be upon him): "The Messenger of man is the interpreter of his intellect." He is a messenger sent by the intellect of man.⟪ar:’حق‘⟫ And that is why every word of Maulana Ali reflects the Qur'an. Every word of yours moves from the words of the Qur'an to its revelation, from the revelation to its soul, and from the soul to the one who reveals it. His statement returns the words of the Qur'an through all these stages to its origin and origin⟪ar:عقل اول⟫. Therefore, the one who revealed this word (the Qur'an) is simultaneously hidden in your statements (in terms of its meaning) and is also manifest through words. ⟪ar:’الہ‘⟫ It cannot be understood or described; only through the impressions of its creations its existence and appearance can be acknowledged.

power hierarchies - giving children power over parents

power imbalance

Revelation and intellect are apparently two distinct objects, which scholars divide into two different categories:

| Revelation | Mind |
| --- | --- |
| Convention Tradition | Nature |
| Imitation Imitation | Research Verification |
| Piety | Get Inquiry |

But in reality, the two are close to each other. There is complementarity and complementarity of one to the other. These two different objects join together to form one object, which is the main purpose of the object⟪ar:توحید⟫, since ⟪ar:’توحید‘⟫ it literally means 'to make one or to make one'. An example of this is the emergence of a truth or truth through a combination of negation and affirmation. For example, if the truth is that Ahmad has one goat, then it can only be fulfilled by denying that Ahmad does not have two goats.

This combination of intellect and revelation, to which the 'one' reality points to, is that ⟪ar:’روح‘⟫ which is between the two. The intellect is limited in its vastness (without the soul) and cannot resist revelation. But the soul, which is the driver of this intellect, is unlimited in its vastness. Only the soul can receive the messages of revelation, be aware of it, and test its high quality. It receives the messages of revelation and conveys it to the intellect, and the intellect processes it and processes it.  If this were not the case, revelation would have become the name of innumerable rules and regulations for human will, instead of being a creative inspiration for the intellect.

> — *Image text (from image 001; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at .. /images/001.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

Revelation, which is multidimensional, cannot be confined to a single dimension of words. The Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings of Allaah be upon him) clothed the Revelation of Allah with words so that spirituality could take on a physical nature and man could see, hear and read it with the five senses. And here the connection between revelation and intellect is established, that instead of confinement the meaning in words, the intellect frees the meaning from the confinement of words. ** Through it, the outward appearance of words produces countless streams of inner meaning, as it is mentioned in the story of Moses that when Moses struck the stone with a stick (intellect), twelve springs of meaning gushed forth from it.

> ⟪quran 2:60⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ وَإِذِ ٱسْتَسْقَىٰ مُوسَىٰ لِقَوْمِهِۦ فَقُلْنَا ٱضْرِب بِّعَصَاكَ ٱلْحَجَرَ ۖ فَٱنفَجَرَتْ مِنْهُ ٱثْنَتَا عَشْرَةَ عَيْنًۭا ۖ قَدْ عَلِمَ كُلُّ أُنَاسٍۢ مَّشْرَبَهُمْ ۖ كُلُوا۟ وَٱشْرَبُوا۟ مِن رِّزْقِ ٱللَّهِ وَلَا تَعْثَوْا۟ فِى ٱلْأَرْضِ مُفْسِدِينَ ‎⟫
> *And (remember) when Musa (Moses) asked for water for his people, We said: "Strike the stone with your stick." Then gushed forth therefrom twelve springs. Each (group of) people knew its own place for water. "Eat and drink of that which Allah has provided and do not act corruptly, making mischief on the earth." *
> When Moses prayed for water for his people, We said, 'Strike the rock with your staff.' Thereupon twelve springs gushed forth from it, and each tribe knew its drinking-place. Eat and drink of God's provision, and do not act corruptly on the earth, making mischief.
> — **Quran 2:60 (inline widget)**

The more talent and delicacy the soul has, the more it will be able to grasp the content of this revelation and the more high-meaning pearls it will be able to extract from this one shell. The intellect is the inner messenger (or inner consciousness) through which a person can empirically confirm and confirm the divine messages of revelation. If this were not the case, then man (the soul) is forced to accept the message of revelation only dogmatically.

For this reason, Amir al-Mu'minin told Hazrat Kamil that one of the reasons for sending Allah's prophets was to reveal the hidden treasures of the intellect. The intellect is alive and awakened by revelation. Revelation is, in fact, a voice that reaches to the spiritual depths of the intellect, through which the seeds of consciousness are awakened and flourished, which Allah has sown in it on the eternal day. Revelation cannot be obtained from anything other than the intellect, and the treasures hidden under the earth of the intellect cannot be revealed except by revelation. From this point of view, we see an eternal connection between intellect and revelation, whereby the two can be described as analogous, or at least intellect can be said to be a form of revelation.

  (image preserved at .. /images/002.png)
