Maulana Ali's statement in which he has mentioned the reason for the sending of the Prophets is the extraction of the hidden treasures of the intellect, proves that the spiritual intellect of any human being cannot be ignorant of the message of revelation but recognizes it because the message of Allah is in accordance with the essence of his intellect. Since both have the same origin, the intellect recognizes the source and origin of the revelation that it is from the Divine Message ⟪ar:’الہ الحقیقی‘⟫ . The divine messages (revelation) of the prophets awaken the intellect, so these messages cannot be considered separate from the intellect, rather these messages are the real purpose and purpose of the intellect. So that ⟪ar:’روح‘⟫ he may receive these divine messages through the intellect and inculcate them in himself in such a way that the two become one. When this happens, the heart becomes able to 'see' Allah. Allah cannot be seen with the eyes, only through the heart, which is called Amir al-Mu'minin ⟪ar:’حق الیقین‘⟫ .<!-- section 2 (id=3599, raw_sort=2): عقل اور استدلال کا فرق -->There is a kind of continuity between the power of intellect and the power of reasoning, and in a way, the two are separate and separate. Continuity is in the sense that every thought and idea begins with a meaningful concept. The power of reasoning leads to ideas that are logical and based on reality. She ⟪ar:مفارقۃ⟫proceeds through (paradox), ⟪ar:تناقض⟫(antinomies), ⟪ar:نفی⟫(negation) and ⟪ar:اثبات⟫(assertion) and cultivates the hidden treasures of the intellect through these instruments. But there is a 'limit' to this thinking that she cannot move on. Its limits are limited to physical matters and it cannot enter into spiritual realms. In order to enter these spiritual realms, he needs an external guide, which ⟪ar:’وحی‘⟫ he is, and whom he can understand as the inner messenger who is⟪ar:’عقل‘⟫.  Through this companion, the intellect steps into the realm of spirituality. Therefore, when ⟪ar:’الہ‘⟫ Maulana Ali rejects the concepts related to him, he does so because of the lack and weakness of the power of Asadlal; This spiritual or spiritual concept becomes the beginning of evoking and absorbing the consciousness hidden in the intellect that is beyond the limits of reason. Thus the negation of the finite human imagination forms the basis for the confession of infinite divinity (impasse). It is negation that leads to highs, not destructive that leads to lows. This contradiction ⟪ar:نہج البلاغۃ⟫ of negation and affirmation is found in his saying, in which he praises Allah and says:

| {{IMG_URL:.. /images/quote_open.gif}} Praise be to Allah, whose praise is not attained by those who say, and whose blessings are not counted, and whose diligent people do not perform His duty, who does not realize it after determination, and who does not attain the diving of understanding, whose attribute has no limit, no adjective, no limited time, and no extended time. He created the creatures by His power, and He spread the winds by His mercy, and He swallowed the field of IMG_URL His land with rocks. /images/quote_closed.gif}} |
| --- |

We see this paradox in Amir al-Mu'minin's statement (and many other sayings) that Allah is praiseworthy, but He cannot be praised, His blessings are present but cannot be counted, even though all other things can be counted.  It is obligatory to fulfill the right of Allah, but it cannot be fulfilled. We see such contradictory obligations in many of your quotes.

Divine attributes cannot⟪ar:لیس لصفاتہ حد محدود⟫ be defined, nor can they be described, but they still exist. The Qur'an itself describes the attributes of Allah as is⟪ar:’کریم‘⟫, is⟪ar:’عزیز‘⟫, ⟪ar:’رحیم‘⟫ and is, but Maulana Ali says that none of these attributes can be determined. God is gracious, but by how much? And how much cream is it? A cream like me, or a cream like you, or a cream like this? Or a cream like them?

He says, "⟪ar:أخلاص⟫It comes from the negation of all His attributes from Allah." On the one hand, we have to acknowledge the attributes of Allah and on the other hand, we have to deny these attributes. The problem is that the human mind can think of God through these attributed words. But Ali (a.s.) negates these attributes and leaves no way for us to grasp the concept of Allah. If it is possible to identify his attributes by these words, and if we are to negate these attributes, then what should a person do? But from this contradiction of your affirmation and negation, a new and deeper level of knowledge emerges and the hidden treasures of the intellect are awakened, and man is forced to think that the knowledge of Allah is greater than our powers of thinking, thought, reasoning, reasoning, etc., which only the soul can feel, but the intellect cannot understand! He says, "My Lord cannot be imprisoned in dimensions, motion, time and space, He is subtle but not subtle, magnificent but not in majesty, great but not in majesty."

Here again, he acknowledges the attributes of Allah and denies them. Allah is the owner of these attributes, but He cannot be imprisoned in these attributes, and He cannot be reduced to our imaginations and thoughts. These attributes provide a concept for the intellect to some extent, but this concept is weak and incomplete, and in order to acknowledge the perfection of these attributes, they must be negated (due to the defect of the concept). It is from the combination of the dimensions and dimensions of negation and affirmation that the depth of 'knowledge' is created. But this depth cannot be established unless it is acknowledged that these dimensions of dimensions (negation) and dimensions (positives) are not sufficient to accurately reflect this picture. To deny all attributes is to 'confess' His infinite self, which is the real purpose of the Universe⟪ar:کلمۃ اخلاص، لا الہ الا اللہ⟫. In order for any kind of concept to be established in the human mind, it is necessary to close the definition. And where there is a definition, there will be limits and exclusions. But the definition of divine attributes is free from these limitations and exclusions because they are the infinite 'attributes' of the infinite 'essence'. Therefore, in a sense, we can put all the attributes in the place of negation in the word of sincerity and then recite the Kalimah, '⟪ar:⟪ar:’لا رحمن الا اللہ‘⟫La Rahim illa Allah' ⟪ar:’لا عظیم الا اللہ‘⟫ ⟪ar:’لا کریم الا اللہ‘⟫, etc. In this way, the apparent negation of our attributes becomes an affirmation of their identity. All these attributes are not externally attached to his self, but are part of his essence, which can be distinguished only by ⟪ar:’علم الوجود‘⟫ mental conceptions.  For this reason, Allaah Himself says (interpretation of the meaning):

> ⟪quran 23:91⟫
> ⟪ar:‏مَا ٱتَّخَذَ ٱللَّهُ مِن وَلَدٍۢ وَمَا كَانَ مَعَهُۥ مِنْ إِلَهٍ ۚ إِذًۭا لَّذَهَبَ كُلُّ إِلَهٍۭ بِمَا خَلَقَ وَلَعَلَا بَعْضُهُمْ عَلَىٰ بَعْضٍۢ ۚ سُبْحَنَ ٱللَّهِ عَمَّا يَصِفُونَ ‎⟫
> *No son (or offspring or children) did Allah beget, nor is there any ilah (god) along with Him; (if there had been many gods), behold, each god would have taken away what he had created, and some would have tried to overcome others! Glorified be Allah above all that they attribute to Him!*
> Allah has not begotten a son, nor is there any god besides Him; if there were, each god would have taken away what he had created, and some of them would have risen above others. Glory be to Allah, that which they describe.
> — **Quran 23:91 (inline widget)**

God's 'infinity' deserves to be freed from all imaginary constraints, but the 'heart' is not incapable of knowing Him. He can see it through his own eyes. The heart has always been the center of rational thought and wisdom and the intellect has been in need of it for its purification. ⟪ar:’ذکر اللہ‘⟫ In fact, it is the source of purity of the intellect and that is why Ali says, "The remembrance of Allah is the best form of worship." But here too we see a paradox that ⟪ar:ذکر⟫reality cannot be attained unless the worshipper 'loses' himself in the remembrance of Allah. Losing it here does not mean the cessation of his intellect, but the loss of his soul in the remembrance of Allah, which ⟪ar:’فنا بااللہ‘⟫ is his state. 

Intellect is the name of a spiritual ability and the soul is its origin and the cause of life for it. Without intellect, the soul becomes an unconscious entity, and without this true soul, the intellect is inclined to inanimate thoughts. Allaah says (interpretation of the meaning):

> ⟪quran 32:7-9⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱلَّذِىٓ أَحْسَنَ كُلَّ شَىْءٍ خَلَقَهُۥ ۖ وَبَدَأَ خَلْقَ ٱلْإِنسَنِ مِن طِينٍۢ ‎ ‏ثُمَّ جَعَلَ نَسْلَهُۥ مِن سُلَلَةٍۢ مِّن مَّآءٍۢ مَّهِينٍۢ ‎ ‏ثُمَّ سَوَّىٰهُ وَنَفَخَ فِيهِ مِن رُّوحِهِۦ ۖ وَجَعَلَ لَكُمُ ٱلسَّمْعَ وَٱلْأَبْصَرَ وَٱلْأَفْـِٔدَةَ ۚ قَلِيلًۭا مَّا تَشْكُرُونَ ‎⟫
> *Who made everything He has created good, and He began the creation of man from clay. Then He made his offspring from semen of worthless water (male and female sexual discharge). Then He fashioned him in due proportion, and breathed into him the soul (created by Allah for that person), and He gave you hearing (ears), sight (eyes) and hearts. Little is the thanks you give!*
> Who created all that He created, and He originated man from clay, then He made his progeny from an abject fluid, then He fashioned his fragments, and breathed into him of His spirit, and made for you hearing, and sight, and hearts. Little thanks do you give!
> — **Quran 32:7-9 (inline widget)**

⟪ar:’نفخ الروح‘⟫ It creates life and consciousness. If the soul is not given its due, such a life is like death. It is through this spirit that static things are animated, and unconscious objects are awakened and aware. Through this Divine Spirit, a person acquires knowledge not only about others but also about himself. It is from the combination of this 'existence' and 'knowledge' that every spiritual concept is established. When this soul is attached to the body, it comes to life, and that is why knowledge revives it, as Allah says:

> ⟪quran 8:24⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ ٱسْتَجِيبُوا۟ لِلَّهِ وَلِلرَّسُولِ إِذَا دَعَاكُمْ لِمَا يُحْيِيكُمْ ۖ وَٱعْلَمُوٓا۟ أَنَّ ٱللَّهَ يَحُولُ بَيْنَ ٱلْمَرْءِ وَقَلْبِهِۦ وَأَنَّهُۥٓ إِلَيْهِ تُحْشَرُونَ ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Answer Allah (by obeying Him) and (His) Messenger when he (PBUH) calls you to that which will give you life, and know that Allah comes in between a person and his heart (i.e. He prevents an evil person to decide anything). And verily to Him you shall (all) be gathered.*
> O you who believe! Obey Allah and the Messenger when He calls you to that matter in which you live, and know that Allah stands as a barrier between a man and his heart, and that to Him you will be gathered.
> — **Quran 8:24 (inline widget)**

Ali (a.s.) has already stated that the divine invitation in which people live is the ⟪ar:’وحی‘⟫ one that awakens and awakens the hidden treasures of the intellect. The intellect, which is the expression of the soul, is not just the name of a mental power, but it is based on 'life'.  Maulana Ali says that ⟪ar:’عاقل‘⟫ he is the one whose knowledge is not only correct but also his action is correct, and whose effort is always towards the Absolute Truth. ⟪ar:’عاقل‘⟫ Another definition of 'keeps things in their proper place';⟪ar:’عادل‘⟫ This proves that only the wise can be just, because only the one who can see things according to their reality will be able to put them in their rightful place. Correct thinking, impeccable virtue, and authentic being are things related to the intellect.<!-- section 3 (id=3578, raw_sort=3): علی کا کمیل ابن زیاد کو خطاب -->Kumayl ibn Ziyad An-Nakha'i has related that Amir al-mu'minin, peace be upon him, caught hold of my hand and took me to the graveyard. When he had passed through the graveyard and left the city behind, he took a deep sigh and said:
⟪ar-quote:قال كُمَيْل بن زياد- أخذ بيدي أميرالمؤمنين علي بن أبي طالب عليه السلام ، فأخرجني إلى الجبّان فلمّا أصحر تنفّس الصّعَدَاء ثمّ قال⟫

O Kumayl, these hearts are containers. The best of them is that which preserves (its contents). So, preserve what I say to you.

⟪ar-quote:يَا كُمَيْل بْن زِيَادٍ، إِنَّ هذهِ الْقُلُوبَ أَوْعِيَةٌ فَخَيْرُهَا أَوْعَاهَا فَاحْفَظْ عَنِّي مَا أَقُولُ لَكَ⟫

People are of three types: First is the scholar and the divine. Second is the seeker of knowledge who is also on the way to deliverance. And lastly is the common rot, who run after every caller and bend in the direction of every wind. They seek no light from the effulgence of knowledge and do not take protection of any reliable support.

⟪ar-quote:النَّاسُ ثَلاَثَةٌ- فَعَالِمٌ رَبَّانِيٌّ وَمُتَعَلِّمٌ عَلَى سَبِيلِ نَجَاةٍ، وَهَمَجٌ رَعَاعٌ أَتْبَاعُ كُلِّ نَاعِقٍ يَمِيلُونَ مَعَ كُلِّ رِيحٍ، لَمْ يَسْتَضِيئُوا بِنُورِ الْعِلْمِ، وَلَمْ يَلْجَؤُوا إِلَى رُكْنٍ وَثِيقٍ⟫

O Kumayl, knowledge is better than wealth. Knowledge guards you, while you have to guard the wealth. Wealth decreases by spending, while knowledge multiplies by spending, and the results of wealth die as wealth decays.

⟪ar-quote:يَا كُمَيْلُ، الْعِلْمُ خَيْرٌ مِنَ الْمَالِ- الْعِلْمُ يَحْرُسُكَ وَأَنْتَ تَحْرُسُ المَالَ، وَالْمَالُ تَنْقُصُهُ النَّفَقَةُ، وَالْعِلْمُ يَزْكُوعَلَى الاْنْفَاقِ، وَصَنِيعُ الْمَالِ يَزُولُ بِزَوَالِهِ⟫

O Kumayl, knowledge is belief which is acted upon. With it man acquires obedience during his life and a good name after his death. Knowledge is the ruler, while wealth is ruled upon.

⟪ar-quote:يَا كُمَيْلَ بْنَ زِيَادٍ مَعْرِفَةُ الْعِلْمِ دِينٌ يُدَانُ بِهِ . بِهِ يَكْسِبُ الْإِنْسَانُ الطَّاعَةَ فِى حَيَاتِهِ وَ جَمِيلَ الْأُحْدُوثَةِ بَعْدَ وَفَاتِهِ وَ الْعِلْمُ حَاكِمٌ وَ الْمَالُ مَحْكُومٌ عَلَيْهِ⟫

O Kumayl, those who amass wealth are dead even though they may be living; while those endowed with knowledge will remain as long as the world lives. Their bodies are not present, but their example exist in the hearts. Look, here is a heap of knowledge (and Amir al-mu'minin pointed to his chest). I wish I could get someone to bear it. Yes, I did find (someone); but either he was one who could not be relied upon. He would exploit the religion for worldly gains, and by virtue of Allah's favours on him he would domineer over the people and through Allah's pleas he would rule over His devotees. Or he was one who was obedient to the hearers of truth but there was no intelligence in his bosom. At the first appearance of doubt he would entertain misgivings in his heart.

⟪ar-quote:يَا كُمَيْلُ هَلَكَ خُزَّانُ الْأَمْوَالِ وَ هُمْ أَحْيَاءٌ وَ الْعُلَمَاءُ بَاقُونَ مَا بَقِيَ الدَّهْرُ أَعْيَانُهُمْ مَفْقُودَةٌ وَ أَمْثَالُهُمْ فِى الْقُلُوبِ مَوْجُودَةٌ هَا إِنَّ هَاهُنَا لَعِلْماً جَمّاً وَ أَشَارَ بِيَدِهِ إِلَى صَدْرِهِ لَوْ أَصَبْتُ لَهُ حَمَلَةً بَلَى أَصَبْتُ لَقِناً غَيْرَ مَأْمُونٍ عَلَيْهِ مُسْتَعْمِلًا آلَةَ الدِّينِ لِلدُّنْيَا وَ مُسْتَظْهِراً بِنِعَمِ اللَّهِ عَلَى عِبَادِهِ وَ بِحُجَجِهِ عَلَى أَوْلِيَائِهِ أَوْ مُنْقَاداً لِحَمَلَةِ الْحَقِّ لَا بَصِيرَةَ لَهُ فِى أَحْنَائِهِ يَنْقَدِحُ الشَّكُّ فِى قَلْبِهِ لِأَوَّلِ عَارِضٍ مِنْ شُبْهَةٍ⟫

So, neither this nor that was good enough. Either the man is eager for pleasures, easily led away by passions, or is covetous for collecting and hoarding wealth. Neither of them has any regard for religion in any matter. The nearest example of these is the loose cattle. This is the way that knowledge dies away with the death of its bearers.

⟪ar-quote:أَلَا لَا ذَا وَ لَا ذَاكَ أَوْ مَنْهُوماً بِاللَّذَّةِ سَلِسَ الْقِيَادِ لِلشَّهْوَةِ أَوْ مُغْرَماً بِالْجَمْعِ وَ الِادِّخَارِ لَيْسَا مِنْ رُعَاةِ الدِّينِ فِى شَيْ‏ءٍ أَقْرَبُ شَيْ‏ءٍ شَبَهاً بِهِمَا الْأَنْعَامُ السَّائِمَةُ كَذَلِكَ يَمُوتُ الْعِلْمُ بِمَوْتِ حَامِلِيهِ⟫

O My God! Yes; but the earth is never devoid of those who maintain Allah's plea either openly and reputedly or, being afraid, as hidden in order that Allah's pleas and proofs should not be rebutted. How many are they and where are they? By Allah, they are few in number, but they are great in esteem before Allah. Through them Allah guards His pleas and proofs till they entrust them to others like themselves and sow the seeds thereof in the hearts of those who are similar to them.

⟪ar-quote:اللَّهُمَّ بَلَى! لاَ تَخْلُو الاْرْضُ مِنْ قَائِمٍ لله بِحُجَّةٍ، إِمَّا ظَاهِراً مَشْهُوراً، أوْ خَائِفاً مَغْمُوراً لِئَلاَّ تَبْطُلَ حُجَجُ اللهِ وَبَيِّنَاتُهُ. وَكَمْ ذَا وَأَيْنَ أُولئِكَ؟ أُولئِكَ ـ وَاللَّهِ ـ الاْقَلُّونَ عَدَداً، وَالاْعْظَمُونَ قَدْراً، يَحْفَظُ اللهُ بِهِمْ حُجَجَهُ وَبَيِّنَاتِهِ، حَتَّى يُودِعُوهَا نُظَرَاءَهُمْ، وَيَزْرَعُوهَا فِي قُلُوبِ أَشْبَاهِهِمْ⟫

Knowledge has led them to real understanding and so they have associated themselves with the spirit of conviction. They take easy what the easygoing regard as hard. They endear what the ignorant take as strange. They live in this world with their bodies here but their spirits resting in the high above. They are the vicegerents of Allah on His earth and callers to His religion.

Oh, oh, how I yearn to see them! Go away now, O Kumayl, wherever you wish!⟪ar-quote:هَجَمَ بِهِمُ الْعِلْمُ عَلَى حَقِيقَةِ الْبَصِيرَةِ، وَبَاشَرُوا رُوحَ الْيَقِينِ، وَاسْتَلاَنُوامَا اسْتَوْعَرَهُ الْمُتْرَفُونَ وَأَنِسُوا بِمَا اسْتَوْحَشَ مِنْهُ الْجَاهِلُونَ، وَصَحِبُوا الدُّنْيَا بِأَبْدَانٍ أَرْوَاحُهَا مُعَلَّقَةٌ بِالْـمَحَلِّ الاْعْلَى، أُولئِكَ خُلَفَاءُ اللهِ فِي أَرْضِهِ، وَالدُّعَاةُ إِلَى دِينِهِ، آهِ آهِ شَوْقاً إِلَى رُؤْيَتِهِمْ! انْصَرِفْ إذَا شِئْتَ!⟫

<!-- section 4 (id=3579, raw_sort=4): علم اور بصیرت -->In this sermon, he mentions the blessed servants of Allah (Imams) and says that they are the life of Allah's religion. By "Divine Religion" you mean the religion that has come from the Almighty, which is the essence of faith, which is complete and immutable. He said, "Religion is established because of the knowledge of true scholars." That is, if they were not the scholars (Imams) of truth, all traces of religion would have been erased. Then he said, "⟪ar-quote:هَجَمَ بِهِمُ الْعِلْمُ عَلَى حَقِيقَةِ الْبَصِيرَةِ⟫(Through them, knowledge is embedded in the realities of insight)." As has been stated, although knowledge has always been hidden in the essence of the intellect, it has to be revived. And your use of the word 'Puzt' is an argument that this knowledge is hidden in the meaning hidden in the depths of words. Deeper meanings that are subordinate to superficial meanings. This quote of yours refers to different degrees of knowledge. Pointing to his chest , he said :⟪ar-quote:هَاهُنَا لَعِلْماً جَمّاً⟫ The chest obviously has the heart hidden inside, but to reach the chest to the heart, one has to go deep into the chest. Words can point to hidden truths, but they cannot encompass them.

> — *Image text (from image 003; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at .. /images/003.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

In Arabic, the word ⟪ar:’ھَجَمَ‘⟫ means 'to attack'. The purpose of attacking an army is to enter the heart of the army, which is in the middle of the army. Therefore, the word ⟪ar:ھجم⟫invites us to 'research' to attack the appearance of words and to get to the depths of the realities hidden within them. When the depths of insight are embedded, the doors of contemplation are opened for the intellect and man knows the truth of this knowledge, as the Lord says: ⟪ar-quote:من فَھِم عَلِمَ گوہر العلم⟫ "He who has created understanding has reached the essence of knowledge." It takes a struggle to reach the depth to which you say: ⟪ar-quote:بالتَّعَلُّم یَناَلُ العلم⟫ "(Knowledge is gained through education)." The purpose is that a person should inculcate this external knowledge in his own self through the intellect in such a way that the two become one. It is the power ⟪ar:’روح‘⟫ that creates this ⟪ar:’توحید‘⟫ (unification) of knowledge and essence. 

### Jihad al-Nafs:

But this can only be possible when it is devoid of egocentricity⟪ar:أنانیت⟫. Maulai Kainat says that the wise man is the one who is always fighting against these inferior tendencies, lusts and desires of his soul, because all of them transgress against the power of his knowledge. The evils of the soul are like clouds that when they overwhelm the sky of the intellect, the vision becomes weak and the reality is not clearly visible. The Qur'an describes these evils as "rust":

> ⟪quran 83:14⟫
> ⟪ar:‏كَلَّا ۖ بَلْۜ رَانَ عَلَىٰ قُلُوبِهِم مَّا كَانُوا۟ يَكْسِبُونَ ‎⟫
> *Nay! But on their hearts is the Ran (covering of sins and evil deeds) which they used to earn .*
> by no means, but their hearts are rusted by what they used to do.
> — **Quran 83:14 (inline widget)**

Although evils are morally unacceptable, if viewed from a spiritual point of view, these evils stand against them as the antithesis of God's created realities. Following them obliterates the sight and blinds the eye of the heart (from which Allah can see). A wise man is therefore engaged in a constant struggle against his desires and adopts good morals. The root of all immorality is ignorance, which one has to wage a great war against one's self to get rid of, which the Prophet (peace be upon ⟪ar:’جہاد اکبر‘⟫ him) called it.  Maulana Ali says about this⟪ar:جہاد النفس⟫:

| The wise man fights against his self through knowledge.
| --- |
| The most powerful is the one who stands against his own self.
| Indeed, those who fight against their souls in the cause of Allah, their status in the sight of Allah is that of those who are martyred.
| The ultimate battle is man's war with his own self.
| He who knows his self fights with it.
| No Jihad is Greater Than Jihad of the Self |

He says that although this war is ostensibly against the self, in reality it is for its own good.  He says⟪ar:العقل⟫, ⟪ar:رحمن⟫"He is the leader of the army and ⟪ar:الھوی⟫the leader of the army of Satan." The self is troubled between the two and is affected⟪ar:متجاذبہ بینھُما⟫ by the words of both of them, and the one who overcomes it joins his army. This shows that it is necessary to conquer the self completely in order ⟪ar:’رحمن‘⟫ to be included in the army. The goal is not the end of the self, but the end of what is ⟪ar:’ھوی‘⟫ in it. The Qur'an says that they did not speak on the basis of the Messenger⟪ar:ھوی⟫:

> ⟪quran 53:3-4⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَمَا يَنطِقُ عَنِ ٱلْهَوَىٰٓ ‎ ‏إِنْ هُوَ إِلَّا وَحْىٌۭ يُوحَىٰ ‎⟫
> *Nor does he speak of (his own) desire. It is only an Inspiration that is inspired.*
> Nor does he say anything of his own accord. It is naught but a revelation that comes to him.
> — **Quran 53:3-4 (inline widget)**

Intellect is the interpreter of the army of the Most Merciful, who fights against the army of Satan.  The word ⟪ar:الھوی⟫Allaah is mentioned in the Qur'an in another way:

> ⟪quran 25:43⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَرَءَيْتَ مَنِ ٱتَّخَذَ إِلَهَهُۥ هَوَىٰهُ أَفَأَنتَ تَكُونُ عَلَيْهِ وَكِيلًا ‎⟫
> *Have you (O Muhammad PBUH) seen him who has taken as his ilah (god) his own desire? Would you then be a Wakîl (a disposer of his affairs or a watcher) over him?*
> Have you seen him who has taken his God for his own desires? Will you then be a guardian over him?
> — **Quran 25:43 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 45:23⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَفَرَءَيْتَ مَنِ ٱتَّخَذَ إِلَهَهُۥ هَوَىٰهُ وَأَضَلَّهُ ٱللَّهُ عَلَىٰ عِلْمٍۢ وَخَتَمَ عَلَىٰ سَمْعِهِۦ وَقَلْبِهِۦ وَجَعَلَ عَلَىٰ بَصَرِهِۦ غِشَوَةًۭ فَمَن يَهْدِيهِ مِنۢ بَعْدِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ أَفَلَا تَذَكَّرُونَ ‎⟫
> *Have you seen him who takes his own lust (vain desires) as his ilah (god), and Allah knowing (him as such), left him astray, and sealed his hearing and his heart, and put a cover on his sight. Who then will guide him after Allah? Will you not then remember?*
> have you seen him who has become a slave of his own desire, and Allah has led him astray despite his knowledge, and set a seal upon his hearing and his heart, and put a covering on his sight? Who will guide him after Allah? Will you not then understand?
> — **Quran 45:23 (inline widget)**

⟪ar:’شرک خفی‘⟫ The ⟪ar:ھوی⟫Messenger of Allah (s.a.w.a ⟪ar-quote:الشرك فيكم أخفی من دبيب النمل⟫ .) said: "Shirk will be hidden among you like a spear." In order to break its ⟪ar:أنانیت⟫ idols of the self, there is a need for an external force that is not related to the self itself. They are the 'divine sciences' that come from reason and faith. ⟪ar:ھوی⟫Allaah says (interpretation of the meaning):

> ⟪quran 79:40-41⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَأَمَّا مَنْ خَافَ مَقَامَ رَبِّهِۦ وَنَهَى ٱلنَّفْسَ عَنِ ٱلْهَوَىٰ ‎ ‏فَإِنَّ ٱلْجَنَّةَ هِىَ ٱلْمَأْوَىٰ ‎⟫
> *But as for him who feared standing before his Lord, and restrained himself from impure evil desires, and lusts. Verily, Paradise will be his abode.*
> But as for him who fears to stand before his Lord, and restrain himself from lust, his abode is Paradise.
> — **Quran 79:40-41 (inline widget)**

The core energy of the soul cannot be eliminated, but it can be diverted from the myriad satanic desires and directed towards a Beneficent. Tawheed means 'to make one' or 'integration'. Allah is not only Himself ⟪ar:’أحد‘⟫ but ⟪ar:أحد⟫also the Creator. In this sense, monotheism is not only an acknowledgment of ⟪ar:أحدیت⟫Allah but also a declaration of oneself⟪ar:أحد⟫, so ⟪ar:أحد حقیقی⟫ that it can be properly reflected. To know God is to be connected with Him. One of the meanings of intellect is 'binding', because it encompasses and encompasses meaning. Unlike intellect, there is the 'heart', which ⟪ar:الحام⟫is the place of the intellect and broadcasts spiritual realities. In other words, the intellect captures and the heart radiates. Intellect is the force that binds the different elements of the soul together and unites them. For this reason, the Creator of the Universe says:

⟪ar-quote:مَنْ عَرَفَ اللہ تَوَحَّدُ⟫ (He who knows Allah becomes one with Him)*
⟪ar-quote:⟪ar-quote:مَنْ عَرَفَ⟫ Abstraction ⟫ * (He who knows his own self is separated from it)*
⟪ar-quote:⟪ar-quote:مَنْ عَرَفَ⟫ People are different⟫ * (He who knows the people is separated from them)*
⟪ar-quote:⟪ar-quote:مَنْ عَرَفَ⟫ Al-Dunya Tazhd ⟫ * (He who knows the world restrains himself from it)*

### Sincerity:

In another place, Maulana Ali calls this complete arrangement of the self with divine reality as 'Ikhlas'. The word ⟪ar:خَلُصَ⟫means to be completely purified, to descend into the essence, or to be unadulterated. In this sense, he says: ⟪ar-quote:أخلص لی اللہ العلم و العمل والحب و العداوۃ، والقبض و المغادرۃ، والنطق و الصمت⟫ "Make your knowledge and deeds, love and hatred, gain and renounce, speech and silence pure for the sake of Allah." The meaning of sincerity is to purify one's self for the sake of Allah in such a way that there is no stain left in it. Here, the stain refers to everything⟪ar:’غیر اللہ‘⟫. That is, the name of purification of other than Allah from every devotion, action, intention and passion is sincerity. The most damaging of these is the stain⟪ar:أنانیت⟫. Sincerity demands that every action, thought and existence of a person should be selfless and for the sake of Allah. You used the word final battle to emphasize the same point. Whoever develops such sincerity is a martyr in the sight of Allah, because he has killed himself in the way of Allah, and he is living his life in the light of reason and obtaining his sustenance through revelation, as He said:

> ⟪quran 3:169⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَحْسَبَنَّ ٱلَّذِينَ قُتِلُوا۟ فِى سَبِيلِ ٱللَّهِ أَمْوَتًۢا ۚ بَلْ أَحْيَآءٌ عِندَ رَبِّهِمْ يُرْزَقُونَ ‎⟫
> *Think not of those who are killed in the Way of Allah as dead. Nay, they are alive, with their Lord, and they have provision.*
> Think not of those who are slain in the way of Allah as dead.
> — **Quran 3:169 (inline widget)**

⟪ar:شہید⟫There is also another meaning of 'witness'. That is, the Creator of sincerity testifies through the sacrifice of his soul that he is with Allah and against all other than Allah. The focus of such a person is not his own self, but the center of all becomes Allah.  Thus, sincerity is the existence for the sake of Allaah, and the fullness of Allaah, as Allaah says (interpretation of the meaning):

> ⟪quran 6:162⟫
> ⟪ar:‏قُلْ إِنَّ صَلَاتِى وَنُسُكِى وَمَحْيَاىَ وَمَمَاتِى لِلَّهِ رَبِّ ٱلْعَلَمِينَ ‎⟫
> *Say (O Muhammad PBUH): "Verily, my Salat (prayer), my sacrifice, my living, and my dying are for Allah, the Lord of the 'Alamîn (mankind, jinns and all that exists).*
Say> Surely my prayer and my sacrifice and my life and my death are all for Allah, the Lord of all the worlds.
> — **Quran 6:162 (inline widget)**

### Sincerity and Prayer:

Prayer is an integral part of sincerity. The food of the human soul is worship and there is no better sustenance for it than prayer. That is why in this verse and in many other verses, Allaah mentions prayer first. If a person does not pray, he has deprived his soul of its sustenance and has not fulfilled its due. And he who is not able to fulfill his own rights will never be able to fulfill the rights of others. Whoever sets things right between himself and Allah, Allah will set things right between him and His servants. Here is also the verse of the Qur'an:

> ⟪quran 15:99⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱعْبُدْ رَبَّكَ حَتَّىٰ يَأْتِيَكَ ٱلْيَقِينُ ‎⟫
> *And worship your Lord until there comes unto you the certainty (i.e. death).*
> and worship your Lord until there comes to you certainty.
> — **Quran 15:99 (inline widget)**

If the hidden treasures of the intellect are to be awakened, then it is necessary to seek knowledge with consistency and complete dedication. This dedication requires a focus on divine realities and a deep form of worship, a worship in which there is no barrier between the seeker and the seeker. Such worship in which the servant forgets everyone, even himself, otherwise there is no use in mechanical worship. Maulana Ali says that the example of a person who prays without ijtihad is like a person who throws an arrow without a bow. In the same way, knowledge is dependent on action, and if it does not find a balanced action, it is lost. The heart cannot digest the knowledge that it has acquired without seriousness, due to which it does not have insight and it cannot see Allah.

The Master of the Universe says, "Acquire knowledge, and life will acquire you." In the beginning, a person is unaware of the realities of life. He acquires knowledge that awakens consciousness in him. But when he does this with sincerity for a period of time (i.e., he keeps turning his knowledge into action), then there comes a time when he does not integrate knowledge into himself, but real life absorbs it. The process that he was initially doing with utmost effort and ijtihad, now becomes a routine of his life, which he unconsciously starts to do with the same dedication. It is as if habit turns into instinct.

Let us return to the saying of the Master of the Universe that knowledge is embedded in the realities of insight. ⟪ar:’عالم‘⟫ He is not immersed in insights, but ⟪ar:’علم‘⟫ he receives these divine insights, and the world itself becomes a means for him, because he himself has integrated himself into this knowledge.<!-- section 5 (id=3580, raw_sort=5):  یقین کی روح -->Then you say, "⟪ar-quote:وبشِّرُ روح الیقین⟫(They rejoice because they are attached to the Spirit of Faith)." Human beings mean 'close relationship' or 'physical relationship' with something, and hence the word ⟪ar:’مباشرت‘⟫ derivation. It also has another meaning of 'extreme happiness'.  When a person touches the spirit of faith, the joy he receives cannot be expressed in words. That happiness is greater than any other blessing of Paradise for which Allaah says (interpretation of the meaning):

> ⟪quran 9:72⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَعَدَ ٱللَّهُ ٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ وَٱلْمُؤْمِنَتِ جَنَّتٍۢ تَجْرِى مِن تَحْتِهَا ٱلْأَنْهَرُ خَلِدِينَ فِيهَا وَمَسَكِنَ طَيِّبَةًۭ فِى جَنَّتِ عَدْنٍۢ ۚ وَرِضْوَنٌۭ مِّنَ ٱللَّهِ أَكْبَرُ ۚ ذَلِكَ هُوَ ٱلْفَوْزُ ٱلْعَظِيمُ ‎⟫
> *Allah has promised to the believers -men and women, - Gardens under which rivers flow to dwell therein forever, and beautiful mansions in Gardens of 'Adn (Eden Paradise). But the greatest bliss is the Good Pleasure of Allah. That is the supreme success.*
> Allah has promised the believers, men and women, Gardens beneath which rivers flow, wherein they will abide for ever, and noble dwellings and Gardens of Eden. And the greatest of all, the pleasure of Allah; that is the great attainment.
> — **Quran 9:72 (inline widget)**

Maulana Ali says that it is a blessing for a scholar to acquire knowledge and contemplate it. Allah Himself is 'One' and He has created every being 'One'. Every human being is unique in that he has an identity in which no one else shares him. He is alone in this circle and his caste is not divisive. Therefore, the true knowledge of man is the knowledge of his own self, which he cannot fully grasp. That is why the Messenger of Allah (swt) said: ⟪ar-quote:من عرف نفسہ فقد عرف ربہ⟫ "Whoever knows his own soul, he has done it by his Lord." In the early stages, when a person acquires knowledge, his happiness is like that of a person who has returned from the exile of ignorance to the peace of his home. The wisest is the one who is the most alive, and the most alive is the one who is closest to Allah, and life itself is a joy! This happiness is different from the pleasures that a person gets in different ways. Maulana Ali says that ⟪ar:’فقیہ‘⟫ he is the one who does not disappoint people with the mercy of Allah. He is always lost in the light of Allah's mercy, due to which he never feels disappointed. He is confident that whatever Allah deals with him, Allah's mercy will be included in it. Allaah says (interpretation of the meaning):

> ⟪quran 15:56⟫
> ⟪ar:‏قَالَ وَمَن يَقْنَطُ مِن رَّحْمَةِ رَبِّهِۦٓ إِلَّا ٱلضَّآلُّونَ ‎⟫
> *[Ibrahim (Abraham)] said: "And who despairs of the Mercy of his Lord except those who are astray?" *
> said, Only those who despair of the mercy of their Lord are those who have gone astray.
> — **Quran 15:56 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 6:54⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَإِذَا جَآءَكَ ٱلَّذِينَ يُؤْمِنُونَ بِـَٔايَتِنَا فَقُلْ سَلَمٌ عَلَيْكُمْ ۖ كَتَبَ رَبُّكُمْ عَلَىٰ نَفْسِهِ ٱلرَّحْمَةَ ۖ أَنَّهُۥ مَنْ عَمِلَ مِنكُمْ سُوٓءًۢا بِجَهَلَةٍۢ ثُمَّ تَابَ مِنۢ بَعْدِهِۦ وَأَصْلَحَ فَأَنَّهُۥ غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *When those who believe in Our Ayat (proofs, evidences, verses, lessons, signs, revelations, etc.) come to you, say: "Salamun 'Alaikum" (peace be on you); your Lord has written Mercy for Himself, so that, if any of you does evil in ignorance, and thereafter repents and does righteous good deeds (by obeying Allah), then surely, He is Oft&shy;Forgiving, Most Merciful.*
> And those who believe in Our verses, when they come to you, say, Peace be upon you. Your Lord has made mercy incumbent upon Himself. So whoever among you does evil in ignorance, then repents thereafter and does good, then indeed He is Oft-Forgiving, Most Merciful.
> — **Quran 6:54 (inline widget)**

The joy of Allah's mercy is in fact the definition of 'beauty'. This beauty is different from aesthetics. This is the true beauty, the imagination that arises from his intellect. The meaning of the word ⟪ar:’أحسان‘⟫ in Arabic is often taken for virtue or excellence. But it also has a meaning ⟪ar:حُسن⟫(beauty), that is, such concepts make the soul beautiful. Maulana Ali has said that the excellence of the intellect lies in being able⟪ar:ینظر جمال الظاہر والباطن⟫ to see the beauty of things both outward and inward. The beauty of outward forms and actions is complemented by their inner beauty. In the same way, the beauty of deeds comes from the beauty or virtue of the soul. That is why the Prophet (peace and blessings of Allaah be upon him) said, "Allah is beautiful and loves beautiful things."

By instilling beautiful morals in oneself, a person is able to love Allah because Allah loves beautiful things. And because of these beautiful manners, he ⟪ar:محمد مصطفی صلی اللہ علیہ و آلہ و سلم⟫became the most beloved servant of Allah, and he invited his Ummah to adopt the same noble manners and said:

> ⟪quran 3:31⟫
> ⟪ar:‏قُلْ إِن كُنتُمْ تُحِبُّونَ ٱللَّهَ فَٱتَّبِعُونِى يُحْبِبْكُمُ ٱللَّهُ وَيَغْفِرْ لَكُمْ ذُنُوبَكُمْ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *Say (O Muhammad PBUH to mankind): "If you (really) love Allah then follow me (i.e. accept Islamic Monotheism, follow the Quran and the Sunnah), Allah will love you and forgive you of your sins. And Allah is Oft-Forgiving, Most Merciful." *
Say, > if you love God, then follow me, and God will love you and forgive you your sins. God is Forgiving and Merciful.
> — **Quran 3:31 (inline widget)**

In explaining this, the Creator of the Universe said: ⟪ar-quote:اول العقل التَوَدُّد⟫ "(The basis of intellect is in love)." That is, to inculcate the principles of love within one's self and then to express this love through one's actions outwardly, so that it becomes the glow of the outward and the attraction of the inward. Following the Messenger of Allah is in fact the name of inculcating the morals of the Messenger of Allah (s.a.w.a.) in oneself because only you have attained the perfection of these morals. It is also understood that the connection of the intellect with the Truth is established by virtue of the best morals (such as gentleness, contentment, gratitude, generosity, shame, wisdom, tolerance, etc.) which are not only beautiful in themselves, but also create love in both the outward and the inward. A true intellect is the embodiment of all these morals, because without them his intellect cannot be complete. Through these morals, man can create depth and depth in his long spontaneous actions and bring out the hidden treasures of the intellect. Moulding all these morals into the mould of one's own soul and uniting them is, in a sense, an act of 'monotheism'. Although truth affects the soul, it is also necessary that morality becomes the 'leaven' for his intellect so that it spreads in the form of action and reaches its perfection through the faculties ⟪ar:بالفعل⟫of ⟪ar:بالقوۃ⟫his intellect. In this sense, all immorality is not only evil but also a cause of intellectual weakness. The heart becomes sick because of them and the eye becomes blind which can no longer see the reality. As the Qur'an says:

> ⟪quran 2:10⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فِى قُلُوبِهِم مَّرَضٌۭ فَزَادَهُمُ ٱللَّهُ مَرَضًۭا ۖ وَلَهُمْ عَذَابٌ أَلِيمٌۢ بِمَا كَانُوا۟ يَكْذِبُونَ ‎⟫
> *In their hearts is a disease (of doubt and hypocrisy) and Allah has increased their disease. A painful torment is theirs because they used to tell lies.*
> is a sickness in their hearts, so Allah has increased their sickness, and there awaits them a painful punishment, for they used to lie.
> — **Quran 2:10 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 22:46⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَفَلَمْ يَسِيرُوا۟ فِى ٱلْأَرْضِ فَتَكُونَ لَهُمْ قُلُوبٌۭ يَعْقِلُونَ بِهَآ أَوْ آذَانٌۭ يَسْمَعُونَ بِهَا ۖ فَإِنَّهَا لَا تَعْمَى ٱلْأَبْصَرُ وَلَكِن تَعْمَى ٱلْقُلُوبُ ٱلَّتِى فِى ٱلصُّدُورِ ‎⟫
> *Have they not travelled through the land, and have they hearts wherewith to understand and ears wherewith to hear? Verily, it is not the eyes that grow blind, but it is the hearts which are in the breasts that grow blind.*
> have they not travelled in the land, so that they have hearts wherewith to understand, or ears wherewith to hear? Verily it is not the eyes that are blinded, but it is the hearts in the breasts that are blinded.
> — **Quran 22:46 (inline widget)**

Maulana Ali says that the one who overcomes his desires has prospered. Through this well-being, one can feel the happiness that comes from certainty. And the spirit of this belief comes from the combination of intentionality and sincerity, along with the observance of the Shariah. If there is no sincerity in the actions of the Shari'ah, then it is hypocrisy and hypocrisy, which is shirk. He says, "Know that even the slightest hypocrisy is shirk." Allaah explains this in this soorah:

> ⟪quran 107:1-7⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَرَءَيْتَ ٱلَّذِى يُكَذِّبُ بِٱلدِّينِ ‎ ‏فَذَلِكَ ٱلَّذِى يَدُعُّ ٱلْيَتِيمَ ‎ ‏وَلَا يَحُضُّ عَلَىٰ طَعَامِ ٱلْمِسْكِينِ ‎ ‏فَوَيْلٌۭ لِّلْمُصَلِّينَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ عَن صَلَاتِهِمْ سَاهُونَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ يُرَآءُونَ ‎ ‏وَيَمْنَعُونَ ٱلْمَاعُونَ ‎⟫
> *Have you seen him who denies the Recompense? That is he who repulses the orphan (harshly), And urges not the feeding of AlMiskîn (the poor), So woe unto those performers of Salat (prayers) (hypocrites), Who delay their Salat (prayer) from their stated fixed times, Those who do good deeds only to be seen (of men), And refuse Al-Ma'un (small kindnesses e.g. salt, sugar, water,  etc.). *
> Hast thou seen him who denies the Day of Judgment, and is he who pusheth away the orphan and does not urge the feeding of the needy? Woe to the worshippers who are heedless of their prayers and restrict them from their prayers.
> — **Quran 107:1-7 (inline widget)**

This Surah shows that outward acts of worship have no value as long as they are combined with sincerity and a moral life. Without this depth, religion is meaningless. An action that has a pure intention behind it is called a true action, otherwise every outward action is dust and they do not rise up in the sight of Allah.

> ⟪quran 22:37⟫
> ⟪ar:‏لَن يَنَالَ ٱللَّهَ لُحُومُهَا وَلَا دِمَآؤُهَا وَلَكِن يَنَالُهُ ٱلتَّقْوَىٰ مِنكُمْ ۚ كَذَلِكَ سَخَّرَهَا لَكُمْ لِتُكَبِّرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ عَلَىٰ مَا هَدَىٰكُمْ ۗ وَبَشِّرِ ٱلْمُحْسِنِينَ ‎⟫
> *It is neither their meat nor their blood that reaches Allah, but it is piety from you that reaches Him. Thus have We made them subject to you that you may magnify Allah for His Guidance to you. And give glad tidings (O Muhammad PBUH) to the Muhsinun (doers of good).*
> It is not their flesh nor their blood that reaches Allah, but piety from you reaches Him. Thus have He subjected them to you, that you may magnify Allah for that He has guided you, and give good tidings to the doers of good.
> — **Quran 22:37 (inline widget)**

Maulana Ali says that he who does not have intellect has no religion. And that the sleep of certainty is better than the awakening of doubt. Such people remain awake (from spiritual realities) even while they sleep. For this reason, the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings of Allaah be upon him) said: "My eyes sleep, but my heart remains awake." The wise man understands that although the outward acts of worship are necessary in their own right, the blessings of Allah cannot be obtained through them alone. It also requires an awareness of what he is doing. And why is it doing?  This consciousness of his, combined with his morals and inner beauty, attracts the acceptance of Allah. Maulana Ali says, "The best knowledge for you is that which makes your deeds acceptable to Allah."

*Verses referenced in this topic (curated linkage from KAHSKOLE. TopicAyats — 5 of 5 not already cited above):*

> ⟪quran 2:25⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَبَشِّرِ ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ أَنَّ لَهُمْ جَنَّتٍۢ تَجْرِى مِن تَحْتِهَا ٱلْأَنْهَرُ ۖ كُلَّمَا رُزِقُوا۟ مِنْهَا مِن ثَمَرَةٍۢ رِّزْقًۭا ۙ قَالُوا۟ هَذَا ٱلَّذِى رُزِقْنَا مِن قَبْلُ ۖ وَأُتُوا۟ بِهِۦ مُتَشَبِهًۭا ۖ وَلَهُمْ فِيهَآ أَزْوَجٌۭ مُّطَهَّرَةٌۭ ۖ وَهُمْ فِيهَا خَلِدُونَ ‎⟫
> *And give glad tidings to those who believe and do righteous good deeds, that for them will be Gardens under which rivers flow (Paradise). Every time they will be provided with a fruit therefrom, they will say: "This is what we were provided with before," and they will be given things in resemblance (i.e. in the same form but different in taste) and they shall have therein Azwajun Mutahharatun (purified mates or wives), (having no menses, stools, urine, etc.) and they will abide therein forever.*
> And give glad tidings to those who believe and do righteous deeds, that for them are Gardens beneath which rivers flow; whenever they are provided with a fruit from it, they will say, This is what we were provided with before. And they will be given fruits like the same, and they will have therein purified spouses, and they will abide in it forever.
> — **Quran 2:25 (TopicAyats)**

> ⟪quran 38:46⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّآ أَخْلَصْنَهُم بِخَالِصَةٍۢ ذِكْرَى ٱلدَّارِ ‎⟫
> *Verily, We did choose them by granting them (a good thing, i.e.) the remembrance of the home [in the Hereafter and they used to make the people remember it, and also they used to invite the people to obey Allah and to do good deeds for the Hereafter].*
> assuredly We preferred unto them a distinct distinction, the remembrance of the Hereafter.
> — **Quran 38:46 (TopicAyats)**

> ⟪quran 55:60⟫
> ⟪ar:‏هَلْ جَزَآءُ ٱلْإِحْسَنِ إِلَّا ٱلْإِحْسَنُ ‎⟫
> *Is there any reward for good other than good?*
> recompense for goodness other than goodness?
> — **Quran 55:60 (TopicAyats)**

> ⟪quran 87:17⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلْآخِرَةُ خَيْرٌۭ وَأَبْقَىٰٓ ‎⟫
> *Although the Hereafter is better and more lasting.*
> whereas the Hereafter is better and more enduring.
> — **Quran 87:17 (TopicAyats)**

> ⟪quran 89:27⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيَّتُهَا ٱلنَّفْسُ ٱلْمُطْمَئِنَّةُ ‎⟫
> *(It will be said to the pious): "O (you) the one in (complete) rest and satisfaction!*
> O soul of contentment,
> — **Quran 89:27 (TopicAyats)**<!-- section 6 (id=3600, raw_sort=6): دنیا میں رہتے ہوئے آخرت کی زندگی -->Then he says that they are related to this world with their bodies, but their soul is connected to the Hereafter. This sentence can be explained by another statement of Amir al-Mu'minin in which he says that he belongs to a group whose spiritual status is such that their hearts are in Paradise but their bodies are engaged in this world.  Your statement that the hearts are 'settled' in heaven indicates that although they are living in this world, they have reached heaven spiritually, conceptually and really. This statement of yours also confirms the statement of the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings of Allaah be upon him) that Allah keeps His servants in the state they desire. Those who live in the upper world depend on the basis of this Hereafter. On the contrary, this world is the source of all their thinking and thinking for those who live in this world. Their thoughts, thoughts, imaginations, thoughts, all are imprisoned in the depths of this world. Every action of theirs bears the seal of this inferior world, but every action of the wise is based on the reward they will receive in the Hereafter. And this is because they understand the fact that every action is dust, except that which is sincere and which Allah accepts the Almighty.

Maulana Ali often mentions the blessings of Paradise and the torments of Hell in his sermons. So does this mean that you have given a commercial colour to the commands of Allah? It's not like that at all! It's one thing to know about heaven and hell and another thing to make sense of it. Your aim is to inculcate in the Ummah the feeling through which morals can be illuminated. Otherwise, from a commercial point of view, the object is of no use after the purpose of any trade has been achieved. So, will the attributes of piety, good manners, forbidden manners, etc., become useless after the attainment of Paradise? Not at all! Rather, the atmosphere of Paradise will be these attributes. The purpose of your mention of Paradise is that a person should prepare himself for the environment of this Paradise while living in this world so that he can enter it. In one of his sermons, he mentions Paradise and says:

If you turn your heart to the descriptions of Paradise, your soul will be disgusted with the wonders, desires, pleasures and charming scenery of this world. And she will be lost in the scene of Paradise, with swaying streams on the banks of the canal, with its roots in the dunes of fragrant musk, and from whose branches hang glittering pearls

The high standard of certainty ⟪ar:’روحانیت‘⟫ is higher than the desire for heaven and the fear of hell. But when this level of spirituality is attained, the soul becomes 'heavenly' even while living in this world. And the state of Paradise is such that the soul is satisfied only with the great presence of its Lord and has no desire for anything else. He calls this state by the name of the Qur'an ⟪ar:’نفس المطمئنۃ‘⟫ :

> ⟪quran 89:27⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيَّتُهَا ٱلنَّفْسُ ٱلْمُطْمَئِنَّةُ ‎⟫
> *(It will be said to the pious): "O (you) the one in (complete) rest and satisfaction!*
> O soul of contentment,
> — **Quran 89:27 (inline widget)**

The satisfaction of this soul is due to his complete faith. This verse of the Qur'an echoes in Maulana Ali's sermons:

> ⟪quran 87:17⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلْآخِرَةُ خَيْرٌۭ وَأَبْقَىٰٓ ‎⟫
> *Although the Hereafter is better and more lasting.*
> whereas the Hereafter is better and more enduring.
> — **Quran 87:17 (inline widget)**

The Hereafter is not only the name of a 'time' when the divine revelations and glad tidings will be fulfilled, but it is also the name of a 'house' where all the highest, earthly and divine attributes will appear, the slightest reflection of which can be seen in this world. In this capacity, the mere mention and concept of Paradise leads to the purification of the intellect and the turning away from the desires and pleasures of this world, as Allah says:

> ⟪quran 38:46⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّآ أَخْلَصْنَهُم بِخَالِصَةٍۢ ذِكْرَى ٱلدَّارِ ‎⟫
> *Verily, We did choose them by granting them (a good thing, i.e.) the remembrance of the home [in the Hereafter and they used to make the people remember it, and also they used to invite the people to obey Allah and to do good deeds for the Hereafter].*
> assuredly We preferred unto them a distinct distinction, the remembrance of the Hereafter.
> — **Quran 38:46 (inline widget)**

In other words, the pure knowledge of the Hereafter creates the concept of becoming a Paradise in this world, which allows a person to do the good deeds and morals that are originally in the Hereafter and he attains happiness in this world as well as in the Hereafter. So it has been proved that these moral qualities can only be created by a person from whose eyes the veil of this world has been removed and he can see and feel the life of the Hereafter while living in this mortal world. That is, goodness and goodness are not done so that they will be rewarded in the Hereafter, rather that goodness itself is a part of that reward. Allaah says (interpretation of the meaning):

> ⟪quran 55:60⟫
> ⟪ar:‏هَلْ جَزَآءُ ٱلْإِحْسَنِ إِلَّا ٱلْإِحْسَنُ ‎⟫
> *Is there any reward for good other than good?*
> recompense for goodness other than goodness?
> — **Quran 55:60 (inline widget)**

Maulana Ali says that the fruit of any good deed is like its root, which means that the end of any action lies in its beginning (intention). At this point, this verse of the Qur'an is very topical:

> ⟪quran 2:25⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَبَشِّرِ ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ أَنَّ لَهُمْ جَنَّتٍۢ تَجْرِى مِن تَحْتِهَا ٱلْأَنْهَرُ ۖ كُلَّمَا رُزِقُوا۟ مِنْهَا مِن ثَمَرَةٍۢ رِّزْقًۭا ۙ قَالُوا۟ هَذَا ٱلَّذِى رُزِقْنَا مِن قَبْلُ ۖ وَأُتُوا۟ بِهِۦ مُتَشَبِهًۭا ۖ وَلَهُمْ فِيهَآ أَزْوَجٌۭ مُّطَهَّرَةٌۭ ۖ وَهُمْ فِيهَا خَلِدُونَ ‎⟫
> *And give glad tidings to those who believe and do righteous good deeds, that for them will be Gardens under which rivers flow (Paradise). Every time they will be provided with a fruit therefrom, they will say: "This is what we were provided with before," and they will be given things in resemblance (i.e. in the same form but different in taste) and they shall have therein Azwajun Mutahharatun (purified mates or wives), (having no menses, stools, urine, etc.) and they will abide therein forever.*
> And give glad tidings to those who believe and do righteous deeds, that for them are Gardens beneath which rivers flow; whenever they are provided with a fruit from it, they will say, This is what we were provided with before. And they will be given fruits like the same, and they will have therein purified spouses, and they will abide in it forever.
> — **Quran 2:25 (inline widget)**

The fruits of the Hereafter are felt in this world in the form of all kinds of goodness, beauty, truth, and all the joys that arise from them. All these tastes are of the real food of the Hereafter, which is to be obtained in Paradise. In the realm of morality, good deeds, but also the sense of the need for good deeds (benevolence) are necessary not only for salvation but also for salvation in this world, and in this world. They liberate them from the bondage of sins outwardly, and from the bondage of ego on the inside. This feeling has been the focus and purpose of all your teachings.<!-- section 7 (id=3581, raw_sort=7): وہ چیز جو آسان بھی ہے اور مشکل بھی -->He said, "Those things are easy for them and difficult for those who are extravagant." They love him from whom the ignorant feel alienated. This quote of yours describes the effect that is always on the heart of the saints of Allah. They always remember their death and their encounter with Allah, and with His help they renounce the world. What is alien to the ignorant are the apparent difficulties, sufferings and deprivations of this world. The Qur'an says about them:

> ⟪quran 2:155-157⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَنَبْلُوَنَّكُم بِشَىْءٍۢ مِّنَ ٱلْخَوْفِ وَٱلْجُوعِ وَنَقْصٍۢ مِّنَ ٱلْأَمْوَلِ وَٱلْأَنفُسِ وَٱلثَّمَرَتِ ۗ وَبَشِّرِ ٱلصَّبِرِينَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ إِذَآ أَصَبَتْهُم مُّصِيبَةٌۭ قَالُوٓا۟ إِنَّا لِلَّهِ وَإِنَّآ إِلَيْهِ رَجِعُونَ ‎ ‏أُو۟لَٓئِكَ عَلَيْهِمْ صَلَوَتٌۭ مِّن رَّبِّهِمْ وَرَحْمَةٌۭ ۖ وَأُو۟لَٓئِكَ هُمُ ٱلْمُهْتَدُونَ ‎⟫
> *And certainly, We shall test you with something of fear, hunger, loss of wealth, lives and fruits, but give glad tidings to As-Sabirin (the patient ones, etc.). Who, when afflicted with calamity, say: "Truly! To Allah we belong and truly, to Him we shall return." They are those on whom are the Salawat (i.e. blessings, etc.) (i.e. who are blessed and will be forgiven) from their Lord, and (they are those who) receive His Mercy, and it is they who are the guided-ones.*
> And We will surely test you with something of fear and hunger and loss of wealth and lives and fruits; and give glad tidings to those who patiently bear them, who, when afflicted with calamity, say: We belong to Allah, and to Him we shall return; these are the ones upon whom there is mercy from their Lord, and mercy, and they are the guided. are
> — **Quran 2:155-157 (inline widget)**

⟪ar:مھتدون⟫These guided people are patient in the face of adversity, and they see and feel the blessings that come from this patience from the reality of their knowledge:

> ⟪quran 103:1-3⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلْعَصْرِ ‎ ‏إِنَّ ٱلْإِنسَنَ لَفِى خُسْرٍ ‎ ‏إِلَّا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ وَتَوَاصَوْا۟ بِٱلْحَقِّ وَتَوَاصَوْا۟ بِٱلصَّبْرِ ‎⟫
> *By Al-'Asr (the time). Verily! Man is in loss, Except those who believe (in Islamic Monotheism) and do righteous good deeds, and recommend one another to the truth (i.e. order one another to perform all kinds of good deeds (Al-Ma'which Allah has ordained, and abstain from all kinds of sins and evil deeds (Al-Munkar which Allah has forbidden), and recommend one another to patience (for the sufferings,  harms, and injuries which one may encounter in Allah's Cause during preaching His religion of Islamic Monotheism or Jihad, etc.). *
By > time, man is in loss, except those who believe, and do righteous deeds, and enjoin one another to the truth and to be patient.
> — **Quran 103:1-3 (inline widget)**

These are the believers who are steadfast in the face of trials, who know their origin and their future, and who believe in Allah's saying, "To Him we shall return." Because of this, the difficulties of the world become easier for them. The extravagant, on the contrary, only feels the bitterness and pain of these sufferings. The ease of these sufferings is concealed by his ignorance, but is obvious to the wise:

> ⟪quran 94:5-6⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَإِنَّ مَعَ ٱلْعُسْرِ يُسْرًا ‎ ‏إِنَّ مَعَ ٱلْعُسْرِ يُسْرًۭا ‎⟫
> *So verily, with the hardship, there is relief, Verily, with the hardship, there is relief (i.e. there is one hardship with two reliefs, so one hardship cannot overcome two reliefs).*
> Surely, with every hardship is ease, and with every hardship is ease.
> — **Quran 94:5-6 (inline widget)**

These wise men not only see the fruit of the ease that comes after hardship with their insight, but also taste it. They take suffering and trials as their friends, while the ignorant become alienated from them. For this reason, he said, "Death is as dear to me as a mother's breast is to a newborn child." And you're talking about that love of death while you're alive yourself. It is as if you are seeing the reality of death, and the blessings that come after it, with your own eyes. He also said, "I am the death of death!" Because life in this life itself is a kind of death, a hindrance and a compulsion. Allaah says (interpretation of the meaning):

> ⟪quran 29:64⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَمَا هَذِهِ ٱلْحَيَوٰةُ ٱلدُّنْيَآ إِلَّا لَهْوٌۭ وَلَعِبٌۭ ۚ وَإِنَّ ٱلدَّارَ ٱلْآخِرَةَ لَهِىَ ٱلْحَيَوَانُ ۚ لَوْ كَانُوا۟ يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫
> *And this life of the world is only amusement and play! Verily, the home of the Hereafter, that is the life indeed (i.e. the eternal life that will never end), if they but knew*
> And the life of this world is naught but a sport and a pastime; and the life of the Hereafter, if they but knew.
> — **Quran 29:64 (inline widget)**

### Asceticism:

It is important to note here that the purpose of these statements is not to renounce this physical world, but to renounce the 'world-being' of this world. That is, we have to overcome the relationship of those ⟪ar:’أنا‘⟫ connected to the world. You refer to ⟪ar:نہج البلاغۃ⟫this state as the ⟪ar:’زہد‘⟫ following:

This world is a place for which destruction has been ordered, and destruction has been decreed for its people. This world is sweet and attractive. He who goes out in search of him comes running to him; he who looks at him settles in his heart. Therefore, gather the best of Tosha from here and leave it, and do not ask for anything other than what is most important

This is the best Tosha! In another place he said that this is the best Tosha ⟪ar:’زہد‘⟫ ⟪ar:’تقوی‘⟫ . For the next life, this tosha is obtained as much as a person is indifferent to the mortal things of this world.

> ⟪quran 17:18⟫
> ⟪ar:‏مَّن كَانَ يُرِيدُ ٱلْعَاجِلَةَ عَجَّلْنَا لَهُۥ فِيهَا مَا نَشَآءُ لِمَن نُّرِيدُ ثُمَّ جَعَلْنَا لَهُۥ جَهَنَّمَ يَصْلَىٰهَا مَذْمُومًۭا مَّدْحُورًۭا ‎⟫
> *Whoever wishes for the quick-passing (transitory enjoyment of this world), We readily grant him what We will for whom We like. Then, afterwards, We have appointed for him Hell, he will burn therein disgraced and rejected, ( far away from Allah's Mercy).*
> whosoever desires this fleeting life, We hasten to give him therein whatsoever We will; then We have prepared for him Gehenna wherein he shall dwell, disgraced and disgraced.
> — **Quran 17:18 (inline widget)**

These sayings of Maulana Ali fully describe the contempt of this world:

I swear by Allah! In my eyes, this world of yours is as despicable as a pig's bone chewed in the hand of a whip
The example of the world is that of a snake that is gentle to the touch, but full of deadly venom
For me, this world is the same as the substance that flows from the goat's nose.

The greatness and greatness of Allah makes this world despicable and humiliating. When this world is viewed in the light of the Absolute Real, all the pleasures of this world appear temporary and trivial. The contempt of His servants in the face of Allah's greatness becomes clear. Maulana Ali praised a believer and said, " ⟪ar-quote:کان یعظمہ فی عینی، صغار الدنیا فی عینہ⟫ (In his eyes, the contempt of the world made him great in my eyes)." This world was not inferior to the Creator of the Universe because it was of no use, but because of the greatness of Allah, the Hereafter and the absolute realities that existed in their eyes, and because of it, this world became inferior to them. Because:

> ⟪quran 28:88⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَدْعُ مَعَ ٱللَّهِ إِلَهًا آخَرَ ۘ لَآ إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ ۚ كُلُّ شَىْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُۥ ۚ لَهُ ٱلْحُكْمُ وَإِلَيْهِ تُرْجَعُونَ ‎⟫
> *And invoke not any other ilah (god) along with Allah, La ilaha illa Huwa (none has the right to be worshipped but He). Everything will perish save His Face. His is the Decision, and to Him you (all) shall be returned.*
> And do not invoke any other god along with Allah; there is no God except Him; all things will perish except His Face; His is the command, and it is to Him that you will be returned.
> — **Quran 28:88 (inline widget)**

The value of this world lies in the fact that there are creatures of Allah in it who praise Allah morning and evening and acknowledge His greatness:

> ⟪quran 17:44⟫
> ⟪ar:‏تُسَبِّحُ لَهُ ٱلسَّمَوَتُ ٱلسَّبْعُ وَٱلْأَرْضُ وَمَن فِيهِنَّ ۚ وَإِن مِّن شَىْءٍ إِلَّا يُسَبِّحُ بِحَمْدِهِۦ وَلَكِن لَّا تَفْقَهُونَ تَسْبِيحَهُمْ ۗ إِنَّهُۥ كَانَ حَلِيمًا غَفُورًۭا ‎⟫
> *The seven heavens and the earth and all that is therein, glorify Him and there is not a thing but glorifies His Praise. But you understand not their glorification. Truly, He is Ever Forbearing, Oft-Forgiving.*
> seven heavens and the earth glorify Him and all that is between them. There is not a thing that does not glorify Him with His praise, but you do not understand their glorification. Indeed, He is all-forbearing, all-forgiving.
> — **Quran 17:44 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 24:41⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَلَمْ تَرَ أَنَّ ٱللَّهَ يُسَبِّحُ لَهُۥ مَن فِى ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ وَٱلطَّيْرُ صَٓفَّتٍۢ ۖ كُلٌّۭ قَدْ عَلِمَ صَلَاتَهُۥ وَتَسْبِيحَهُۥ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ عَلِيمٌۢ بِمَا يَفْعَلُونَ ‎⟫
> *See you not (O Muhammad PBUH) that Allah, He it is Whom glorify whosoever is in the heavens and the earth, and the birds with wings out-spread (in their flight). Of each one He (Allah) knows indeed his Salat (prayer) and his glorification, [or everyone knows his Salat (prayer) and his glorification], and Allah is All-Aware of what they do.*
> do you not see that all those who are in the heavens and the earth, and the birds with outspread wings, glorify Allah? Each one knows its prayer and its glorification, and Allah knows what they do.
> — **Quran 24:41 (inline widget)**

Here again, a contradiction arose in the matter of this world, that it is in a sense a 'bad place' and in a way a 'good place' in which one can prepare all the deeds for the Hereafter. In your sermons, you praise Allah for the creation and industry of nature, peacocks, birds, even ants, dragons and elephants. In another sermon, he uses the blessings of this world to explain the blessings of the Hereafter and says that when the eye sees the scenes of Paradise, then even the worst blessings, the most beautiful scenes, the most delicious pleasures of this world become despised in the eyes of man. And because of this, all the difficulties of this world become easy for man, but also a source of joy. ⟪ar:زاہدین،⟫ With these spiritual resources obtained through faith, we endure all difficulties. They have the knowledge which gives them such a firm and perfect conviction that they say: ⟪ar-quote:لو کشف الغطاء ما الزدت یقینا⟫ "Even if the veil is removed, it will not be possible to increase my faith."

Describing his sincerity, he says, "I bear witness that there is no god but Allah! The sincerity of this testimony of mine has been tested, and the essence of which is mixed⟪ar:مُعتقدٌ مصاصُہُ⟫ with conviction.  In Arabic, the word ⟪ar:’مصاص‘⟫ means to suck, and the subtle part of any object is the one that contains its essence. Just as the origin of any fruit is its juice, which man sucks. The sincerity of which has been ⟪ar:لا الہ الا اللہ⟫tested is the spiritual substance of the soul, not of the imagination arising from its words or its apparent meaning. The words of the Word are merely an echo of the spiritual substance that is established in the concepts.

You return to the saying that the things are easy for them which are difficult for those who are extravagant. They love him from whom the ignorant feel alienated. In one sense, it is 'suffering' and in another sense it is 'death' itself. For the ignorant, death is a terrible disintegration in which he is separated from his body. For him, it is the end of life rather than the beginning of life. It is for him to be separated from the thing that has been his focus and center all his life. On the other hand, for the wise, death is the name of salvation from suffering and meeting Allah; it is the name of the completion of monotheism for him that he merges into his transcendent realm and becomes 'one' with Him. Only a person can taste the pleasure of this ocean who immerses himself in this sea. The heat of this whole burns all the components to ashes. Those who remain slaves of their ego are entangled in the outer and inner aspects of the parts. But the wise man is always focused on the remembrance of the absolute tomorrow, the joy that comes from it displaces his ego and shatters all his illusions.<!-- section 8 (id=3583, raw_sort=8): عدل کا فلسفہ  -->
⟪ar:أمیر المومنین⟫The best example of K.K⟪ar:’عدل‘⟫.'s philosophy is found in the letter he wrote to the commander and commander of ⟪ar:’مالک اشتر بن الحارث النخئی‘⟫ his army when he appointed him governor of Egypt.  In your view, the inclination of moral laws towards justice is not only related to the external world, but also to the spiritual world. The principles of justice that you have outlined are beyond the constraints of this process.  In your statements, thought and action appear to be complementary and close to each other, reflecting ⟪ar:’توحید‘⟫ the message of (which means to be one). The life of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and Ali (a.s.) is a living example of these principles.

One is that ⟪ar:امیر المونین⟫he himself was a perfect embodiment of justice, and secondly, in the foundations of his justice we find great spiritual lessons, how a life spent in love with God automatically leads to a good life. A life that resembles oneself in ⟪ar:’الحق‘⟫ oneself! If we look at ethics ⟪ar:’أحسان‘⟫ in the broad realm of morals, we will find that the combination of the dimensions and dimensions of morals and ethics creates a dimension of depth that molds both of them into a fundamental realm. Common questions of right and wrong are moulded into a specific question, 'What is reality?'

Ali's spiritual view of monotheism is not only that there is no parallel to Allah, but also that no one stands against Him. For this reason, every good⟪ar:حَسَنَ⟫ deed that is a punishment for Allah is not the antithesis of a moral evil. ⟪ar:’الحق‘⟫ It is an individual and singular existence of its own, in contrast to which, if anything, it is only⟪ar:’عدم‘⟫. So if good ⟪ar:الحق⟫is part of the positive aspect, then evil ⟪ar:الحق⟫is the 'ability' or 'intention' to negate evil. In other words, goodness, if it is an attribute of the Creator, then evil is an attribute of the creation He has created. Allaah says (interpretation of the meaning):

> ⟪quran 113:2⟫
> ⟪ar:‏مِن شَرِّ مَا خَلَقَ ‎⟫
> *"From the evil of what He has created;*
> from the evil of His creatures.
> — **Quran 113:2 (inline widget)**

This verse is often mistranslated as the evil that Allah has created, which is both religious and literal. Allah's saying that ⟪ar:‏مِن شَرِّ مَا خَلَقَ،⟫He is clearly stating that the 'evil' that came from His 'creation' was revealed. That is, Allah created the free creatures with good qualities. He himself created 'evil' by negating these attributes. Therefore, it cannot be said that God created evil. He created only those conditions in which His creatures chose to participate, even though they could choose the truth. This proves that evil is in fact only a negation of good and does not exist in itself. This verse can also be understood in the sense that I take refuge in the 'truth' from the 'unjust'. Evil appears only in the form of a negation of the truth, which the eye of the heart sees as an 'illusion'. And just as every illusion can be shattered by reason, in the same way truth and goodness have the power to overcome any evil. The more a soul is an ombudsman before its Lord, the more it will be able to overcome evil with the firmness of its will. This maturity reaches from the intellect to the heart, which convinces it that good is more 'right' than evil, which is strengthened ⟪ar:’الحق‘⟫ by its knowledge. Since evil does not exist, and it is an object that has deviated from its position, there is a need to overcome it and return it to the truth. For this reason, in the eyes of Amir al-Mu'minin, fulfilling one's obligations and fulfilling one's rights for all (Allah, oneself and all creation) is the definition of justice. Referring to this, he says, "Justice is the act of keeping things in their proper place." The more a person's actions are in his place, the more just he will be, and this essence of justice will be present in a person as much as it relates to him⟪ar:’الحق‘⟫. First of all, a person has to be 'good', only then will he be able to do 'good', and to ⟪ar:الحق⟫be good is to become 'one'⟪ar:توحید⟫, because he is only ⟪ar:الحق⟫one!

⟪ar:مالک اشتر⟫ An analysis of the letter you wrote to you shows that justice is not the name of any one of all attributes, but the name of the sum of all attributes, especially the three attributes of temperance, courage, and wisdom. When these three attributes are in their proper places, then this self can be called just.

Ethics and spirituality are intertwined, which is evidenced by the narration that once when the Messenger of Allah (s.a.w.a.) was sitting with his companions, Gabriel (a.s.) came to him in the form of a human being and said, " ⟪ar:یا محمد (ﷺ)!⟫ ⟪ar:’اسلام‘⟫ Tell me about me." He said, ⟪ar:الأسلام⟫"It is to bear witness that there is no god but Allah, and that Muhammad is His Messenger, and that prayer, zakat, fasting, and Hajj to the House of Allah are called Islam." Gabriel said, "You have spoken the truth! ⟪ar:’ایمان‘⟫ He said, "Belief in Allah, His Angels, His Book, His Messengers, and the reward and punishment of the Hereafter is faith." Gabriel then said, "You have spoken the truth! Then he asked, "Tell ⟪ar:’أحسان‘⟫ me what it is." He said, "Worship Allah as you see Him with your own eyes, otherwise at least do it as He sees you."
