The constant presence of Allah and the consciousness of being in His sight is common in all these grand places, as the Prophet (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) said: "Worship Allah as He is visible." Therefore, the concept of benevolence is rooted in Islam. On the one hand, Ali (a.s.) says in his sermons, "Know that every action you do depends on your prayer, i.e., how you look at 'goodness', and on the other hand, he says that pretense, arrogance, and self-praise are the best traps of Satan by which he ⟪ar:محسنین⟫destroys others⟪ar:احسان⟫." The main purpose of worship is to destroy one's self, self and ⟪ar:أنانیت⟫self in the sight of Allah. Your first quote calls for justice, which puts things, ⟪ar:أنائیت⟫including them, in their rightful place, and your second quote explains the cause of all injustices that ⟪ar:کبر⟫are, and ⟪ar:حرس⟫ are⟪ar:’أمہات معاصی‘⟫, ⟪ar:حسد⟫ and are called.<!-- section 9 (id=3582, raw_sort=9): مالک اشتر کے نام خط -->This is what Allah's servant "Ali", Amir al-mu'minin, has ordered Malik ibn al-Harith al-Ashtar in his instrument (of appointment) for him when he made him Governor of Egypt for the collection of its revenues, fighting against its enemies, seeking the good of its people and making its cities prosperous.

⟪ar-quote:هذَا مَا أَمَرَ بِهِ عَبْدُ اللهِ عَلِيٌ أَميِرُ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ، مَالِكَ بْنَ الْحَارِثِ الاْشْتَرَ فِي عَهْدِهِ إِلَيْهِ، حِينَ وَلاَّهُ مِصْرَ- جِبْوةَ خَرَاجِهَا، وَجِهَادَ عَدُوِّهَا، وَاسْتِصْلاَحَ أَهْلِهَا، وَعِمَارَةَ بِلاَدِهَا⟫

He has ordered him to fear Allah, to prefer obedience to Him, and to follow what He has commanded in His Book (Qur'an) out of His obligatory and elective commands, without following which one cannot achieve virtue, nor (can one) be evil save by opposing them and ignoring them, and to help Allah the Glorified, with his heart,  hand and tongue, because Allah whose name is Sublime, takes the responsibility for helping him who helps Him, and for protecting him who gives Him support. He also orders him to break his heart off from passions, and to restrain it at the time of their increase, because the heart leads towards evil unless Allah has mercy.

⟪ar-quote:أَمَرَهُ بِتَقْوَى اللهِ، وَإِيثَارِ طَاعَتِهِ، وَاتِّبَاعِ مَا أَمَرَ بِهِ فِي كِتَابِهِ- مِنْ فَرَائِضِهِ وَسُنَنِهِ، الَّتِي لاَ يَسْعَدُ أَحَدٌ إِلاَّ بِاتِّبَاعِهَا، وَلاَ يَشْقَى إِلاَّ مَعَ جُحُودِهَا وَإِضَاعَتِهَا، وَأَنْ يَنْصُرَ اللهَ سُبْحَانَهُ بَيَدِهِ وَقَلْبِهِ وَلِسَانِهِ، فَإِنَّهُ، جَلَّ اسْمُهُ، قَدْ تَكَفَّلَ بِنَصْرِ مَنْ نَصَرَهُ، وَإِعْزَازِ مَنْ أَعَزَّهُ. وَأَمَرَهُ أَنْ يَكْسِرَ نَفْسَهُ عِنْدَ الشَّهَوَاتِ، وَيَزَعَهَا عِنْدَ الْجَمَحَاتِ، فَإِنَّ النَّفْسَ أَمَّارَةٌ بِالسُّوءِ، إِلاَّ مَا رَحِمَ اللهُ⟫

The qualifications of a governor and his responsibilities

Then, know, O Malik, that I have sent you to an area where there have been governments before you, both just as well as oppressive. People will now watch your dealings as you used to watch the dealings of the rulers before you, and they (people) will criticise you as you criticised them (rulers). Surely, the virtuous are known by the reputation that Allah circulates for them through the tongues of His creatures. Therefore, the best collection with you should be the collection of good deeds. So, control your passions and check your heart from doing what is not lawful for you, because checking the heart means detaining it just half way between what it likes and dislikes.

⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ اعْلَمْ يَا مَالكُ، أَنِّي قدْ وَجَّهْتُكَ إِلَى بِلاَد قَدْ جَرَتْ عَلَيْهَا دُوَلٌ قَبْلَكَ، مِنْ عَدْل وَجَوْر، وَأَنَّ النَّاسَ يَنْظُرُونَ مِنْ أُمُورِكَ فِى مِثْلِ مَا كُنْتَ تَنْظُرُ فِيهِ مِنْ أُمُورِ الْوُلاَةِ قَبْلَكَ، وَيَقُولُونَ فِيكَ مَا كُنْتَ تَقُولُ فِيهِمْ،إِنَّمَا يُسْتَدَلُّ عَلَى الصَّالِحِينَ بِمَا يُجْرِي اللهُ لَهُمْ عَلَى أَلْسُنِ عِبَادِهِ. فَلْيَكُنْ أَحَبَّ الذَّخَائِرِ إِلَيْكَ ذَخِيرَةُ الْعَمَلِ الصَّالِحِ، فَامْلِكْ هَوَاكَ، وَشُحَّ بِنَفْسِكَ عَمَّا لاَ يَحِلُّ لَكَ، فَإِنَّ الشُّحَّ بِالنَّفْسِ الاْنْصَافُ مِنْهَا فَيَما أَحْبَبْتَ وَكَرِهْتَ⟫

Habituate your heart to mercy for the subjects and to affection and kindness for them. Do not stand over them like greedy beasts who feel it is enough to devour them, since they are of two kinds, either your brother in religion or one like you in creation. They will commit slips and encounter mistakes. They may act wrongly, wilfully or by neglect. So, extend to them your forgiveness and pardon, in the same way as you would like Allah to extend His forgiveness and pardon to you, because you are over them and your responsible Commander (Imam) is over you while Allah is over him who has appointed you. He (Allah) has sought you to manage their affairs and has tried you through them.

⟪ar-quote:وَأَشْعِرْ قَلْبَكَ الرَّحْمَةَ لِلرَّعِيَّةِ، وَالْـمَحَبَّةَ لَهُمْ، وَاللُّطْفَ بِهِمْ، وَلاَ تَكُونَنَّ عَلَيْهِمْ سَبُعاً ضَارِياً تَغْتَنِمُ أَكْلَهُمْ، فَإِنَّهُمْ صِنْفَانِ- إِمَّا أَخٌ لَكَ فِي الدِّينِ، وَإمّا نَظِيرٌ لَكَ فِي الْخَلْقِ، يَفْرُطُ مِنْهُمُ الزَّلَلُ، وَتَعْرِضُ لَهُمُ الْعِلَلُ،يُؤْتَى عَلَى أَيْدِيهِمْ فِي الَعَمْدِ وَالْخَطَاَ، فَأَعْطِهِمْ مِنْ عَفْوِكَ وَصَفْحِكَ مِثْلَ الَّذِي تُحِبُّ أَنْ يُعْطِيَكَ اللهُ مِنْ عَفْوِهِ وَصَفْحِهِ، فَإِنَّكَ فَوْقَهُمْ، وَ وَالِي الاْمْرِ عَلَيْكَ فَوْقَكَ، وَاللهُ فَوْقَ مَنْ وَلاَّكَ! وَقَدِ اسْتَكْفَاكَ أَمْرَهُمْ، وَابْتَلاَكَ بِهِمْ⟫

Do not set yourself to fight Allah because you have no power before His power and you cannot do without His pardon and mercy. Do not repent of forgiving or be merciful in punishing. Do not act hastily during anger if you can find way out of it. Do not say- "I have been given authority, I should be obeyed when I order," because it engenders confusion in the heart, weakens the religion and takes one near ruin. If the authority in which you are placed produces pride or vanity in you then look at the greatness of the realm of Allah over you and His might the like of which might you do not even possess over yourself. This will curb your haughtiness, cure you of your high temper and bring back to you your wisdom which had gone away from you.

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ تَنْصِبَنَّ نَفْسَكَ لِحَرْبِ اللهِ، فَإِنَّهْ لاَيَدَيْ لَكَ بِنِقْمَتِهِ، وَلاَ غِنَى بِكَ عَنْ عَفْوِهِ وَرَحْمَتِهِ. وَلاَ تَنْدَمَنَّ عَلَى عَفْو، وَلاَ تَبْجَحَنَّ بِعُقُوبَة، وَلاَ تُسْرِعَنَّ إِلَى بَادِرَة وَجَدْتَ مِنْهَا مَنْدُوحَةً، وَلاَ تَقُولَنَّ- إِنِّي مُؤَمَّرٌ آمُرُ فَأُطَاعُ، فَإِنَّ ذلِكَ إِدْغَالٌ فِي الْقَلْبِ، وَمَنْهَكَةٌ لِلدِّينِ، وَتَقَرُّبٌ مِنَ الْغِيَرِ. وَإِذَا أَحْدَثَ لَكَ مَا أَنْتَ فِيهِ مِنْ سُلْطَانِكَ أُبَّهَةً أَوْ مَخِيلَةً، فَانْظُرْ إِلَى عِظَمِ مُلْكِ اللهِ فَوْقَكَ، وَقُدْرَتِهِ مَنْكَ عَلَى مَا لاَ تَقْدرِ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ نَفْسِكَ، فَإِنَّ ذلِكَ يُطَامِنُ إِلَيْكَ مِنْ طِمَاحِكَ، وَيَكُفُّ عَنْكَ مِنْ غَرْبِكَ،يَفِيءُ إِلَيْكَ بِمَا عَزَبَ عَنْكَ مِنْ عَقْلِكَ⟫

Beware of comparing yourself to Allah in His greatness or likening yourself to Him in His power, for Allah humiliates every claimant of power and disgraces every one who is haughty.

⟪ar-quote:إِيَّاكَ وَمُسَامَاةَ اللهِ فِي عَظَمَتِهِ، وَالتَّشَبُّهَ بِهِ فِي جَبَرُوتِهِ، فَإِنَّ اللهَ يُذِلُّ كُلَّ جَبَّار، وَيُهِينُ كُلَّ مُخْتَال⟫

Do justice for Allah and do justice towards the people, as against yourself, your near ones and those of your subjects for whom you have a liking because if you do not do so you will be oppressive, and when a person oppresses the creatures of Allah then, instead of His creatures, Allah becomes his opponent,  and when Allah is the opponent of a person He tramples his plea; and he will remain in the position of being at war with Allah until he gives it up and repents. Nothing is more inducive of the reversal of Allah's bounty or for the hastening of His retribution than continuance in oppression, because Allah hears the prayer of the oppressed and is on the look out for the oppressors.

⟪ar-quote:أَنْصِفِ اللهَ وَأَنْصِفِ النَّاسَ مِنْ نَفْسِكَ، وَمِنْ خَاصَّةِ أَهْلِكَ، وَمَنْ لَكَ فِيهِ هَوىً مِنْ رَعِيَّتِكَ، فَإِنَّكَ إِلاَّ تَفْعَلْ تَظْلِمْ، وَمَنْ ظَلَمَ عِبَادَ اللهِ كَانَ اللهُ خَصْمَهُ دُونَ عِبَادِهِ، وَمَنْ خَاصَمَهُ اللهُ أَدْحَضَ حُجَّتَهُ، وَكَانَ لله حَرْباً حَتَّى يَنْزعَ وَيَتُوبَ. وَلَيْسَ شَيْءٌ أَدْعَى إِلَى تَغْيِيرِ نِعْمَةِ اللهِ وَتَعْجِيلِ نِقْمَتِهِ مِنْ إِقَامَة عَلَى ظُلْم، فَإِنَّ اللهَ سَميِعٌ دَعْوَةَ الْمَظْلُومِينَ، وَهُوَ لِلظَّالِمِينَ بِالْمِرْصَادِ⟫

The way most coveted by you should be that which is the most equitable for the right, the most universal by way of justice, and the most comprehensive with regard to the agreement among those under you, because the disagreement of the common people sweeps away the arguments of the chiefs while the disagreement of the chiefs can be disregarded when compared with the agreement of the common people. No one among those under you is more burdensome to the ruler in times of ease, less helpful in distress, more disliking of equitable treatment, more importunate in asking favours, less thankful when given (anything), less appreciative of reasons at the time of refusal, and weaker in endurance at the time of the discomforts of life than the chiefs. It is the common people of the community who are the pillars of the religion, the power of the Muslims and the defence against the enemies. Your leanings should therefore be towards them and your inclination with them.

⟪ar-quote:كُنْ أَحَبَّ الاْمُورِ إِلَيْكَ أَوْسَطُهَا فِي الْحَقِّ، وَأَعَمُّهَا فِي الْعَدْلِ، وَأَجْمَعُهَا لِرِضَى الرَّعِيَّةِ، فَإِنَّ سُخْطَ الْعَامَّةِ يُجْحِفُ بِرِضَى الْخَاصَّةِ، وَإِنَّ سُخْطَ الْخَاصَّةِ يُغْتَفَرُ مَعَ رِضَى الْعَامَّةِ. وَلَيْسَ أَحَدٌ مِنَ الرَّعِيَّةِ، أَثْقَلَ عَلَى الْوَالِي مَؤُونَةً فِي الرَّخَاءِ، وَأَقَلَّ مَعُونَةً لَهُ فِي الْبَلاَءِ، وَأَكْرَهَ لِلاْنْصَافِ، وَأَسْأَلَ بِالاْلْحَافِ، وَأَقَلَّ شُكْراً عِنْدَ الاْعْطَاءِ، وَأَبْطَأَ عُذْراً عِنْدَ الْمَنْعِ، وَأَضْعَفَ صَبْراً عِنْدَ مُلِمَّاتِ الدَّهْرِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْخَاصَّةِ، وَإِنَّمَا عَمُودُ الدِّينِ، وَجِمَاعُ الْمُسْلِمِينَ، وَالْعُدَّةُ لِلاْعْدَاءِ، الْعَامَّةُ مِنَ الاْمَّةِ، فَلْيَكُنْ صِغْوُكَ لَهُمْ، وَمَيْلُكَ مَعَهُمْ⟫

The one among the people under you who is furthest from you and the worst of them in your view should be he who is the most inquisitive of the shortcomings of the people, because people do have shortcomings and the ruler is the most appropriate person to cover them. Do not disclose whatever of it is hidden from you because your obligation is to correct what is manifest to you, while Allah will deal with whatever is hidden from you. Therefore, cover shortcomings so far as you can; Allah would cover those of your shortcomings which you would like to remain under cover from your subjects. Unfasten every knot of hatred in the people and cut away from yourself the cause of every enmity. Feign ignorance from what is not clear to you. Do not hasten to second a backbiter, because a backbiter is a cheat although he looks like those who wish well.

⟪ar-quote:وَلْيَكُنْ أَبْعَدَ رَعِيَّتِكَ مِنْكَ، وَأشْنَأَهُمْ عِنْدَكَ، أَطْلَبُهُمْ لِمَعَائِبِ النَّاسِ، فإنَّ في النَّاسِ عُيُوباً، الْوَالِي أَحَقُّ مَنْ سَتَرَهَا، فَلاَ تَكْشِفَنَّ عَمَّا غَابَ عَنْكَ مِنْهَا، فَإنَّمَا عَلَيْكَ تَطْهِيرُ مَا ظَهَرَ لَكَ، وَاللهُ يَحْكُمُ عَلَى مَا غَابَ عَنْكَ، فَاسْتُرِ الْعَوْرَةَ مَا اسْتَطَعْتَ يَسْتُرِ اللهُ مِنْكَ ما تُحِبُّ سَتْرَهُ مِنْ رَعِيَّتِكَ. أَطْلِقْ عَنِ النَّاسِ عُقْدَةَ كُلِّ حِقْد، وَاقْطَعْ عَنْكَ سَبَبَ كُلِّ وِتْر، وَتَغَابَ عَنْ كلِّ مَا لاَ يَضِحُ لَكَ، وَلاَ تَعْجَلَنَّ إِلَى تَصْدِيقِ سَاع، فَإِنَّ السَّاعِيَ غَاشٌ،⟫

Do not include among those you consult a miser who would keep you back from being generous and caution you against destitution, nor a coward who would make you feel too weak for your affairs, nor a greedy person who would make beautiful to you the collection of wealth by evil ways. This is because miserliness, cowardice and greed are different qualities that an unfavourable opinion of Allah brings together.

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ تُدْخِلَنَّ فِي مَشُورَتِكَ بَخِيلاً يَعْدِلُ بِكَ عَنِ الْفَضْلِ، وَيَعِدُكَ الْفَقْرَ، وَلاَ جَبَاناً يُضعِّفُكَ عَنِ الاْمُورِ، وَلاَ حَرِيصاً يُزَيِّنُ لَكَ الشَّرَهَ بِالْجَوْرِ، فَإِنَّ الْبُخْلَ وَالْجُبْنَ وَالْحِرْصَ غَرَائِزُ شَتَّى يَجْمَعُهَا سُوءُ الظَّنِّ بِاللهِ⟫

The worst minister for you is he who has been a minister for mischievous people before you, and who joined them in sins. Therefore, he should not be your chief man, because they are abettors of sinners and brothers of the oppressors. You can find good substitutes for them who will be like them in their views and influence, while not being like them in sins and vices. They have never assisted an oppressor in his oppression or a sinner in his sin. They will give you the least trouble and the best support. They will be most considerate towards you and the least inclined towards others. Therefore, make them your chief companions in privacy as well as in public.

⟪ar-quote:شَرُّ وُزَرَائِكَ مَنْ كَانَ لِلاْشْرَارِ قَبْلَكَ وَزِيراً، وَمَنْ شَرِكَهُمْ فِي الاْثَامِ، فَلاَ يَكُونَنَّ لَكَ بِطَانَةً، فَإِنَّهُمْ أَعْوَانُ الاْثَمَةِ، وَإِخْوَانُ الظَّلَمَةِ، وَأَنْتَ وَاجِدٌ مِنْهُمْ خَيْرَ الْخَلَفِ مِمَّنْ لَهُ مِثْلُ آرَائِهِمْ وَنَفَاذِهِمْ، وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ مِثْلُ آصَارِهِمْ وَأَوْزَارِهِمْ وَ آثَامِهِمْ، مِمَّنْ لَمْ يُعَاوِنْ ظَالِماً عَلَى ظُلْمِهِ، وَلاَ آثِماً عَلَى إِثْمِهِ، أُولئِكَ أَخَفُّ عَلَيْكَ مَؤُونَةً، وَأَحْسَنُ لَكَ مَعُونَةً، وَأَحْنَى عَلَيْكَ عَطْفاً، وَأَقَلُّ لِغَيْرِكَ إِلْفاً، فَاتَّخِذْ أُولئِكَ خَاصَّةً لِخَلَوَاتِكَ وَحَفَلاَتِكَ⟫

Then, more preferable among them for you should be those who openly speak bitter truths before you and who support you least in those of your actions which Allah does not approve in His friends, even though they may be according to your wishes. Associate yourself with God-fearing and truthful people; then educate them, so that they should not praise you or please you by reason of an action you did not perform, because an excess of praise produces pride and drives you near haughtiness.

⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ لْيَكُنْ آثَرُهُمْ عِنْدَكَ أَقْوَلَهُمْ بِمُرِّ الْحَقِّ لَكَ، وأَقَلَّهُمْ مُسَاعَدَةً فِيَما يَكُونُ مِنْكَ مِمَّا كَرِهَ اللهُ لاِوْلِيَائِهِ، وَاقِعاً ذلِكَ مِنْ هَوَاكَ حَيْثُ وَقَعَ. وَالْصَقْ بِأَهْلِ الْوَرَعِ وَالصِّدْقِ، ثُمَّ رُضْهُمْ عَلَى أَلاَّ يُطْرُوكَ وَلاَ يُبَجِّحُوكَ بِبَاطِل لَمْ تَفْعَلْهُ، فَإِنَّ كَثْرَةَ الاْطْرَاءِ تُحْدِثُ الزَّهْوَ، وَتُدْنِي مِنَ الْعِزَّةِ⟫

The virtuous and the vicious should not be in equal position before you because this means dissuasion of the virtuous from virtue and persuasion of the vicious to vice. Keep everyone in their appropriate position. You should know that the most conducive thing for the good impression of the ruler on his subjects is that he should extend good behaviour towards them, lighten their hardships, and avoid putting them to unbearable troubles. You should therefore, in this way follow a course by which you will leave a good impression with your subjects, because such good ideas will relieve you of great worries. Certainly, the one most entitled to have a favourable impression of you is he whom whom you have treated well, and the one most entilted to have a bad opinion of you is he whom you have treated badly.

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ يَكُونَنَّ الْـمُحْسِنُ وَالْمُسِيءُ عِنْدَكَ بِمَنْزِلَة سَوَاء، فَإِنَّ فِي ذلِكَ تَزْهِيداً لاِهْلِ الاْحْسَانِ فِي الاْحْسَانِ،تَدْرِيباً لاِهْلِ الاْسَاءَةِ عَلَى الاْسَاءَةِ، وَأَلْزِمْ كُلاًّ مِنْهُمْ مَا أَلْزَمَ نَفْسَهُ. وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّهُ لَيْسَ شَيْءٌ بِأَدْعَى إِلَى حُسْنِ ظَنِّ وَال بِرَعِيَّتِهِ مِنْ إحْسَانِهِ إِلَيْهِمْ، وَتَخْفِيفِهِ الْمَؤُونَاتِ عَلَيْهِمْ، وَتَرْكِ اسْتِكْرَاهِهِ إِيَّاهُمْ عَلَى مَا لَيْسَ لهُ قِبَلَهُمْ، فَلْيَكُنْ مِنْكَ فِي ذلِكَ أَمْرٌ يَجَتَمِعُ لَكَ بِهِ حُسْنُ الظَّنِّ بِرَعِيَّتِكَ، فَإِنَّ حُسْنَ الظَّنِّ يَقْطَعُ عَنْكَ نَصَباً طَوِيلاً، وَإِنَّ أَحَقَّ مَنْ حَسُنَ ظَنُّكَ بِهِ لَمَنْ حَسُنَ بَلاَؤُكَ عِنْدَهُ، وَإِنَّ أَحَقَّ مَنْ سَاءَ ظَنُّكَ بِهِ لَمَنْ سَاءَ بَلاَؤُكَ عِنْدَهُ⟫

Do not discontinue the good practices which the earlier people of this community had acted upon, by virtue of which there was general unity and through which the subjects prospered. Do not innovate any line of action which injures these earlier practices because (in that case) the reward for those who had established those practices will continue, but the burden for discontinuing them will be on you. Keep on increasing your conversations with the scholars and discussions with the wise to stabilize the prosperity of the areas under you, and to continue with that in which your predecessors had established.

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ تَنْقُضْ سُنَّةً صَالِحَةً عَمِلَ بِهَا صُدُورُ هذِهِ الاْمَّةِ، وَاجْتَمَعتْ بِهَا الاْلْفَةُ، وَصَلَحَتْ عَلَيْهَا الرَّعِيَّةُ،لاَ تُحْدِثَنَّ سُنَّةً تَضُرُّ بِشَيء مِنْ مَاضِي تِلْكَ السُّنَنِ، فَيَكُونَ الاْجْرُ بِمَنْ سَنَّهَا، وَالْوِزْرُ عَلَيْكَ بِمَا نَقَضْتَ مِنْهَا. وَأَكْثِرْ مُدَارَسَةَ الَعُلَمَاءِ، وَمُنَافَثَةَ الْحُكَمَاءِ، فِي تَثْبِيتِ مَا صَلَحَ عَلَيْهِ أَمْرُ بِلاَدِكَ،⟫

Know that the people consist of classes who prosper only with the help of one another, and they are not independent of one another. Among them are the army of Allah, then the secretarial workers of the common people and the chiefs, then the dispensers of justice, then those engaged in law and order, then the payers of head tax (jizyah) and land tax (kharaj) from the protected unbelievers and the common Muslims, then there are the traders and the men of industry and then the lowest class of the needy and the destitute. Allah has fixed the share of every one of them and laid down His precepts about the limits of each in His Book (Qur'an) and the sunnah of His Prophet by way of of a settlement which is preserved with us.⟪ar-quote:وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ الرَّعِيَّةَ طَبَقَاتٌ لاَ يَصْلُحُ بَعْضُهَا إلاَّ بِبَعْض، وَلاَ غِنَى بِبَعْضِهَا عَنْ بَعْض- فَمِنْهَا جُنُودُ اللهِ،مِنْهَا كُتَّابُ الْعَامَّةِ وَالْخَاصَّةِ، وَمِنْهَا قُضَاةُ الْعَدْلِ، وَمِنهَا عُمَّالُ الاْنْصَافِ وَالرِّفْقِ، وَمِنْهَا أَهْلُ الْجِزْيَةِ وَالْخَراجِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الذِّمَّةِ وَمُسْلِمَةِ النَّاسِ، وَمِنْهَا التُّجَّارُ وَأَهْلُ الصِّنَاعَاتِ، وَمِنهَا الطَّبَقَةُ السُّفْلَى مِنْ ذَوِي الْحَاجَةِ وَالْمَسْكَنَةِ، وَكُلٌّ قَدْ سَمَّى اللهُ سَهْمَهُ، وَوَضَعَ عَلَى حَدِّهِ وَفَرِيضَتِهِ فِي كِتَابِهِ أَوْ سُنَّةِ نَبِيِّهِ (صلى الله عليه وآله)عَهْداً مِنْهُ عِنْدَنَا مَحْفُوظاً⟫

Now the army is, by the will of Allah, the fortress of the subjects, the ornament of the ruler, the strength of the religion and the means of peace. The subjects cannot exist without them while the army can be maintained only by the funds fixed by Allah in the revenues, through which they acquire the strength to fight the enemies, on which they depend for their prosperity, and with which they meet their needs. These two classes cannot exist without the third class namely the judges, the executives and the secretaries who pass judgements about contracts, collect revenues and are depended upon in special and general matters.

⟪ar-quote:فَالْجُنُودُ، بِإِذْنِ اللهِ، حُصُونُ الرَّعِيَّةِ، وَزَيْنُ الْوُلاَةِ، وعِزُّ الدِّينِ، وَسُبُلُ الاْمْنِ، وَلَيْسَ تَقُومُ الرَّعِيَّةُ إِلاَّ بِهِمْ. ثُمَّ لاَ قِوَامَ لِلْجُنُودِ إِلاَّ بِمَا يُخْرِجُ اللهُ لَهُمْ مِنَ الْخَرَاجِ الَّذِي يَقْوَوْنَ بِهِ فِي جِهَادِ عَدُوِهِمْ، وَيَعْتَمِدُونَ عَلَيْهِ فِيَما أصْلَحهُمْ، وَيَكُونُ مِنْ وَرَاءِ حَاجَتِهِمْ. ثُمَّ لاَ قِوَامَ لِهذَيْنِ الصِّنْفَيْنِ إِلاَّ بِالصِّنْفِ الثَّالِثِ مِنَ الْقُضَاةِ وَالْعُمَّالِ وَالْكُتَّابِ، لِمَا يُحْكِمُونَ مِنَ الْمَعَاقِدِ، وَيَجْمَعُونَ مِنْ الْمَنَافِعِ، وَيُؤْتَمَنُونَ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ خَوَاصِّ الاْمُورِ وَعَوَامِّهَا⟫

And these classes cannot exist except with the traders and men of industry, who provide necessities for them, establish markets and make it possible for others not to do all this with their own hands. Then is the lowest class of the needy and the destitute support of and help for whom is an obligation, and everyone of them has (a share in) livelihood in the name of Allah. Everyone of them has a right on the ruler according to what is needed for his prosperity. The ruler cannot acquit himself of the obligations laid on him by Allah in this matter except by striving and seeking help from Allah and by training himself to adhere to the right and by enduring on that account all that is light or hard.

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ قِوَامَ لَهُمْ جَمِيعاً إِلاَّ بِالتُّجَّارِ وَذَوِي الصِّنَاعَاتِ، فِيَما يَجْتَمِعُونَ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ مَرَافِقِهِمْ، وَيُقِيمُونَهُ مِنْ أَسْوَاقِهِمْ، وَيَكْفُونَهُمْ مِنَ التَّرَفُّقِ بِأَيْدِيهِمْ ممّا لاَ يَبْلُغُهُ رِفْقُ غَيْرِهِمْ. ثُمَّ الطَّبَقَةُ السُّفْلَى مِنْ أَهْلِ الْحَاجَةِ وَالْمَسْكَنَةِ الَّذِينَ يَحِقُّ رِفْدُهُمْ وَمَعُونَتُهُمْ. وَفِي اللهِ لِكُلّ سَعَةٌ، وَلِكُلٍّ عَلَى الْوَالِي حَقٌ بِقَدْرِ مَا يُصْلِحُهُ. وَلَيْسَ يَخْرُجُ الْوَالِي مِنْ حَقِيقَةِ مَا أَلْزَمَهُ اللهُ مِنْ ذلِكَ إِلاَّ بِالاْهْتِمامِ وَالاسْتِعَانَةِ بِاللهِ، وَتَوْطِينِ نَفْسِهِ عَلَى لُزُومِ الْحَقِّ، وَالصَّبْرِ عَلَيْهِ فِيَما خَفَّ عَلَيْهِ أَوْ ثَقُلَ

.⟫

1. The Army

Put in command of your forces the man who in your view is the best well - wisher of Allah, His Prophet and your Imam. **The chastest of them in heart and the highest of them in endurance is he who is slow in getting enraged, accepts excuses, is kind to the weak and is strict with the strong; violence should not raise his temper and weakness should not keep him sitting.**

⟪ar-quote:فَوَلِّ مِنْ جُنُودِكَ أَنْصَحَهُمْ فِي نَفْسِكَ لله وَلِرَسُولِهِ وَلاِمَامِكَ، وَأَنْقَاهُمْ جَيْباً، وَأَفْضَلَهُمْ حِلْماً مِمَّنْ يُبْطِىءُ عَنِ الْغَضَبِ، وَيَسْتَرِيحُ إِلَى الْعُذْرِ، وَيَرْأَفُ بِالضُّعَفَاءِ، وَيَنْبُو عَلَى الاْقْوِيَاءِ، وَمِمَّنْ لاَ يُثِيرُهُ الْعُنْفُ، وَلاَ يَقْعُدُ بِهِ الضَّعْفُ⟫

Also associate with considerate people from high families, virtuous houses and decent traditions, then people of courage, valour, generosity and benevolence, because they are repositories of honour and springs of virtues. Strive for their matters as the parents strive for their child. Do not regard anything that you do to strengthen them as big nor consider anything that you have agreed to do for them as little (so as to give it up), even though it may be small, because this will make them your well-wishers and create a good impression of you. Do not neglect to attend to their small matters, confining yourself to their important matters, because your small favours will also be of benefit to them while the important ones are such that they cannot ignore them.

⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ الْصَقْ بَذَوِي الْمُرُوءَاتِ وَالاْحْسَابِ، وَأَهْلِ الْبُيُوتَاتِ الصَّالِحَةِ، وَالسَّوَابِقِ الْحَسَنَةِ، ثُمَّ أَهْلِ النَّجْدَةِ وَالشَّجَاعَةِ، وَالسَّخَاءِ وَالسَّماحَةِ، فَإِنَّهُمْ جِمَاعٌ مِنَ الْكَرَمِ، وَشُعَبٌ مِنَ الْعُرْفِ. ثُمَّ تَفَقَّدْ مِنْ أُمُورِهِمْ مَا يَتَفَقَّدُهُ الْوَالِدَانِ مِنْ وَلَدِهِمَا، وَلاَ يَتَفَاقَمَنَّ فِي نَفْسِكَ شَيْءٌ قَوَّيْتَهُمْ بِهِ، وَلاَ تَحْقِرَنَّ لُطْفاً تَعَاهَدْتَهُمْ بِهِ وَإِنْ قَلَّ، فَإِنَّهُ دَاعِيَةٌ لَهُمْ إِلَى بَذْلِ النَّصِيحَةِ لَكَ، وَحُسْنِ الظَّنِّ بِكَ. وَلاَ تَدَعْ تَفَقُّدَ لَطيِفِ أُمُورِهِمُ اتِّكَالاً عَلَى جَسِيمِهَا، فَإِنَّ لِلْيَسِيرِ مِنْ لُطْفِكَ مَوْضِعاً يَنْتَفِعُونَ بِهِ، وَلِلْجَسِيمِ مَوْقِعاً لاَ يَسْتَغْنُونَ عَنْهُ.⟫

That commander of the army should have such a position before you that he renders help to them equitably and spends from his money on them and on those of their families who remain behind so that all their worries converge on the one worry for fighting the enemy. Your kindness to them will turn their hearts to you. The most pleasant thing for the rulers is the establishment of justice in their areas and the manifestation of the love of their subjects, but the subjects' love manifests itself only when their hearts are clean. Their good wishes prove correct only when they surround their commanders (to protect them). Do not regard their positions to be a burden over them and do not keep watching for the end of their tenure. Therefore, be broad-minded in regard to their desires, continue praising them and recounting the good deeds of those who have shown such deeds, because the mention of good actions shakes the brave and rouses the weak, if Allah so wills.

⟪ar-quote:وَلْيَكُنْ آثَرُ رُؤوسِ جُنْدِكَ عِنْدَكَ مَنْ وَاسَاهُمْ فِي مَعُونَتِهِ، وَأَفْضَلَ عَلَيْهِمْ مِنْ جِدَتِهِ بِمَا يَسَعُهُمْ يَسَعُ مَنْ وَرَاءَهُمْ مِنْ خُلُوفِ أَهْلِيهِمْ حَتَّى يَكُونَ هَمُّهُمْ هَمّاً وَاحِداً فِي جِهَادِ الْعَدُوِّ، فَإِنَّ عَطْفَكَ عَلَيْهِمْ يَعْطِفُ قُلُوبَهُمْ عَلَيْكَ. وَإِنَّ أَفْضَلَ قُرَّةِ عَيْنِ الْوُلاَةِ اسْتِقَامَةُ الْعَدْلِ فِي الْبِلاَدِ، وَظُهُورُ مَوَدَّةِ الرَّعِيَّةِ، وَإِنَّهُ لاَ تَظْهَرُ مَوَدَّتُهُمْ إِلاَّ بَسَلاَمَةِ صُدُورِهِمْ، وَلاَ تَصِحُّ نَصِيحَتُهُمْ إِلاّ بِحِيطَتِهِمْ عَلَى وُلاَةِ أُمُورِهِمْ، وَقِلَّةِ اسْتِثْقَالِ دُوَلِهِمْ، وَتَرْكِ اسْتِبْطَاءِ انْقِطَاعِ مُدَّتِهِمْ. فَافْسَحْ فِي آمَالِهِمْ، وَوَاصِلْ فِي حُسْنِ الثَّنَاءِ عَلَيْهِمْ، وَتَعْدِيدِ مَا أَبْلى ذَوُوالْبَلاَءِ مِنْهُمْ، فَإِنَّ كَثْرَةَ الذِّكْرِ لِحُسْنِ أَفْعَالِهِمْ تَهُزُّ الشُّجَاعَ، وَتُحَرِّضُ النَّاكِلَ، إِنْ شَاءَ اللهُ⟫

Appreciate the performance of every one of them, do not attribute the performance of one to the other, and do not minimize the reward below the level of the performance. The high position of a man should not lead you to regard his small deeds as big, nor should the low position of a man make you regard his big deeds as small.

⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ اعْرِفْ لِكُلِّ امْرِىء مِنْهُمْ مَا أَبْلى، وَلاَ تَضُمَّنَّ بَلاَءَ امْرِىء إِلَى غَيْرِهِ، وَلاَ تُقَصِّرَنَّ بِهِ دُونَ غَايَةِ بَلاَئِهِ، وَلاَ يَدْعُوَنَّكَ شَرَفُ امْرِىء إِلَى أَنْ تُعْظِمَ مِنْ بَلاَئِهِ مَا كَانَ صَغِيراً، وَلاَضَعَةُ امْرِىء إِلَى أَنْ تَسْتَصْغِرَ مِنْ يَلاَئِهِ مَاكَانَ عَظيِماً⟫

Refer to Allah and His Prophet the affairs which wory you and matters which appear confusing to you, because, addressing the people whom Allah the Sublime, wishes to guide, He said-

> ⟪quran 4:59⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوٓا۟ أَطِيعُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ وَأَطِيعُوا۟ ٱلرَّسُولَ وَأُو۟لِى ٱلْأَمْرِ مِنكُمْ ۖ فَإِن تَنَزَعْتُمْ فِى شَىْءٍۢ فَرُدُّوهُ إِلَى ٱللَّهِ وَٱلرَّسُولِ إِن كُنتُمْ تُؤْمِنُونَ بِٱللَّهِ وَٱلْيَوْمِ ٱلْآخِرِ ۚ ذَلِكَ خَيْرٌۭ وَأَحْسَنُ تَأْوِيلًا ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Obey Allah and obey the Messenger (Muhammad PBUH), and those of you (Muslims) who are in authority.&nbsp;(And) if you differ in anything amongst yourselves, refer it to Allah and His Messenger (PBUH), if you believe in Allah and in the Last Day.&nbsp;That is better and more suitable for final determination.&nbsp;*
>O you who believe! Obey Allah and obey the Messenger and those in authority among you. And if you dispute among yourselves about anything, refer it to Allah and His Messenger, if you believe in Allah and the Last Day. That is better and better in the end.
> — **Quran 4:59 (inline widget)**

Another definition of justice is that in the Hereafter, in the sight of Allah, all things are established in the same places and ranks, in this world as well.

If we look at this principle in the governmental and social sphere, we will find that justice is attained as a result of piety and righteousness**. He says that as much as the ruler has the right over his subjects, the right of the subjects is over his ruler. He says that the ruler cannot be righteous ⟪ar:’صالح‘⟫ unless the ruler is righteous, and the ruler cannot be righteous unless his subjects are righteous. If the subjects fulfill the rights of their ruler, and the ruler fulfills the rights of his subjects, then the truth will be respected, the paths of religion will prevail, and the flags of justice will be established. That is why you have put so much emphasis on the piety of the ruler.

If we analyze the life of Amir al-Mu'minin, we will find that his entire life has been spent according to these divine principles and divine nature. It is not possible to describe all these aspects. But if we consider only one aspect of this, when his apparent caliphate was established after the assassination of Uthman, this fact becomes clear. If we examine the history carefully, we will find that the civil war caused by Mu'awiya's rebellion did not begin in Siffin, but in Medina. When Ali (a.s.) came to the throne of the Caliphate, he (his cousin) ⟪ar:ابن عباس⟫advised him to let the heads of Uthman's government remain in their positions for the time being. When you have formed your government, then you will depose them. He said, "I have no doubt that what you are saying is the best strategy for reconciliation in this world." But I have⟪ar:الادھی یلزمنی من الحق⟫ an obligation to the truth.  When I know the truth about the Walis established by Uthman, how can I keep them in their positions? Oh my God! I will never keep them in their positions!

He deposed Mu'awiya and all the other governors as soon as he came to the caliphate. It was clear to you that ⟪ar:ابن عباس⟫there was certainly a worldly success in his strategy. This is because Mu'awiya wanted only worldly power and government, and he was content with the rule of Syria for the rest of his life. Although historians have seen Ali's act as a political mistake, we should look at his actions from the point of view of hatred of this world and its government and luxury. Whenever the comfort of the world has been achieved at the expense of the principles of the Hereafter, you have always rejected such simplicity. As he said in one of his letters, "When people abandon a part of their religion for the sake of the world, Allah opens the gates of more trouble for them in this world." And it is clear that Ali's retaining the people of the Ottoman period (whose wickedness and corruption were well known) was merely a matter of strategy, his renunciation of a part of his religion for the sake of the world, and his compromise with it.  And even such an idea was unimaginable to you. In this case, and in countless other such decisions, and especially in the letter to Malik al-Ashtar, we see this attitude of your justice clearly.<!-- section 11 (id=3594, raw_sort=11): عدل اور ظلم -->Since this letter is addressed to one of Maulana Ali's dearest associates, your warning against tyranny and tyranny needs to be understood in a certain way. These messages are not only for those who are just themselves, and want to rule with justice, but also for those who, although they believe in the philosophy of justice, have the potential to be drawn to tyranny. For when the intoxication of the government rises, it makes even the just king a tyrant.

The potential for evil is present in every human being. When this power is combined with personal resources, and the ruler is deprived of divine support, then that potential state of evil becomes a reality. At the beginning of his letter, he says to Malik al-Ashtar, "Give priority to the obedience of Allah over everything else!" And obey the commandments that are in His book, for he who follows ⟪ar:’سعد‘⟫ them is done, and he who disobeys ⟪ar:’خبیث‘⟫ them is done. This preamble of yours is introductory, but not just a notification. Not only is it obligatory to obey Allah, but it also grants spiritual freedom. This plague frees the soul from the tyranny of the soul because ⟪ar-quote:ان انفس أمارۃ بالسوء الا ما رحم ربی⟫ (the soul commands evil until the mercy of Allah is attached)*! ⟪ar:حضرت یوسف علیہ السلام⟫

> ⟪quran 12:53⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ وَمَآ أُبَرِّئُ نَفْسِىٓ ۚ إِنَّ ٱلنَّفْسَ لَأَمَّارَةٌۢ بِٱلسُّوٓءِ إِلَّا مَا رَحِمَ رَبِّىٓ ۚ إِنَّ رَبِّى غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *"And I free not myself (from the blame). Verily, the (human) self is inclined to evil, except when my Lord bestows His Mercy (upon whom He wills). Verily, my Lord is Oft-Forgiving, Most Merciful." *
> And I do not say of my own acquittal. Indeed, the soul incites evil, except upon whom my Lord has mercy. Indeed my Lord is Forgiving and Merciful.
> — **Quran 12:53 (inline widget)**

This statement clearly shows the relationship between divine grace⟪ar:رحم⟫ and the self. If this mercy of the Lord is not involved, then the soul is inclined towards sin and evil, but by the grace of Allah, the soul is freed from the trap of its own desires and desires and returns to its original nature with satisfaction, for which the Qur'an says:

> ⟪quran 89:27-29⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيَّتُهَا ٱلنَّفْسُ ٱلْمُطْمَئِنَّةُ ‎ ‏ٱرْجِعِىٓ إِلَىٰ رَبِّكِ رَاضِيَةًۭ مَّرْضِيَّةًۭ ‎ ‏فَٱدْخُلِى فِى عِبَدِى ‎⟫
> *(It will be said to the pious): "O (you) the one in (complete) rest and satisfaction! " Come back to your Lord, Well-pleased (yourself) and well-pleasing unto Him! "Enter you, then, among My honoured slaves,*
> Return, O soul of peace, to your Lord, well-pleased with Him, so be one of My servants.
> — **Quran 89:27-29 (inline widget)**

So it is understood that 'nature' is the beginning and the end of the self, because the self is carved into the divine nature and its return is also towards this natural state.<!-- section 12 (id=3595, raw_sort=12): روحانیت اور اخلاق -->Amir al-Mu'minin says in his first sermon:

---

⟪ar-quote:وَاصْطَفى سُبْحَانَهُ مِنْ وَلَدَهِ أَنْبيَاءَ أَخَذَ عَلَى الْوَحْيِ مِيثَاقَهُم، وَعَلَى تَبْليغِ الرِّسَالَةِ أَمَانَتَهُمْ، لَمَّا بَدَّلَ أَكْثَرُ خَلْقِهِ عَهْدَ اللهِ إِلَيْهِمْ، فَجَهِلُوا حَقَّهُ، واتَّخَذُوا الاْنْدَادَ مَعَهُ، وَاجْتَالَتْهُمُ الشَّيَاطِينُ عَنْ مَعْرفَتِهِ، وَاقتَطَعَتْهُمْ عَنْ عِبَادَتِهِ، فَبَعَثَ فِيهمْ رُسُلَهُ، وَوَاتَرَ إِلَيْهِمْ أَنْبِياءَهُ،**لِيَسْتَأْدُوهُمْ مِيثَاقَ فِطْرَتِهِ**، وَيُذَكِّرُوهُمْ مَنْسِيَّ نِعْمَتِهِ، وَيَحْتَجُّوا عَلَيْهِمْ بَالتَّبْلِيغِ، **وَيُثِيرُوا لَهُمْ دَفَائِنَ الْعُقُولِ**، وَيُرُوهُمْ آيَاتِ الْمَقْدِرَةِ⟫

From his (Adam’s) progeny Allah chose prophets and took their pledge for his revelation and for carrying His message as their trust. In course of time many people perverted Allah’s trust with them and ignored His position and took compeers along with Him. Satan turned them away from knowing Him and kept them aloof from His worship. Then Allah sent His Messengers and series of His prophets towards them to get them to fulfil the pledges of His creation, to recall to them His bounties, to exhort them by preaching, to unveil before them the hidden virtues of wisdom and show them the signs of His Omnipotence

---

These buried treasures are the ⟪ar:’علم کلی‘⟫ ones that were given to these souls on the eternal day, and this knowledge, nature and life, was their 'nature', because they are the possibility of the existence of all good things. That is why the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to say, "It should be your most beloved deed ⟪ar:’عمل صالح‘⟫ , because ⟪ar:’الحق‘⟫ it is not only the root of all good deeds, but it is also the essence of all creation." In one place, he praises Allah, saying:

By Thy majesty which fills all things, by Thy names which are the foundation of all things, by Thy knowledge which encompasses all things, by the light of Thy face by which everything is illuminated.

From this point of view, every good deed ⟪ar:خُلق حسنۃ⟫in this world is a reflection of one or the other ⟪ar:’الہی صفت‘⟫ , and that is one of the names of Allah! ⟪ar:’أحسانی‘⟫ ⟪ar-quote:تخلُقو بأخلاق اللہ⟫ In morality and divinity, monotheism is established in such a way that on the one hand, creating good morals attracts the divine substance, and on the other hand, the same 'divine substance' has become the essence of every good creation. That is, every good quality is related to itself and in the expression of its existence! ⟪ar:’اللہُ وحدہ لا شریک لہ‘⟫ Allah says in the Qur'an:

> ⟪quran 8:17⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَلَمْ تَقْتُلُوهُمْ وَلَكِنَّ ٱللَّهَ قَتَلَهُمْ ۚ وَمَا رَمَيْتَ إِذْ رَمَيْتَ وَلَكِنَّ ٱللَّهَ رَمَىٰ ۚ وَلِيُبْلِىَ ٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ مِنْهُ بَلَآءً حَسَنًا ۚ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ سَمِيعٌ عَلِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *You killed them not, but Allah killed them. And you (Muhammad PBUH) threw not when you did throw but Allah threw, that He might test the believers by a fair trial from Him. Verily, Allah is All-Hearer, All-Knower.*
> It was not you who killed them, but it was God who killed them. And you did not throw your handful when you threw, but it was God who threw, and that He might bestow His grace on the believers. God is All-hearing, All-knowing.
> — **Quran 8:17 (inline widget)**

This shows that ⟪ar:’متقی‘⟫ in order to exist, it is not enough for a person to negate his own self, but he also has to develop divine attributes in himself. Knowledge of the attributes of Allah will humble him, and he will turn his soul away from desires and towards divine realities, which are the essence of all virtue and morality.

Now we consider him ⟪ar:’نفس امارۃ‘⟫ ( who commands evil) and the story of Yusuf ( Joseph ) . When Joseph's innocence was proved in the king's court, he said, "I do not exonerate myself!" Indeed, the soul commands evil until the mercy of Allah is attached. In the story of Zulekha, the Qur'an clearly states that her success was not due to her own self, but to the grace of Allah. In the test of evil desires and false satisfaction, no other verse can better describe this helplessness of man, except this verse: ⟪ar-quote:إِنَّ ٱلنَّفْسَ لَأَمَّارَةٌۢ بِٱلسُّوٓءِ إِلَّا مَا رَحِمَ رَبِّىٓ⟫ So the human soul lives between two pillars. The first is his own selfish desires, which lead to evil in this temporary deceitful world. The second pillar is its attention to the grace of God, which returns the soul to its original position. This proves that man needs the grace of Allah at all times. The moment this grace stops, the moment a person will be inclined to sin. That is why you begin your letter with this verse because you entrusted Malik al-Ashtar with the government of a place that was full of wealth and where the chances of inclination towards evil were high. When a person tries to avoid sins, it does not mean that he is self-sufficient and does not need the grace of Allah. Rather, he shows that Allah's grace is upon him, and only then does he desire not to sin and strives. And the pursuit of goodness is also a sign of Allah's bounty, which Allah has placed in its original (nature) the Day of Eternity, which He invokes by His sincere efforts to attract more of the bounty that He has received from Allah.

It is worth noting that, although we find a full explanation of the laws that need to be fulfilled in order to do justice, we do not find how to keep these laws in the face of an onslaught of desires, power and greed. Laws can be made to punish the oppressor, but the 'intention' not to be misled cannot be legislated. For this reason, you give such advice: Break your soul in the form of strong desires, overcome your desires, and restrain yourself from things that are not lawful for you. 

The purpose of living according to just instructions is not merely to superficially obey the laws stated. Rather, their purpose is the moral discipline of the self towards these instructions. In other words, the concept of justice is not just about doing the right thing or obeying the law, but ⟪ar:’الحق‘⟫ about recognizing it. The concept of man shifts from 'doing' to 'being', or from 'action' to 'thinking'. But this does not mean that doing so makes the process weak or indeterminate. Rather, action becomes a mirror of divine thought, and because of this, it grows in strength and abundance. ⟪ar:الحق⟫Constant attention to the self enhances action and establishes truth and justice in the soul. The level of human beings is also of the same level, which ⟪ar:’تحقیق‘⟫ is called 'to do the truth'. 'Spirituality' is researched through spirituality, and 'spirituality' is researched through piety.<!-- section 13 (id=3596, raw_sort=13): کبر اور غرور سے بچنے کی نصیحت -->He warns the owner of the wickedness, "Do not prepare your soul for war with Allah!" What are the actions that are equivalent to fighting against Allah? If you look closely, you will find that in this quote you are referring to attitudes in which there is apparent evil in actions, but thinking is against the spirit of those actions.  We can take the example of arrogance in this regard, which Maulana Ali has warned against in many places. When a ruler becomes 'arrogant', he usurps one of the great attributes of Allah. He considers himself entitled to an attribute that is worthy of Allah alone, because ⟪ar:’المتکبر‘⟫ his title is worthy of him alone. Boasting in front of people and showing off one's greatness is tantamount to inwardly opposing Allah and denying His ⟪ar:أحدیت⟫greatness. This hidden 'denial' can be seen from the perspective of waging war with Allah. Enmity towards 'ultimately⟪ar:الحق⟫' is the hidden substance that a ruler displays to his subjects in every form of arrogance, arrogance, and oppression. The ruler's notion of superiority over his 'lower' is, in fact, a declaration of rebellion against his 'above'. Therefore, the oppressor not only inflicts the just wrath of the Creator on himself by oppressing the creatures, but also opposes the Creator through his own actions. The root of this worldly evil is ⟪ar:الحق⟫a spiritual defect that arises from the denial of the Lord ⟪ar:أحدیت⟫(who possesses all power and authority), ⟪ar:حقانیت⟫and from forgetting the verse of the Qur'an:

> ⟪quran 40:16⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَوْمَ هُم بَرِزُونَۖ لَا يَخْفَىٰ عَلَى ٱللَّهِ مِنْهُمْ شَىْءٌۭۚ لِّمَنِ ٱلْمُلْكُ ٱلْيَوْمَۖ لِلَّهِ ٱلْوَحِدِ ٱلْقَهَّارِ ‎⟫
> *The Day when they will (all) come out, nothing of them will be hidden from Allah. Whose is the kingdom this Day? (Allah Himself will reply to His Question): It is Allah's the One, the Irresistible!*
> day when they will all come forth, nothing of them will be hidden from Allah.
> — **Quran 40:16 (inline widget)**

This ⟪ar:’الیوم‘⟫ verse does not refer only to the Last Day, but to every day. In his famous sermon (known as Joe⟪ar:’القاصیۃ‘⟫), he describes the humiliation of the arrogant Iblis, saying that he was the first to confront Allah in the field of arrogance, and that is why he became the center and source of all arrogance. When Allah asked him to prostrate himself before Adam, he flatly refused. And he was filled with great pride, and he considered himself greater than Adam, and said, I am made of fire, and man is made of clay.  Because of this arrogance, Iblis not only became the first enemy of Allah, but also became the leader⟪ar:أمام المتعصبین و صلف المستکبرین⟫ of all the arrogant people who came after him. Beware of the sickness caused by his whispers, whispers and tricks! Always wear a cloak of insult!  Crush self-praise under your feet! Keep the shackles away from your neck! and to fortify themselves in the safe building of humility.

This shows that 'humility' is the best weapon against the devil because its real purpose is to inculcate arrogance in man. Arrogance is not only a worst trait in itself, but it is like a killer poison to everyone ⟪ar:خصال محمودۃ⟫else. What is good with arrogance turns into evil. He says, "A sin that grieves you is better than a good deed that makes you arrogant." Times of praise and arrogance provide the best opportunities for Satan to be attacked.

> whosoever is on the earth will perish.

> ⟪quran 55:27⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَيَبْقَىٰ وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو ٱلْجَلَلِ وَٱلْإِكْرَامِ ‎⟫
> *And the Face of your Lord full of Majesty and Honour will abide forever.*
> and of your Lord will remain the Countenance of the Most Majesty and the Most Honourable.
> — **Quran 55:27 (TopicAyats)**<!-- section 14 (id=3601, raw_sort=14): شرک خفی -->Although the outward meaning of shirk is considered to be the worship of idols, in another sense, the worship of idols hidden within the self is also shirk, which exists in the self in the form of intentions, attitudes, inclinations, pride, display, boasting, fabrication, etc. Referring to this, the Prophet (peace and blessings of Allaah be upon him) said, "Shirk is hidden in my Ummah like the trick of a black thorn on a black stone in a black night." He says, "Know that even the slightest bit of hypocrisy is shirk." Because to act for the praise of others and not to act for the sake of Allah is to associate with Allah!  Whoever acts for other than Allah, Allah entrusts that servant to them.

Due to the deterioration of Iblis's inner arrogance, he committed the sin of outward disobedience, which resulted in his destiny of humiliation. Iblis was humiliated because of his disobedience to Allah, and he disobeyed Allah out of arrogance. This shows that kubar itself is a disgrace, and a seed of destruction. Do you not see how Allah has humiliated him? To be arrogant is to be humiliated in reality, and self-aggrandizement is actually self-humiliation. That is why he said to Malik al-Ashtar, "Do not say that I have the authority, I command and I am obeyed." Because such an idea creates a disorder in the heart and destroys the religion. From this statement of yours, it is also understood that for the appearance of religion to be correct, it is necessary that the inner intentions and concepts should be correct. That is why you advise that when power rises to the head, faith comes out of the heart, and that in order for faith to survive in this world, it must come out of the heart and manifest itself in the form of humility. And it is a form of keeping things in their proper place (justice).

Then he says to Malik al-Ashtar, "If your position makes you arrogant and visible, then look at the greatness of Allah over whom you do." This concept will help you overcome your desires, and restore your intellect by protecting you from the rigidity of yourself. The relationship between intellect and humility is worth considering here. The part of the intellect that is distracted by arrogance and pretense, this is the part that understands the reality of Allah, and is aware of the branches that emerge from that reality. In Arabic, it ⟪ar:’مَخِلا‘⟫ is called arrogance, which has its origin in 'khyal'. That is, kubar is an 'idea' that has a deep connection to this real and deceptive world. Arrogance is a severe form of suspicion that arises from a disorder of intellect. He is seen as evil and is recognized as immoral. It has to do not only with thinking of oneself as great, but ⟪ar:الحق⟫also with belittling. Only one ⟪ar:ولی اللہ⟫can understand the reality of the following verses, and draw from them the humility that ⟪ar:’أنائیت‘⟫ erases from the root, which is the root of all arrogance, display, and pride, and which is the food for every oppression:

> ⟪quran 28:88⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَدْعُ مَعَ ٱللَّهِ إِلَهًا آخَرَ ۘ لَآ إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ ۚ كُلُّ شَىْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُۥ ۚ لَهُ ٱلْحُكْمُ وَإِلَيْهِ تُرْجَعُونَ ‎⟫
> *And invoke not any other ilah (god) along with Allah, La ilaha illa Huwa (none has the right to be worshipped but He). Everything will perish save His Face. His is the Decision, and to Him you (all) shall be returned.*
> And do not invoke any other god along with Allah; there is no God except Him; all things will perish except His Face; His is the command, and it is to Him that you will be returned.
> — **Quran 28:88 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 55:26-27⟫

> — **Quran 55:26-27 (inline widget)**

> *And say: "Truth (i.e. Islamic Monotheism or this Quran or Jihad against polytheists) has come and Batil (falsehood, i.e. Satan or polytheism, etc.) has vanished. Surely! Batil is ever bound to vanish." *
> And say, The truth has come, and falsehood has vanished. Falsehood is bound to vanish.
> — **Quran 17:81 (inline widget)**

After understanding these things, we can now enjoy what you said: "Be afraid to imitate Allah and confront Him, for Allah despises every wrongdoer and humiliates every arrogant." And whoever does not do justice to Allah and His creation, he will see that on the Day of Resurrection not only Allah's creation but Allah Himself will be his opponent. Man is in a state of war with Allah until he gives up his oppression and repents before Allah. Even if he survives in this world, he will not be able to survive in the hereafter.

The more the oppressor continues, the more his soul will become wicked, and the more his soul will be soaked in suffering. The Qur'an presents it ⟪ar:’استدراج‘⟫ in the concept of what means degrees of punishment. This verse not only describes these degrees, but also clarifies the distinction between those who do justice to the truth and those who do wrong.

> ⟪quran 7:181-182⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَمِمَّنْ خَلَقْنَآ أُمَّةٌۭ يَهْدُونَ بِٱلْحَقِّ وَبِهِۦ يَعْدِلُونَ ‎ ‏وَٱلَّذِينَ كَذَّبُوا۟ بِـَٔايَتِنَا سَنَسْتَدْرِجُهُم مِّنْ حَيْثُ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫
> *And of those whom We have created, there is a community who guides (others) with the truth, and establishes justice therewith. Those who reject Our Ayat (proofs, evidences, verses, lessons, signs, revelations, etc.), We shall gradually seize them with punishment in ways they perceive not.*
> And of those whom We have created there is a community guiding the truth and justifying by it. And those who belie Our signs, We will seize them little by little from where they are unaware.
> — **Quran 7:181-182 (inline widget)**

This punishment is not only in the form of poverty, sickness and suffering, but also in the form of success, glory and children in the world, as Allah says:

> ⟪quran 9:85⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تُعْجِبْكَ أَمْوَلُهُمْ وَأَوْلَدُهُمْ ۚ إِنَّمَا يُرِيدُ ٱللَّهُ أَن يُعَذِّبَهُم بِهَا فِى ٱلدُّنْيَا وَتَزْهَقَ أَنفُسُهُمْ وَهُمْ كَفِرُونَ ‎⟫
> *And let not their wealth or their children amaze you. Allah's Plan is to punish them with these things in this world, and that their souls shall depart (die) while they are disbelievers.*
> Do not amaze at their riches or their children. Allah only desires to punish them with these in this world, and that their souls will depart while they are unbelievers.
> — **Quran 9:85 (inline widget)**

The wrongdoer can be at the same ⟪ar:’مسلمان‘⟫ time and he can be at ⟪ar:’کافر‘⟫ the same time because of his disbelief (kufr means hiding something) because he has concealed the truth from himself and his deeds, and all the good that comes from it.<!-- section 15 (id=3597, raw_sort=15): اخلاقی و روحانی ضمیر -->Another form of fighting God is to fight with your 'voice of conscience'. A soul, which knows and understands its moral obligations, speaks to the self as the voice of the inner conscience.  It is as if the voice of conscience is really the voice of an awakened soul.

> ⟪quran 91:7-8⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَنَفْسٍۢ وَمَا سَوَّىٰهَا ‎ ‏فَأَلْهَمَهَا فُجُورَهَا وَتَقْوَىٰهَا ‎⟫
> *And by Nafs (Adam or a person or a soul, etc.), and Him Who perfected him in proportion; Then He showed him what is wrong for him and what is right for him;*
> and soul, and He who made it right, then He made to him his evil and his good.
> — **Quran 91:7-8 (inline widget)**

This verse is telling us that ⟪ar:نفس⟫⟪ar:أمارۃ بالسوء⟫ the one who corrects and guides the right path is the 'conscience', on which there are good and bad arguments. A morally awakened soul will inspire goodness, and a low moral soul will inspire evil.  Allah Almighty has sown in every soul in the midst of the conscience, to which the above verse indicates. For this reason, every soul not only distinguishes between good and evil, but it also instinctively recognizes itself ⟪ar:’عبدیت‘⟫ and that of Allah ⟪ar:’الہیت‘⟫. The Qur'an mentions the moment when Allaah created man and took from him a covenant of His Lordship:

> ⟪quran 7:172⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَإِذْ أَخَذَ رَبُّكَ مِنۢ بَنِىٓ آدَمَ مِن ظُهُورِهِمْ ذُرِّيَّتَهُمْ وَأَشْهَدَهُمْ عَلَىٰٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ ۖ قَالُوا۟ بَلَىٰ ۛ شَهِدْنَآ ۛ أَن تَقُولُوا۟ يَوْمَ ٱلْقِيَمَةِ إِنَّا كُنَّا عَنْ هَذَا غَفِلِينَ ‎⟫
> *And (remember) when your Lord brought forth from the Children of Adam, from their loins, their seed (or from Adam's loin his offspring) and made them testify as to themselves (saying): "Am I not your Lord?" They said: "Yes! We testify," lest you should say on the Day of Resurrection: "Verily, we have been unaware of this." *
> And when your Lord brought forth from the Children of Adam from their loins, their offspring, and made them testify as to themselves, I am not your Lord, they said, Yes, we testify. Lest you should say on the Day of Resurrection, We were not aware of this.
> — **Quran 7:172 (inline widget)**

This shows that the wrongdoer is the one who breaks his covenant with Allah and takes himself ⟪ar:نفس امارۃ بالسوء⟫as his Lord instead of believing in Allah as his Lord. For this reason, 'Ali (a.s.) said to Malik al-Ashtar, "Do not say, 'I command, and obey me,' for this is the way ⟪ar:نفس امارۃ بالسوء⟫of the one who commands, and whose commands are obeyed by the body, the soul, the imagination, the intellect, the intention, the emotions, and the consciousness." The way to do justice to oneself is⟪ar:مجاہدۃ النفس⟫ to first remove one's own shortcomings. That is why he said, "If you want to reform others, you must first start with yourself, because trying to improve the souls of others while there is evil in oneself is the greatest sin."

 ⟪ar:مالک اشتر⟫Before him, ⟪ar:محمد بن ابی بکر⟫he had made him the ruler of Egypt. He also advised them, saying, "I have appointed you as the guardian of the people of Egypt." It is inherently incumbent upon you to oppose yourselves and protect your religion! This quote of yours is very interesting! He gave power to Muhammad bin Abi Bakr and imposed two obligations on him. The first is to protect one's own self and its desires, and the second is to protect one's religion. The more power and authority there is, the greater the responsibility to control oneself and to restrain oneself.  This is because if the soul becomes subservient to desires and fulfills them with his own powers, then man not only destroys himself but also destroys religion. The outward act of a Muslim's religion depends on the inner integrity of the soul for its survival.  It's another form of keeping things in their rightful place. Upon attaining power, ⟪ar:نفس امارۃ⟫the Qur'an describes the one who creates arrogance, and the desire for dominance and power, as follows:

> ⟪quran 96:6-7⟫
> ⟪ar:‏كَلَّآ إِنَّ ٱلْإِنسَنَ لَيَطْغَىٰٓ ‎ ‏أَن رَّآهُ ٱسْتَغْنَىٰٓ ‎⟫
> *Nay! Verily, man does transgress all bounds (in disbelief and evil deed, etc.). Because he considers himself self-sufficient.*
> indeed, man becomes arrogant when he finds himself rich.
> — **Quran 96:6-7 (inline widget)**

The more a soul is deceived by 'autonomy' and runs away from trusting in Allah, the more it will come to think of itself as God, and this will be its greatest injustice. He will become the person to whom Allaah says (interpretation of the meaning):

> ⟪quran 45:23⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَفَرَءَيْتَ مَنِ ٱتَّخَذَ إِلَهَهُۥ هَوَىٰهُ وَأَضَلَّهُ ٱللَّهُ عَلَىٰ عِلْمٍۢ وَخَتَمَ عَلَىٰ سَمْعِهِۦ وَقَلْبِهِۦ وَجَعَلَ عَلَىٰ بَصَرِهِۦ غِشَوَةًۭ فَمَن يَهْدِيهِ مِنۢ بَعْدِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ أَفَلَا تَذَكَّرُونَ ‎⟫
> *Have you seen him who takes his own lust (vain desires) as his ilah (god), and Allah knowing (him as such), left him astray, and sealed his hearing and his heart, and put a cover on his sight. Who then will guide him after Allah? Will you not then remember?*
> have you seen him who has become a slave of his own desire, and Allah has led him astray despite his knowledge, and set a seal upon his hearing and his heart, and put a covering on his sight? Who will guide him after Allah? Will you not then understand?
> — **Quran 45:23 (inline widget)**

The more a person acquires the knowledge of his 'contempt' and the more he is in need of Allah, the more his ⟪ar:نفس امارۃ بالسوء⟫grip will loosen around his neck. This is because only the soul that commands itself to evil can command others to do evil, and the soul that humbles itself before Allah can treat people with humility, mercy and justice.

He says, "In your view, your actions should be the most dear, the most just, and the most just, and the most acceptable of the people, because the disapproval of the people weakens the approval of the people." You have insisted on the approval of 'ordinary human beings' in your words! The one who despises himself in the sight of Allaah will be with the common people, and the one who is arrogant will only like the company of the arrogant and will interpret the verse correctly:

> ⟪quran 35:15⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلنَّاسُ أَنتُمُ ٱلْفُقَرَآءُ إِلَى ٱللَّهِۖ وَٱللَّهُ هُوَ ٱلْغَنِىُّ ٱلْحَمِيدُ ‎⟫
> *O mankind! it is you who stand in need of Allah, but Allah is Rich (Free of all wants and needs), Worthy of all praise.*
> O men, it is you who are in need of Allah, and Allah is All-sufficient, All-laudable.
> — **Quran 35:15 (inline widget)**

In this regard, the life of Ameer-ul-Momineen, the Maulai of the Universe, is an argument. Once ⟪ar:آثم بن زیاد⟫, the family of a dervish complained to you that he was living a very poor life unnecessarily. He called them and advised them to take care of their families and not to abandon the gifts given by Allah. He replied, "O Ali! You are telling me all this, and you yourself are wrapped in a khadar sheet and eating dry bread. He said, "Woe to you! I'm not like you! ⟪ar:ائمۃ الحق⟫Allah has made it obligatory for them to live their lives as the poorest people of their people, so that they can feel the poverty of the poor, and so that they do not become greedy.

This incident of yours shows that it is necessary for the ruler to live his worldly life at the level of the poorest person of his subjects. He (Ali) chose for himself the least that he could get. And this was because they had a very deep connection with Him ⟪ar:’الحق‘⟫ , in the light of which every material object in the world became despicable, despicable, and worthless in their eyes.<!-- section 16 (id=3587, raw_sort=16): عدل اور ہمدردی -->Feeling the sufferings of the poor increases the awareness of a person's dependence on his Lord, which allows him to spend his life between hope and fear at the mercy of Allah. And while living such a life, Fitrata treats his fellows with compassion and compassion. The ability to empathize does not go against the requirements of justice in any way, but it is an essential part of justice because it not only helps to keep things in their proper place, but it is in accordance with the nature of the universe, and is a great attribute of truth. For this reason, Allaah has started every Surah of the Qur'an with Bismillah-your-Rahman ar-Rahim, in which He mentions His mercy and protection. We see the same behavior in the lives of the Prophet (s) and Amir al-Mu'minin (a.s.) that they always treated the people of God with mercy. And he did it not because of his personal feelings, but because it was his fault of Allah, as He said:

> ⟪quran 7:156⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ وَٱكْتُبْ لَنَا فِى هَذِهِ ٱلدُّنْيَا حَسَنَةًۭ وَفِى ٱلْآخِرَةِ إِنَّا هُدْنَآ إِلَيْكَ ۚ قَالَ عَذَابِىٓ أُصِيبُ بِهِۦ مَنْ أَشَآءُ ۖ وَرَحْمَتِى وَسِعَتْ كُلَّ شَىْءٍۢ ۚ فَسَأَكْتُبُهَا لِلَّذِينَ يَتَّقُونَ وَيُؤْتُونَ ٱلزَّكَوٰةَ وَٱلَّذِينَ هُم بِـَٔايَتِنَا يُؤْمِنُونَ ‎⟫
> *And ordain for us good in this world, and in the Hereafter.&nbsp;Certainly we have turned unto You." He said: (As to) My Punishment I afflict therewith whom I will and My Mercy embraces all things.&nbsp;That (Mercy) I shall ordain for those who are the Muttaqun (pious - see V.2:2), and give Zakat; and those who believe in Our Ayat (proofs, evidences, verses, lessons, signs and revelations, etc.); *
> And ordain for us in this world that which is good, and in the world to come. We turn unto Thee. He said, I afflict with My chastisement whomsoever I will, and My mercy encompasses all things. So I shall ordain it for those who fear Allah and pay the poor-rate and those who believe in Our signs.
> — **Quran 7:156 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 6:54⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَإِذَا جَآءَكَ ٱلَّذِينَ يُؤْمِنُونَ بِـَٔايَتِنَا فَقُلْ سَلَمٌ عَلَيْكُمْ ۖ كَتَبَ رَبُّكُمْ عَلَىٰ نَفْسِهِ ٱلرَّحْمَةَ ۖ أَنَّهُۥ مَنْ عَمِلَ مِنكُمْ سُوٓءًۢا بِجَهَلَةٍۢ ثُمَّ تَابَ مِنۢ بَعْدِهِۦ وَأَصْلَحَ فَأَنَّهُۥ غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *When those who believe in Our Ayat (proofs, evidences, verses, lessons, signs, revelations, etc.) come to you, say: "Salamun 'Alaikum" (peace be on you); your Lord has written Mercy for Himself, so that, if any of you does evil in ignorance, and thereafter repents and does righteous good deeds (by obeying Allah), then surely, He is Oft&shy;Forgiving, Most Merciful.*
> And those who believe in Our verses, when they come to you, say, Peace be upon you. Your Lord has made mercy incumbent upon Himself. So whoever among you does evil in ignorance, then repents thereafter and does good, then indeed He is Oft-Forgiving, Most Merciful.
> — **Quran 6:54 (inline widget)**

Similarly, we also find many sayings of Maulana Ali about mercy. He said: "The act of mercy sends down the mercy of Allah upon you, and you will be shown mercy as you have mercy on others, and I wonder at the one who expects mercy from those above him but does not show mercy to those below him."

According to this theory, the more a person is compassionate in his spiritual thoughts and morals with people, the closer he will be to the Almighty. In a society, justice demands that people should be treated with compassion wherever possible. Of course, sometimes, when there is no other option, severe punishments are imposed. For this reason, in his letter, he asked Malik al-Ashtar to punish those officers who were found guilty of usurping their wealth so that Allah's justice could be established. In another place, he writes to his cousin, whom he appointed as the governor of Basra, "I swear by Allah with all sincerity that if the news reaches me that you have usurped the wealth of the Muslims, whether it is too little or too much, I will punish you severely!" A punishment that will diminish your wealth, break your back, and bring down your deeds.

Similarly, whenever someone asked you for a favor, you would treat them harshly, even if they were your own relatives. Once, your brother Aqeel asked you for more money from Bait-ul-Maal, so you put a burning tongsaw on his hand. Aqeel started crying in pain. He said, "Brother Aqeel, if you cannot bear this little fire, how will I bear the blazing fire of Allah's Hell on the Day of Resurrection to which you are inviting me?" Similarly, when he was informed that his cousin Abdullah ibn 'Abbas had usurped the wealth of the Muslims, he said to them: "Fear Allah! And give back to the people what they deserve. If you do not do that and Allah gives me power over you, then I will strike you with my sword, and whoever I strike has entered the jinn. By Allah, if Hasan and Hussein do the same, they will not get any kind of concession like me.

This shows that no matter how high someone's status, everyone is equal in terms of justice. This act of theirs was quite different from that of the previous caliphs, in which they divided the governments among their relatives and plundered the wealth of the Muslims, as Ali said, in the spring a camel swallows soft buds. Allaah says in the Qur'an:

> ⟪quran 4:135⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ كُونُوا۟ قَوَّمِينَ بِٱلْقِسْطِ شُهَدَآءَ لِلَّهِ وَلَوْ عَلَىٰٓ أَنفُسِكُمْ أَوِ ٱلْوَلِدَيْنِ وَٱلْأَقْرَبِينَ ۚ إِن يَكُنْ غَنِيًّا أَوْ فَقِيرًۭا فَٱللَّهُ أَوْلَىٰ بِهِمَا ۖ فَلَا تَتَّبِعُوا۟ ٱلْهَوَىٰٓ أَن تَعْدِلُوا۟ ۚ وَإِن تَلْوُۥٓا۟ أَوْ تُعْرِضُوا۟ فَإِنَّ ٱللَّهَ كَانَ بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ خَبِيرًۭا ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Stand out firmly for justice, as witnesses to Allah, even though it be against yourselves, or your parents, or your kin, be he rich or poor, Allah is a Better Protector to both (than you).&nbsp;So follow not the lusts (of your hearts), lest you may avoid justice, and if you distort your witness or refuse to give it,  verily, Allah is Ever Well&shy;Acquainted with what you do.*
> O you who believe! Be just, bear witness to Allah, even if it be against yourselves or against your parents or your relatives, whether it be rich or poor, for Allah is better for them than you. So do not follow your desires in justice, and if you distort or transgress, then surely Allah is Aware of what you do.
> — **Quran 4:135 (inline widget)**

This part of your letter is noteworthy in which you have adapted compassion into a universal context in which you have brought the whole world to a level where all are equal. In this statement of yours, there is a cure for all kinds of prejudice and sectarianism. You say

⟪ar-quote:وَأَشْعِرْ قَلْبَكَ الرَّحْمَةَ لِلرَّعِيَّةِ، وَالْـمَحَبَّةَ لَهُمْ، وَاللُّطْفَ بِهِمْ، وَلاَ تَكُونَنَّ عَلَيْهِمْ سَبُعاً ضَارِياً تَغْتَنِمُ أَكْلَهُمْ، فَإِنَّهُمْ صِنْفَانِ- إِمَّا أَخٌ لَكَ فِي الدِّينِ، وَإمّا نَظِيرٌ لَكَ فِي الْخَلْقِ، يَفْرُطُ مِنْهُمُ الزَّلَلُ، وَتَعْرِضُ لَهُمُ الْعِلَلُ،يُؤْتَى عَلَى أَيْدِيهِمْ فِي الَعَمْدِ وَالْخَطَاَ، فَأَعْطِهِمْ مِنْ عَفْوِكَ وَصَفْحِكَ مِثْلَ الَّذِي تُحِبُّ أَنْ يُعْطِيَكَ اللهُ مِنْ عَفْوِهِ وَصَفْحِهِ، فَإِنَّكَ فَوْقَهُمْ، وَ وَالِي الاْمْرِ عَلَيْكَ فَوْقَكَ، وَاللهُ فَوْقَ مَنْ وَلاَّكَ! وَقَدِ اسْتَكْفَاكَ أَمْرَهُمْ، وَابْتَلاَكَ بِهِمْ⟫

Habituate your heart to mercy for the subjects and to affection and kindness for them. Do not stand over them like greedy beasts who feel it is enough to devour them, since they are of two kinds, either your brother in religion or one like you in creation. They will commit slips and encounter mistakes. They may act wrongly, wilfully or by neglect. So, extend to them your forgiveness and pardon, in the same way as you would like Allah to extend His forgiveness and pardon to you, because you are over them and your responsible Commander (Imam) is over you while Allah is over him who has appointed you. He (Allah) has sought you to manage their affairs and has tried you through them

You have drawn attention to the mercy of Allah by admonishing mercy for all mankind. Every person, no matter how great a ruler and king, is a slave of Allah and is completely in need of His mercy. Therefore, if a person sees that he is a ruler over another human being, he should remember that he is submissive before Allah. This thought of him will make him kind and sympathetic to those below him, and will draw the mercy of Allah towards him. He reminded Malik al-Ashtar that although he is a ruler, he is a human being like all other human beings.

Once Maulana Ali saw a blind fakir who was asking a question but no one was begging him. You were told that he was a Christian. He said to them, "You have taken so much advantage of him that he has become old and weak, and now you refuse to help him." From today, it should be spent from Bait-ul-Maal. Your action teaches the lesson of spices that both Muslims and non-Muslims are equal in the matter of justice. Social justice and religious equality arise from mercy, so mercy is an important duty on Muslims.

He said to Malik Ashrat that his rule is not an honor from Allah but a test and a test which shows what he himself thought of ruling during his caliphate. He said in his sermon: "If Allah had not promised the scholars that they would disobey the oppressor and support the oppressed, I would have thrown the reins of this caliphate on his shoulders, and you would have seen that this world is more worthless to me than the substance that flows from the nose of a goat." Here we see a resemblance to Plato's thinking when he said that a true philosopher is one who rules only for the sake of the people. He does not consider it an honor for himself, but an indispensable duty, and his main purpose is only to establish justice, because the establishment and restoration of any society can only be based on this one attribute.

We learn from your sayings that the government and powers work under the principle of welfare of the poor. If Allah has bestowed upon one of His servants the privilege of knowledge, and has given him the consciousness of justice, then his responsibility is increased. The more God's grace increases upon man, the greater his obligation to do favor to the creatures. In one of his sermons, he says, "Allah's grace does not increase upon His servant until Allah's right is great in his eyes."<!-- section 17 (id=3588, raw_sort=17): اللہ کے بارے میں خوش گمانی -->Let us now consider the part of Amir al-Mu'minin's letter in which he asked Malik al-Ashtar who he should appoint as his minister and adviser. He advised us to stay away from the miserly and the cowardly, saying, "Surely, stinginess, cowardice and greed arise from mistrust of Allaah." And this misconception arises from not understanding the Divine Fitrah, and the ignorance of the Fitrah arises from the lack of proper knowledge of the attributes of Allah. From this point of view, all human evils are associated with the deterioration of the intellect due to the weakness of faith. On the contrary, a strong faith produces a good sense of God, a strong intellect, and a thoughtful conception of the reality of God, and this concept highlights the divine attributes in it. One should not think that since these attributes are related to Allah, one should not try to acquire them. Rather, a person should make these qualities an example for himself and a way of life, and remove the defects of the soul. This does not mean that man is competing with the greatness of God, but that the goal is to try to become like God. And this spiritual development is achieved through the worship of Allah. In other words, a person should be generous because Allah is generous and he should be merciful because Allah is Merciful and Merciful. But at the same time, a person should also establish humility and devotion and believe that he can never develop in himself any quality that is worthy of the attributes of God!

All the attributes of Allah describe man's complete dependence and dependence on Allah, and the Oneness and Companionship of Allah. In this way, a positive and a non-positive relationship was established between Allah and His servant. Positive, in the case of Maulana Ali's saying that whoever does not show mercy to another, Allah does not have mercy on him, and according to the non-positive saying of Allah:

> ⟪quran 35:15⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلنَّاسُ أَنتُمُ ٱلْفُقَرَآءُ إِلَى ٱللَّهِۖ وَٱللَّهُ هُوَ ٱلْغَنِىُّ ٱلْحَمِيدُ ‎⟫
> *O mankind! it is you who stand in need of Allah, but Allah is Rich (Free of all wants and needs), Worthy of all praise.*
> O men, it is you who are in need of Allah, and Allah is All-sufficient, All-laudable.
> — **Quran 35:15 (inline widget)**

In this way, there is a synthesis between the two that man's good morals and virtues are a reflection of Allah's divine attributes, and his belief that he is in a position of non-existence before Allah's greatness.  He is the representative of Allah and His slave⟪ar:خلیفۃ اللہ و عبد اللہ⟫. His servitude keeps him within the limits of his servitude lest he should transgress and become a partner in the glory of Allah, and his representation reminds him that the consciousness of his servitude to Allah does not make him forget his obligation towards the creation of Allah which Allah has enjoined upon him. This balance of representation and slavery, or between Allah and His servants, is another example of keeping things in their proper place, and a means of creating harmony between moral practice and self-purification.<!-- section 18 (id=3590, raw_sort=18): شہر اور معاشرا -->Then in your letter, you mention the different sections of the society, armies, scribes, judiciary, officers, tax collectors, peasants, merchants, artisans, and destitutes, and describe their responsibilities. The advice you have given about them can be seen as practical justice. The ruler should fulfill the rights of all the people of these classes, knowing their duty to Allah. This is because Allah has established all these classes and has given them their fate and sustenance, and He has established the boundaries of all of them and has taken a pledge to abide by the Qur'an and Sunnah.

The ruler's obligation to society is part of his commitment to Allah, as he said:

> ⟪quran 13:19-20⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ أَفَمَن يَعْلَمُ أَنَّمَآ أُنزِلَ إِلَيْكَ مِن رَّبِّكَ ٱلْحَقُّ كَمَنْ هُوَ أَعْمَىٰٓ ۚ إِنَّمَا يَتَذَكَّرُ أُو۟لُوا۟ ٱلْأَلْبَبِ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ يُوفُونَ بِعَهْدِ ٱللَّهِ وَلَا يَنقُضُونَ ٱلْمِيثَقَ ‎⟫
> *Shall he then who knows that what has been revealed unto you (O Muhammad PBUH) from your Lord is the truth be like him who is blind? But it is only the men of understanding that pay heed. Those who fulfill the Covenant of Allah and break not the Mîthaq (bond, treaty, covenant);*
> he who knows that what has been revealed to you from your Lord is the truth is like him who is blind? Only those who fulfil the covenant of God and do not break it.
> — **Quran 13:19-20 (inline widget)**

And he said,

> ⟪quran 17:34⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَقْرَبُوا۟ مَالَ ٱلْيَتِيمِ إِلَّا بِٱلَّتِى هِىَ أَحْسَنُ حَتَّىٰ يَبْلُغَ أَشُدَّهُۥ ۚ وَأَوْفُوا۟ بِٱلْعَهْدِ ۖ إِنَّ ٱلْعَهْدَ كَانَ مَسْـُٔولًۭا ‎⟫
> *And come not near to the orphan's property except to improve it, until he attains the age of full strength. And fulfil (every) covenant. Verily! the covenant, will be questioned about.*
> And do not approach the property of the orphan except in the best manner, until he reaches maturity. And fulfil your promise; indeed the promise will be called into account.
> — **Quran 17:34 (inline widget)**

Then you advise the master to take the company of scholars and wise men so that they may bring prosperity to their government and increase in their land the welfare that those who came before them.  After that, we now mention each class separately and declare the ruler as the center of all those around whom they are all revolved. You say that the center is nothing but its circle that connects it, and the whole society, to God.

Then he first mentions the army and says that they are like a fortress to the people. For the selection of the Amir of the Army, he says, "The one who is most sincere to Allah, His Messenger and the Imam of the Time should be chosen, whose heart is pure and pure, who is forbearing, who is late in anger, who is quick to forgive, who is gentle with the weak, and who is hard with the strong." Who does not panic in intensity and which weakness cannot stop. If we look at it, we see all these qualities prominently in the personality and character of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The emphasis you have placed on compassion, gentleness and tolerance is noteworthy because these are qualities that are not usually used in any war, because they are fond of fighting and dying. But what is needed here is a brave battle that is fierce only with the enemies but also with its own people, as the Qur'an says:

> ⟪quran 48:29⟫
> ⟪ar:‏مُّحَمَّدٌۭ رَّسُولُ ٱللَّهِ ۚ وَٱلَّذِينَ مَعَهُۥٓ أَشِدَّآءُ عَلَى ٱلْكُفَّارِ رُحَمَآءُ بَيْنَهُمْ ۖ تَرَىٰهُمْ رُكَّعًۭا سُجَّدًۭا يَبْتَغُونَ فَضْلًۭا مِّنَ ٱللَّهِ وَرِضْوَنًۭا ۖ سِيمَاهُمْ فِى وُجُوهِهِم مِّنْ أَثَرِ ٱلسُّجُودِ ۚ ذَلِكَ مَثَلُهُمْ فِى ٱلتَّوْرَىٰةِ ۚ وَمَثَلُهُمْ فِى ٱلْإِنجِيلِ كَزَرْعٍ أَخْرَجَ شَطْـَٔهُۥ فَـَٔازَرَهُۥ فَٱسْتَغْلَظَ فَٱسْتَوَىٰ عَلَىٰ سُوقِهِۦ يُعْجِبُ ٱلزُّرَّاعَ لِيَغِيظَ بِهِمُ ٱلْكُفَّارَ ۗ وَعَدَ ٱللَّهُ ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ مِنْهُم مَّغْفِرَةًۭ وَأَجْرًا عَظِيمًۢا ‎⟫
> *Muhammad (PBUH) is the Messenger of Allah, and those who are with him are severe against disbelievers, and merciful among themselves. You see them bowing and falling down prostrate (in prayer), seeking Bounty from Allah and (His) Good Pleasure. The mark of them (i.e. of their Faith) is on their faces (foreheads) from the traces of (their) prostration (during prayers). This is their description in the Taurat (Torah). But their description in the Injeel (Gospel) is like a (sown) seed which sends forth its shoot, then makes it strong, it then becomes thick, and it stands straight on its stem, delighting the sowers that He may enrage the disbelievers with them. Allah has promised those among them who believe (i.e. all those who follow Islamic Monotheism, the religion of Prophet Muhammad PBUH till the Day of Resurrection) and do righteous good deeds, forgiveness and a mighty reward (i.e. Paradise).*
> Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah, and those who are with you are stern against the disbelievers, merciful to one another, so you will see them bowing down and prostrating, seeking Allah's bounty and His pleasure. Then he pulled out a needle, then strengthened it, then it became thick, then she erected on her chins, pleasing the farmers, so that Allah might provoke the disbelievers with them. Allah has promised forgiveness and a great reward to the believers and the doers of good.
> — **Quran 48:29 (inline widget)**

Then he explains the qualities of the judges and says that they should be such that they should not be confused by complicated matters, that they should not be irritated by constant complaints, that they should be as firm as a mountain in the matter of truth, that they should not be satisfied with superficial tactics, that they should be successful in the debate, that they should be in search of the truth, that they should be protected from praise and desires. Then you say that of course such people are rare. He also says that they should be paid generously so that they do not need money from people.

With regard to the wise men, he says that their honesty should be tested in order to hold offices, and there should be no bias in selecting them. And even after they have been installed in their place, their actions should be investigated, and they should be severely punished for any abuse of privilege.

Regarding the peasants who sow the land and who collect the revenue, they say, "You should be more concerned with cultivating the land than with the revenue, because if there is no cultivation, there will be no revenue, and whoever establishes a tax without inspecting the cultivation kills the people." He says that the destruction of the earth is due to the destruction of the people who live on it, and poverty comes upon them when the desire of the wise man to accumulate wealth dominates the souls of the wise, when they are in doubt about their own survival, and when they cannot benefit from the best examples. Doubting their own survival means that they think that they will live forever and will not be held accountable. Allaah says to them:

> ⟪quran 104:1-4⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَيْلٌۭ لِّكُلِّ هُمَزَةٍۢ لُّمَزَةٍ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِى جَمَعَ مَالًۭا وَعَدَّدَهُۥ ‎ ‏يَحْسَبُ أَنَّ مَالَهُۥٓ أَخْلَدَهُۥ ‎ ‏كَلَّا ۖ لَيُنۢبَذَنَّ فِى ٱلْحُطَمَةِ ‎⟫
> *Woe to every slanderer and backbiter. Who has gathered wealth and counted it, He thinks that his wealth will make him last forever! Nay! Verily, he will be thrown into the crushing Fire.*
> Woe to every backbiter and slanderer. He who hoardeth up wealth and counteth it, thinketh that his wealth will abide therein. Nay, but he will surely be thrown into the utter.
> — **Quran 104:1-4 (inline widget)**

When a person forgets that there is nothing left, he develops a desire to accumulate and instead of acquiring true spiritual treasures, he spends his life accumulating false material wealth and as a result, oppression is created.

Regarding the election of representatives, you say that you should not elect people who have demonstrated their morals to you, but rather look at their past, and look at the opinion of the public about them, and give the office only to those who have a reputation for trust.

Regarding the traders, he says that these are the people who benefit the society a lot, so they should be treated the best. These people are generally peace-loving and should be left to do their work, but the evils, hoarding, miserliness and deceit that arise in them should be stopped.

### Poor who need it the most:

Amir al-Mu'minin says about the poor, the disabled, the orphans and the elderly that these are the people who are in dire need of the ruler's justice, but they do not extend their hands to anyone.
