He said, "The ruler should take special care of these people if he wants Allah to forgive him on the Day of Resurrection." He should appoint a special officer who will take care of the needs of these people and present them to the ruler. Then you say, "This is a burden for the ruler, but Allah makes it easy for those who look forward to the Hereafter, and who exhort themselves to patience, and are certain in what Allah has promised them."

Here you have again linked the difficulty of this matter with spirituality, that if one looks beyond this world towards the Hereafter, even the most difficult task becomes easier. But those whose demand does not outpace the world will fall prey to negligence on the part of these poor. Because, from a worldly point of view, it is politically useless to help the poor, because there is no apparent benefit for the ruler in the expenditure of government welfare for these poor. But when this view is accompanied by a sense of Allah's omnipotent justice, abundant mercy, and the desire to attain the Hereafter through the help of these people, the task becomes easier, and the rulers of the time are engaged in sincere support to these people.

This approach transcends general generosity and charity. A person will bring the concept of helping the poor to a level of perfection, he will not be a victim of selfish desires, selfishness, intentional or unintentional negligence. And after developing this attribute, the next attribute described by Maulana Ali, patience, will be born instantaneously, because this act of his is not limited to his personal desires and efforts, but is accompanied by divine grace which comes from the roots of faith. As a result, such people believe in God's reward, His justice, and His promise of mercy, and the ruler's desire to help the poor and do justice to them becomes stronger. 

These morals of the reality of the Hereafter are hidden from the eyes of the worldly rulers, because of their hidden prejudices and outward evils. Such wrongdoers do not believe in the blessings of the Hereafter, nor in the punishments and punishments therein. They were called oppressors because they disobeyed the requirements of divine justice, and they denied the great attribute of mercy which is the essence of God's nature.<!-- section 19 (id=3591, raw_sort=19): نیت کی اہمیت -->The most important element of all the commands you have given is intention.  Even if man's process of establishing justice cannot be fulfilled due to the impermanence of this world, then his pure intention becomes the basis of his moral life and fills him with the taste of Allah's grace. If God's promise is true, and if man believes in this fact, then this belief has such an effect on the soul that it transforms a personal creation into a non-conditional need, and transforms a desirable attribute into an unconditional reality. This shows that morality is strengthened by spirituality, after which all the Shariah commandments become easy. After that, man establishes justice in order to be grateful for what he has received from Allah, not for what he will receive in the Hereafter. The Qur'an mentions the blessings of Paradise as if they had been given to the believers, and as if what is going to happen in the future has passed on them:

> ⟪quran 108:1-2⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّآ أَعْطَيْنَكَ ٱلْكَوْثَرَ ‎ ‏فَصَلِّ لِرَبِّكَ وَٱنْحَرْ ‎⟫
> *Verily, We have granted you (O Muhammad (Peace be upon him)) Al-Kauthar (a river in Paradise); Therefore turn in prayer to your Lord and sacrifice (to Him only).*
> indeed We have given you abundance, so perform the prayer to your Lord and sacrifice.
> — **Quran 108:1-2 (inline widget)**

Explaining this point, Maulana Ali says:

Surely, there is a group that worships Allah out of the desire for Paradise and this is commercial worship, one group worships out of fear of Hell and this is slave worship, and a group worships Allah out of gratitude, and this is the worship of the free. For this reason, he said in one place: ⟪ar-quote:یا الہی ما عبدتک من شوق جنتک ولا من خوف النارک بل وجدت مستحق لی العبادۃ فالعبدتک⟫ "O Allah, I do not worship You in the passion of Paradise, nor fear of those whom I worship, but I have found You worthy of worship, so I worship You."

A person is acquitted of the shortcomings of his actions through the sincerity of his intentions, and his action does not depend on the result but on the sincerity of his intention. It is not about establishing justice for any worldly purpose, but about establishing justice in order to fulfill the requirements of justice, because the justice of the just is part of his purpose.  Justice is not associated with Allah in the sense that He is the one who does justice, rather He is the One who is just, so He is just. And for this reason, a just person acts justly in order to be in accordance with the will of Allah, and not just to obey Allah's command, nor out of worldly greed. Allaah says (interpretation of the meaning):

> ⟪quran 92:17-21⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَسَيُجَنَّبُهَا ٱلْأَتْقَى ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِى يُؤْتِى مَالَهُۥ يَتَزَكَّىٰ ‎ ‏وَمَا لِأَحَدٍ عِندَهُۥ مِن نِّعْمَةٍۢ تُجْزَىٰٓ ‎ ‏إِلَّا ٱبْتِغَآءَ وَجْهِ رَبِّهِ ٱلْأَعْلَىٰ ‎ ‏وَلَسَوْفَ يَرْضَىٰ ‎⟫
> *And Al-Muttaqun (the pious and righteous - see V.2:2) will be far removed from it (Hell). He who spends his wealth for increase in self-purification, And have in his mind no favour from anyone for which a reward is expected in return, Except only the desire to seek the Countenance of his Lord, the Most High; He surely will be pleased (when he will enter Paradise).*
>And away from it is the God-fearing one who gives his wealth so that he may be purified; and no soul has any favour against it, but he who is recompensed only with the Countenance of his Lord, the Most High, and he shall soon be well-pleased.
> — **Quran 92:17-21 (inline widget)**

And that's ⟪ar:’ابرار‘⟫ the definition. All the scholars are unanimous that these verses were revealed in honor of Maulana Ali and his family when they fasted for three days and fed the bread of their house to the poor, the needy and the orphans:

> ⟪quran 76:8-9⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَيُطْعِمُونَ ٱلطَّعَامَ عَلَىٰ حُبِّهِۦ مِسْكِينًۭا وَيَتِيمًۭا وَأَسِيرًا ‎ ‏إِنَّمَا نُطْعِمُكُمْ لِوَجْهِ ٱللَّهِ لَا نُرِيدُ مِنكُمْ جَزَآءًۭ وَلَا شُكُورًا ‎⟫
> *And they give food, inspite of their love for it (or for the love of Him), to Miskin (poor), the orphan, and the captive, (Saying): "We feed you seeking Allah's Countenance only. We wish for no reward, nor thanks from you.*
> And they feed the needy, and the orphan, and the captive, out of love for Him. Whatever We feed you, it is only for the sake of Allah; it is not for us to take any retribution from you, nor to be grateful.
> — **Quran 76:8-9 (inline widget)**

The more a person's action is for the sake of Allah, and he will not be praised or blamed by anyone, and the action that is neither weakened by external difficulties nor strengthened by internal consequences, his action will be acceptable. This relationship between intention and action helps us to understand Ali's statement that his heart is in heaven while his body is acting in the world. It is worth noting here that worldly morals are strong or weak in the form of results, i.e., if a good result is obtained, a person continues to do so, and if he does not get it, he abandons it, but the action of the one who watches over the Hereafter is fulfilled by the sincerity of his intention. This does not mean that a person should not do a lot of deeds after doing good intentions, rather the argument of sincere intention is that no matter what the result is, he goes on doing good deeds and never gets tired or stops. Otherwise, an action that stops due to circumstances, or is reduced to a bookish extent, shows a lack of intention.  Pure intention requires that a person should strive relentlessly and relentlessly to achieve his intentions. 

A just man never despairs, and never abandons trying to establish justice. His purpose is not to establish justice in order to achieve any result, but rather his intention is the spiritual fulfillment of his justice, and he understands that his physical existence is linked to external circumstances and, ultimately, to God's pleasure. Yet, such a person does not get tired of not getting results, but his effort is as permanent as he is sure of the permanence of his blessings. His actions are strengthened by the attribute of divine justice.

Jesus Christ said, "When the principles of justice are thought of separately from spirituality, personal idealism arises, which is influenced by external consequences, and is therefore broken by the pressure of difficulties and despair."  But when spirituality is associated with justice, the indestructible attribute of divine justice supports it and gives it the power of fulfillment.  As much as man's principles are based on spiritual knowledge, he cannot be touched by despair and despair in the face of difficulties. We find an example of this in the biography of Amir al-Mu'minin himself, that when he came to the throne of the apparent caliphate, a storm of wars and rebellions arose one after another, due to which he could not promote all the principles and strategies that he wanted to do, but despite all these difficulties, he was never disappointed, disappointed, or depressed, nor did he do justice There was no shortage of effort and quest in establishing. And he used to say that no action is ordinary if piety is associated with it. That is, despair is separated from the pious person, because he is always conscious of the truth. This level of piety becomes a way out for him to get out of the injustices of this world, as Ali (a.s.) said: ⟪ar-quote:من یتق اللہ یجعل لہ مخرجا من الفتن وا نور من الظلم⟫ "Whoever fears Allah, Allah will make for him a way in trials and light in darkness."<!-- section 20 (id=3592, raw_sort=20): عبادت کی فضیلت -->Then we come to the point of your letter in which you describe what is the essence of all virtues, which is prayer. At the beginning of the letter, you advise that the ruler should perform the duties of prayer. Here he tells the owner that he should spend the best part of his time working for the sake of Allah after he has done all his administrative tasks, and that is an act of worship and dedication. Malik al-Ashtar has been specifically instructed to purify his religion through obligatory acts of worship and to purify his devotion. By purifying your religion, your purpose is to purify the substance of your relationship with Allah through worship, which is between them and their soul and Allah. Because the depth of this relationship is the hallmark of the quality of all human virtues.

He says, "Know that your every action depends on your worship." By worship here, you do not mean only the outward bowing and prostration, but the inner sincerity that is connected to this outward act and keeps it alive. The sincerity, intensity and fulfillment of this prayer achieve its purpose. He said, "Use your strength of night and day for the sake of Allah, and complete the deeds by which you draw near to Him, and do them without fatigue, and take your body to its limits." The most important word here is closeness, which one gets from the dedication that arises from the depths of the heart in the solitude of the darkest part of the night. That is, all outward actions are governed by the pure intention of man to surrender himself to Allah. If a person's inner life is overwhelmed by the light of prayer, then his rays also emerge in the outward life. For this reason, he asked Malik to devote the best part of his time to Allah. That is, every part of the ruler's time is for Allah, if the intention behind the action is good and if the people are protected as a result. At that time, a person will see that the fountains of obligatory and voluntary prayers will be spilled out and their effects will be on the outward actions of life. The hadith of the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings of Allaah be upon him) narrates this beautiful truth:

I do not love my servant as much as I love my servant through duty. My servant, through the Revelations, never ceases to draw near to me until I fall in love with Him. I am his hearing with which he hears, his sight with which he sees, his hand with which he grasps, and his feet with which he walks.

Seeing and acting through Allah means seeing things according to their reality and then acting according to Him. In the second sense, it is to do justice, i.e., to keep things in their proper place. It is important to note in this hadith that the prayers of the obligatory and the obligatory prayers are the cause of nearness to Allah, but the place of the act of the divine is through the acts of worship and not through the obligatory prayers. As Ali says, take your actions to the limits of your body. This showed that there was no benefit to mere careless and mechanical worship. He said, "The example of a person who prays without ijtihad is like a person who throws an arrow without a bow."

As mentioned earlier, in order to connect with Allah and become one with Him (Tawheed), pure integration of the self is required, and prayer is the place where the deep dimensions of the human soul are revealed, cultivated, and merged. Therefore, the fulfillment of prayer is not only with the tongue and the body, but with the whole of the soul and body. Allaah says (interpretation of the meaning):

> ⟪quran 24:36⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فِى بُيُوتٍ أَذِنَ ٱللَّهُ أَن تُرْفَعَ وَيُذْكَرَ فِيهَا ٱسْمُهُۥ يُسَبِّحُ لَهُۥ فِيهَا بِٱلْغُدُوِّ وَٱلْآصَالِ ‎⟫
> *In houses (mosques), which Allah has ordered to be raised (to be cleaned, and to be honoured), in them His Name is glorified in the mornings and in the afternoons or the evenings,*
> in houses which Allah has commanded to be venerated and His name to be remembered therein, glorifying Him in the mornings and evenings.
> — **Quran 24:36 (inline widget)**

Regarding nearness to Allah, Ali (a.s.) said: "Indeed, Allah has made remembrance for hearts, through which they may hear when they are deaf and see when they are blind." In every age, there have been special servants of Allah with whom Allah speaks in their thoughts, and speaks to them through the essence of their intellect. They spread the light of Allah in their hearts, hearings and sight and call people to the remembrance of the days of Allah.

The importance of dhikr is evident in your saying, through which the consciousness of the truth is created. By dhikr you mean not only the act of invoking a specific name of Allah, but also the constant awareness of Allah, which is the essence of all worship, meditation, and thought. The purpose is not just to remember Allah, or to chant His name, but to contemplate His divine realities through the outward and inward manifestations of His names. In another place, Maulana Ali says about dhikr:

Indeed, there are those who have adopted the remembrance of this world in such a way that neither trade nor economy diverts them from the remembrance of Allah. They spend the days of their lives in it. He exhorts people to be just, and he himself stands for justice. That is, they themselves show people how things are kept in their proper place and explain how things are kept in their proper place. Spirituality is not a separate thing from actions, but is a connection to the moral depths that ⟪ar:’الہ‘⟫ arise from the relationship, a relationship that is through worship in general and through remembrance in particular.  Just as it has been proved earlier that sincerity in intention is the main substance, it is now known that sincerity is the most important thing in prayer which takes the body to its limits. If the attribute of justice is in the essence of God, then the closer a person attains to Allah through prayer and remembrance, the more he will be just and will develop in himself positive abilities, spirituality, intellect and morals. Justice is both the cause of worship and its consequence. This made the connection between worship and justice clear. Justice teaches us to keep things in their proper place. Therefore, justice to Allah is to be fulfilled through prayer and remembrance, and justice towards oneself and people is the result of the closeness that comes from the worship of Allah, and from which all virtues are produced.

Amir al-Mu'minin (a.s.) has emphasized the apparent prayer and its origin (dhikr). Plato said that the highest knowledge ⟪ar:’خیر‘⟫ is knowledge because all good and right are born from it. If a person acquires all the knowledge of the world and does not acquire the knowledge of goodness, then he has not acquired any knowledge. He drew a comparison between virtue and the Sun and said that what the Sun does for sight, does the same for the intellect and existence.

Once, Zalib al-Yamani asked Ali, "O Ali! Have you seen the purpose of your sincerity? He said, "If I had not seen him, I would not have worshipped him." He asked, "How did you see him?" He replied, "He cannot be seen with the eyes of the eyes, but the heart sees him with the truth of faith." From this statement of yours we know that dhikr is very important because it is through it that the heart is pure and pure.  However, dhikr does not refer to the knowledge of outward forms, rather it is the knowledge of the Creator of these forms, which is described as the divine attribute in ⟪ar:’المصور‘⟫ Islam. But this mention cannot be expressed in words like other sciences. It requires tireless worship and hard work day and night. This is like a spark that is created by the hard work of friction, but once this candle is lit, it never goes out again and continues to nurture itself throughout its life.

The essence of justice in Amir al-Mu'minin's letter is that in order for any society to establish justice, it must understand these Islamic concepts not only from the intellect but also from the heart, because the heart is connected with the inner realities and only the heart can see them with the light of Allah. It is not possible without his kindness. The prophetic requirement of justice is that all the components of human life, worship, morality, action, should be connected in harmony with each other on the principle of monotheism. The world of ethics cannot be separated from the world of spirituality, because in Ali's view, true virtue is that which is original, strengthened, and directed towards the truth. Therefore, these requirements of justice in the soul can only be created through worship whose spirituality is through remembrance. Only this last analysis proves that it is the remembrance that establishes the standard of human virtues.<!-- section 21 (id=3602, raw_sort=21): ذکر اللہ -->Ali al-Hajwiri, the author of Kashf al-Mahjoob, writes about Maulana Ali (a.s.):

One of them was the cousin of Muhammad Mustafa (peace be upon him), who was drowned in the stormy sea of trials, and who was engulfed by the flames of love. who are the chiefs of Asfiyya and Auliya (Muqtada Auliya wa'l-Asfiyya). They have a grand and noble place in this path. He had complete mastery of all the realities of the higher world, so much so that Junaid said that 'Ali is our master in the knowledge of principles and principles (Shaykhna fi Usul wal Balaya).  Ali is the Imam of all intellectual and practical realms. Sufis interpret the knowledge of this path as a matter of principle, and recognize its practice as enduring calamities.

His tolerance of these calamities reminds us of the saying of Amir al-Mu'minin in which he said that he loves those with whom the ignorant feel alienated. The one thing that the Sufis love and feel alienated by the ignorant is worship, and in worship they are especially attentive to the Creator, from whom all other creatures are excluded. It is as if their worship is a kind of death during which they sacrifice their grandfather and all other occupations in the way of Allah's attention. They destroy themselves for the sake of the truth.

The word dhikr is very eloquent in its meaning and has no substitute for it in other languages. It is taken in the sense of remembrance, reflection, complaint, repetition, tasbih, recitation. It also has another meaning of remembrance, statement, praise, celebration, fame, greatness, honor, admonition, warning. Allah has also described the Qur'an as dhikr.

But the best definition of this is found in the dictionary of Raghib al-Isfahani, in which he writes that remembrance is the power by which a person preserves knowledge and knowledge. Although memory is taken in the sense of memory (the past), remembrance is in the sense of remembering (presenting). Dhikr is also referred to as the existence of something in the consciousness and speech of a person. That is why it is said that there are two types of dhikr. One is the mention of the heart, and the other is the mention of the tongue, and there are two more types of both. The dhikr on which there is a mistake, i.e., there is a period of this dhikr, and the other is the dhikr on which there is no mistake, i.e., it lasts forever. The remembrance of Allah is possible only through the presence of the heart.

The remembrance of Allah is the name of a consciousness that absorbs the divine being, but at the same time it is a process that works under a spiritual discipline. That is, the remembrance of Allah is both the purpose and the means of attaining the goal, the knowledge and the action towards this knowledge. Zikr is a system for Sufis and saints through which their hearts absorb what is in their intellect. In this way, they transform an abstract imaginary object into a concrete existence of spiritual realities.  If prayer is the basis of worship, then the remembrance of Allah is greater than that, as the Qur'an says:

> ⟪quran 29:45⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱتْلُ مَآ أُوحِىَ إِلَيْكَ مِنَ ٱلْكِتَبِ وَأَقِمِ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ ۖ إِنَّ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ تَنْهَىٰ عَنِ ٱلْفَحْشَآءِ وَٱلْمُنكَرِ ۗ وَلَذِكْرُ ٱللَّهِ أَكْبَرُ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ يَعْلَمُ مَا تَصْنَعُونَ ‎⟫
> *Recite (O Muhammad PBUH) what has been revealed to you of the Book (the Quran), and perform As-Salat (Iqamat&shy;as&shy;Salat). Verily, As-Salat (the prayer) prevents from Al-Fahsha' (i.e. great sins of every kind, unlawful sexual intercourse, etc.) and Al-Munkar (i.e. disbelief, polytheism, and every kind of evil wicked deed, etc.) and the remembering (praising, etc.) of (you by) Allah (in front of the angels) is greater indeed [than your remembering (praising, etc.) Allah in prayers, etc.]. And Allah knows what you do.*
> recite what has been revealed to you of the Book, and be steadfast in prayer. Indeed, prayer prevents indecency and evil, and the remembrance of Allah is greater; and Allah is Aware of what you do.
> — **Quran 29:45 (inline widget)**

There are numerous hadiths of the Prophet (peace and blessings of Allaah be upon him) that describe the virtue of the remembrance of Allah. Once he said to his companions, "Shall I not tell you what is the purest of your deeds?" And he holds the highest rank among you? What is more important than giving gold and silver? And is it better than fighting your enemies? The people said, "O Messenger of Allah! You tell us, of course. He said, "It is your constant remembrance of Allah." Similarly, Maulana Ali says, "Remember Allah continuously, for He enlightens the hearts, and He is the best form of worship." Imam Ja'far al-Sadiq (a.s.) said, "Our Shi'a are those who, when they are alone, often mention Allah."

---

### Remembrance of Allah Strengthens Hearts

Now let us return to the sermon of Amir al-Mu'minin in which he said that the remembrance of Allah is burning for the hearts. At the beginning of his sermon, he recited the following verses of the Qur'an:

> ⟪quran 24:35-37⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ ٱللَّهُ نُورُ ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ ۚ مَثَلُ نُورِهِۦ كَمِشْكَوٰةٍۢ فِيهَا مِصْبَاحٌ ۖ ٱلْمِصْبَاحُ فِى زُجَاجَةٍ ۖ ٱلزُّجَاجَةُ كَأَنَّهَا كَوْكَبٌۭ دُرِّىٌّۭ يُوقَدُ مِن شَجَرَةٍۢ مُّبَرَكَةٍۢ زَيْتُونَةٍۢ لَّا شَرْقِيَّةٍۢ وَلَا غَرْبِيَّةٍۢ يَكَادُ زَيْتُهَا يُضِىٓءُ وَلَوْ لَمْ تَمْسَسْهُ نَارٌۭ ۚ نُّورٌ عَلَىٰ نُورٍۢ ۗ يَهْدِى ٱللَّهُ لِنُورِهِۦ مَن يَشَآءُ ۚ وَيَضْرِبُ ٱللَّهُ ٱلْأَمْثَلَ لِلنَّاسِ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ بِكُلِّ شَىْءٍ عَلِيمٌۭ ‎ ‏فِى بُيُوتٍ أَذِنَ ٱللَّهُ أَن تُرْفَعَ وَيُذْكَرَ فِيهَا ٱسْمُهُۥ يُسَبِّحُ لَهُۥ فِيهَا بِٱلْغُدُوِّ وَٱلْآصَالِ ‎ ‏رِجَالٌۭ لَّا تُلْهِيهِمْ تِجَرَةٌۭ وَلَا بَيْعٌ عَن ذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ وَإِقَامِ ٱلصَّلَوٰةِ وَإِيتَآءِ ٱلزَّكَوٰةِ ۙ يَخَافُونَ يَوْمًۭا تَتَقَلَّبُ فِيهِ ٱلْقُلُوبُ وَٱلْأَبْصَرُ ‎⟫
> *Allah is the Light of the heavens and the earth. The parable of His Light is as (if there were) a niche and within it a lamp, the lamp is in glass, the glass as it were a brilliant star, lit from a blessed tree, an olive, neither of the east (i.e. neither it gets sun-rays only in the morning) nor of the west (i.e. nor it gets sun-rays only in the afternoon,  but it is exposed to the sun all day long), whose oil would almost glow forth (of itself), though no fire touched it. Light upon Light! Allah guides to His Light whom He wills. And Allah sets forth parables for mankind, and Allah is All-Knower of everything. In houses (mosques), which Allah has ordered to be raised (to be cleaned, and to be honoured), in them His Name is glorified in the mornings and in the afternoons or the evenings, Men whom neither trade nor sale diverts them from the Remembrance of Allah (with heart and tongue), nor from performing As&shy;Salat (Iqamat-as-Salat),  nor from giving the Zakat. They fear a Day when hearts and eyes will be overturned (from the horror of the torment of the Day of Resurrection).*
> Allah is the light of the heavens and the earth, the likeness of His light is like a lamp in a niche, a lamp in a glass candle, a candle like a star shining like a pearl, illuminated by a blessed olive tree, neither to the east nor to the west. He wills to guide His light, and Allah sets forth parables for mankind, and Allah knows all things in houses which Allah has commanded to be raised and His name to be remembered therein. They fear a Day whereon hearts and eyes will overturn.
> — **Quran 24:35-37 (inline widget)**

When he reached the point where men whom trade and goods do not neglect from the remembrance of Allah, he said:

Indeed, Allah has made the remembrance of Allah a polish for the hearts, with which they may hear when they are deaf, see when they are blind, and submit when they resist. In every age, there have been servants of Allah to whom Allah has spoken through the origin of their thoughts and their intellects. He spread the light of guidance through his hearing, sight and the light that rose in his heart, and called people to the days of remembrance of Allah. There is a certain group among them who prefer the remembrance of Allah to the remembrance of Allah in this world, so that trade and commerce do not distract them from the remembrance of Allah. They spend the days of their lives in this dhikr. They are alive as if they had gone to the Hereafter, and they are living in this world and living in the Hereafter.

The connection between the burning of hearts and this verse of light is clear.  The hidden light of the hearts is revealed by the remembrance of Allah. The light of the inside (consciousness) is highlighted⟪ar:نُور ⟪ar:علی نُور⟫ by the light of the outside (the remembrance of Allah). When the heart is illuminated by this light, it spreads its effect on all the other organs, and they too are illuminated by this light, which then ⟪ar:نُور⟫explains the meaning of the heart ⟪ar:علی نُور⟫. Burn means to be cleansed, to be revealed, to be brought into light. Allaah says in the Qur'an:

> ⟪quran 92:1-2⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلَّيْلِ إِذَا يَغْشَىٰ ‎ ‏وَٱلنَّهَارِ إِذَا تَجَلَّىٰ ‎⟫
> *By the night as it envelops; And by the day as it appears in brightness;*
> by the night when it envelops, and by the day when it brightens.
> — **Quran 92:1-2 (inline widget)**

In this verse, Allaah swears by the night when it is overwhelmed. That is, it did not exist before and now it has appeared. And he swears by the day when it is bright. That is, it didn't exist before, and then it appeared.  In another place he says:

> ⟪quran 91:3⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلنَّهَارِ إِذَا جَلَّىٰهَا ‎⟫
> *And by the day as it shows up (the sun's) brightness;*
> And by the day when it illuminates it,
> — **Quran 91:3 (inline widget)**

That is, through the remembrance of Allah, the consciousness within the heart is awakened and manifested in the form of action. The role of the heart is worth considering here. On the one hand, he is receiving the divine light through the remembrance of Allah and reflecting it on all the other organs, on the other hand, the remembrance of Allah awakens the hidden consciousness in his depths, which reveals the truths to him. Maulana Ali ⟪ar:’دفائن العقول‘⟫ explained about this hidden consciousness.  So it became clear that the real purpose of dhikr is the purification of the heart, which is the Amir al-Badan and the center of true insight.

Allaah says (interpretation of the meaning):

> ⟪quran 7:179⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَقَدْ ذَرَأْنَا لِجَهَنَّمَ كَثِيرًۭا مِّنَ ٱلْجِنِّ وَٱلْإِنسِ ۖ لَهُمْ قُلُوبٌۭ لَّا يَفْقَهُونَ بِهَا وَلَهُمْ أَعْيُنٌۭ لَّا يُبْصِرُونَ بِهَا وَلَهُمْ آذَانٌۭ لَّا يَسْمَعُونَ بِهَآ ۚ أُو۟لَٓئِكَ كَٱلْأَنْعَمِ بَلْ هُمْ أَضَلُّ ۚ أُو۟لَٓئِكَ هُمُ ٱلْغَفِلُونَ ‎⟫
> *And surely, We have created many of the jinns and mankind for Hell.&nbsp;They have hearts wherewith they understand not, they have eyes wherewith they see not, and they have ears wherewith they hear not (the truth). They are like cattle, nay even more astray; those! They are the heedless ones.*
> And We have created for Hell many of the jinn and men. They have hearts with which they do not understand, eyes with which they do not see, and ears with which they do not hear. They are like cattle; nay, they are further astray. It is they who are the heedless.
> — **Quran 7:179 (inline widget)**

In this, Allah has used the word "heedless". The word "ignorant" is the opposite of dhikr, which means to remember.  And the next verse describes the mystical practice of dhikr:

> ⟪quran 7:180⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلِلَّهِ ٱلْأَسْمَآءُ ٱلْحُسْنَىٰ فَٱدْعُوهُ بِهَا ۖ وَذَرُوا۟ ٱلَّذِينَ يُلْحِدُونَ فِىٓ أَسْمَٓئِهِۦ ۚ سَيُجْزَوْنَ مَا كَانُوا۟ يَعْمَلُونَ ‎⟫
> *And (all) the Most Beautiful Names belong to Allah, so call on Him by them, and leave the company of those who belie or deny (or utter impious speech against) His Names. They will be requited for what they used to do.*
> And all the best names belong to Allah, so invoke Him by them, and leave those who blaspheme the names of Allah, lest they be recompensed for what they used to do.
> — **Quran 7:180 (inline widget)**

In the following verses, the relationship between remembrance and the heart becomes very clear:

> ⟪quran 13:28⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَتَطْمَىِٕنُّ قُلُوبُهُم بِذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ ۗ أَلَا بِذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ تَطْمَىِٕنُّ ٱلْقُلُوبُ ‎⟫
> *Those who believe (in the Oneness of Allah - Islamic Monotheism), and whose hearts find rest in the remembrance of Allah, Verily, in the remembrance of Allah do hearts find rest.*
> those who believe and whose hearts find solace in the remembrance of Allah. Hearts are comforted by the remembrance of Allah
> — **Quran 13:28 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 50:37⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّ فِى ذَلِكَ لَذِكْرَىٰ لِمَن كَانَ لَهُۥ قَلْبٌ أَوْ أَلْقَى ٱلسَّمْعَ وَهُوَ شَهِيدٌۭ ‎⟫
> *Verily, therein is indeed a reminder for him who has a heart or gives ear while he is heedful.*
> surely in that is a lesson for him who possesses a heart, or he is attentive, but he listens attentively.
> — **Quran 50:37 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 8:2⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّمَا ٱلْمُؤْمِنُونَ ٱلَّذِينَ إِذَا ذُكِرَ ٱللَّهُ وَجِلَتْ قُلُوبُهُمْ وَإِذَا تُلِيَتْ عَلَيْهِمْ آيَتُهُۥ زَادَتْهُمْ إِيمَنًۭا وَعَلَىٰ رَبِّهِمْ يَتَوَكَّلُونَ ‎⟫
> *The believers are only those who, when Allah is mentioned, feel a fear in their hearts and when His Verses (this Quran) are recited unto them, they (i.e. the Verses) increase their Faith; and they put their trust in their Lord (Alone);*
> the believers are only those whose hearts are filled with awe when Allah is mentioned, and when His verses are recited to them, their faith increases, and in their Lord they rely.
> — **Quran 8:2 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 39:22⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَفَمَن شَرَحَ ٱللَّهُ صَدْرَهُۥ لِلْإِسْلَمِ فَهُوَ عَلَىٰ نُورٍۢ مِّن رَّبِّهِۦ ۚ فَوَيْلٌۭ لِّلْقَسِيَةِ قُلُوبُهُم مِّن ذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ أُو۟لَٓئِكَ فِى ضَلَلٍۢ مُّبِينٍ ‎⟫
> *Is he whose breast Allah has opened to Islam, so that he is in light from His Lord (as he who is non-Muslim)? So, woe to those whose hearts are hardened against remembrance of Allah! They are in plain error!*
> is he whose breast Allah has opened up to Islam, so that he is in a light from his Lord? Woe to those whose hearts are not affected by the remembrance of Allah. Those are in manifest error.
> — **Quran 39:22 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 39:23⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱللَّهُ نَزَّلَ أَحْسَنَ ٱلْحَدِيثِ كِتَبًۭا مُّتَشَبِهًۭا مَّثَانِىَ تَقْشَعِرُّ مِنْهُ جُلُودُ ٱلَّذِينَ يَخْشَوْنَ رَبَّهُمْ ثُمَّ تَلِينُ جُلُودُهُمْ وَقُلُوبُهُمْ إِلَىٰ ذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ ذَلِكَ هُدَى ٱللَّهِ يَهْدِى بِهِۦ مَن يَشَآءُ ۚ وَمَن يُضْلِلِ ٱللَّهُ فَمَا لَهُۥ مِنْ هَادٍ ‎⟫
> *Allah has sent down the best statement, a Book (this Quran), its parts resembling each other in goodness and truth, oft-repeated.&nbsp;The skins of those who fear their Lord shiver from it (when they recite it or hear it). Then their skin and their heart soften to the remembrance of Allah. That is the guidance of Allah. He Guides therewith whom He pleases and whomever Allah sends astray, for him there is no guide.*
> is Allah's best discourse, the Book, which is continuous, so that the mutually repetitive (its verses) are repeated, so that the goosebumps of those who fear Allah stand up, then their skins soften and their hearts turn to the remembrance of Allah. No
> — **Quran 39:23 (inline widget)**

These verses show that the remembrance of Allah is closely related to the heart, which makes consciousness a reality. This heart needs to be enriched with the remembrance of Allah. The Messenger of Allah (s.a.w.a.) said: "For everything there is a polish." The remembrance of the heart is the remembrance of Allah. In this hadith, you are referring to a systematic process of action along with consciousness which brings us back to your hadith that at least worship Allah as He sees you. On the one hand, it can be used for purification of thoughts, contemplation, and on the other hand, it can be used for regular actions, which ⟪ar:تسبیح⟫are different forms such as glorification, ⟪ar:تمجید⟫magnification, ⟪ar:تحمید⟫ praise, ⟪ar:تقدیس⟫sanctification, ⟪ar:تحلیل⟫declaration of the divine unity, or remembrance of Allah. They remove the rust of forgetfulness from the hearts.  The Messenger of Allah (s.a.w.s.) has described such people as the people of remembrance. He said, "There are angels of Allaah who travel on the streets in search of the people of remembrance, and when they meet them, they say to one another, 'Come to that which you desire.'"

If we now consider that ⟪ar:بصیرت⟫which the heart sees through the remembrance of Allah, and that which is purified by the remembrance of Allah and is revived by faith. Maulana Ali says that this insight is obtained through inspiration and this insight is no less than the sight of Allah Himself. In another place, he calls the pure heart the place of seeing Allah and says, "Whoever purifies his heart, sees Allah." The connection between purity of heart and remembrance of Allah is evident in your saying, "Where are those whose deeds are purely for the sake of Allah, and who purify their hearts with the remembrance of Allah so that it becomes a place of resting for Allah?" His statement is in line with the hadith in which the Prophet (s) said, "Allah says, 'My servant will not stop getting close to Me through Nawafil until I love him.'" And when I love him, I become his hearing with which he hears, his sight with which he sees, his hands with which he holds, and his feet with which he walks.  That is, human feelings and actions are integrated into the realm of divine reality, as a result of which the heart gains spiritual insight. When such a point is reached, the heart, which is the center of consciousness, rises above the realm of physicality, and its inner essence (its head) becomes associated with the truth, and this essence begins to see as Allah sees, and finally sees Allah Himself.

Abu Talib bin Makki (a Sufi) writes that if it is true that Allah enters into human feelings through human actions, then the highest level of spiritual consciousness would be that the vision of Allah is not the sight of Allah, but the sight of Allah becomes the sight of Allah, which is through the heart. Maulana Ali explains this philosophy and says, " ⟪ar-quote:أعرف اللہ با اللہ⟫Acquire the knowledge of Allah through Allah." In this last analysis, Allah is the One who sees and is seen, as Allaah says (interpretation of the meaning):

> ⟪quran 85:3⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَشَاهِدٍۢ وَمَشْهُودٍۢ ‎⟫
> *And by the witnessing day (i.e. Friday), and by the witnessed day [i.e. the day of 'Arafat (Hajj) the ninth of Dhul-Hîjjah];*
> And by the Day that is witnessed and by Him to whom they appear.
> — **Quran 85:3 (inline widget)**

What is seen is the inner head of human consciousness, and what is seen is the divine reality. In other words, a person's deep faith makes Allah present everywhere and at all times, as Maulana Ali said in his sermon: "By Your greatness which fills everything, by Your names which are the foundation of everything, by Your knowledge which surrounds everything, by the light of Your face, by which every thing is found." The object has been illuminated.

Nothing can survive without its foundation. The name of Allah, or the combination of His names, provides that basis. That is, to see things correctly is to see the divine attributes which are real and objects are the physical reflection of these names and the manifestations of these names, and self-disclosures.  When the heart is purified by the remembrance of Allah, it finds Allah everywhere. The existence of Allah in everything is mentioned in two places in the Qur'an, one from the point of view of Allah and the other from the point of view of man:

> ⟪quran 2:115⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلِلَّهِ ٱلْمَشْرِقُ وَٱلْمَغْرِبُ ۚ فَأَيْنَمَا تُوَلُّوا۟ فَثَمَّ وَجْهُ ٱللَّهِ ۚ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ وَسِعٌ عَلِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *And to Allah belong the east and the west, so wherever you turn yourselves or your faces there is the Face of Allah (and He is High above, over His Throne). Surely! Allah is All-Sufficient for His creatures' needs, All-Knowing.*
To God belong > the East and the West. Whichever way you turn, there is the Face of God. God is All-embracing, All-knowing.
> — **Quran 2:115 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 41:53⟫
> ⟪ar:‏سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَتِنَا فِى ٱلأٓفَاقِ وَفِىٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ حَتَّىٰ يَتَبَيَّنَ لَهُمْ أَنَّهُ ٱلْحَقُّ ۗ أَوَلَمْ يَكْفِ بِرَبِّكَ أَنَّهُۥ عَلَىٰ كُلِّ شَىْءٍۢ شَهِيدٌ ‎⟫
> *&nbsp;We will show them Our Signs in the universe, and in their ownselves, until it becomes manifest to them that this (the Quran) is the truth. Is it not sufficient in regard to your Lord that He is a Witness over all things?*
> We will show them Our signs in the world and in their own souls until it becomes clear to them that it is the truth. Is it not sufficient that their Lord is a witness over all things?
> — **Quran 41:53 (inline widget)**

The heart, which has been purified by the remembrance of Allah, can see these signs everywhere and in everything, but such a vision does not mean that Allah has been reduced to human sensible phenomena. Maulana Ali said, "Allah is in everything but not in terms of proximity, and He is separate from everything but not in terms of difference." With-ness in the objects of Allah is not due to the proximity of Allah to the objects, nor is it due to the diminution of the divine. Allah is infinitely nearer to us and we are infinitely farther away from Him, as He said:

> ⟪quran 50:16⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَقَدْ خَلَقْنَا ٱلْإِنسَنَ وَنَعْلَمُ مَا تُوَسْوِسُ بِهِۦ نَفْسُهُۥ ۖ وَنَحْنُ أَقْرَبُ إِلَيْهِ مِنْ حَبْلِ ٱلْوَرِيدِ ‎⟫
> *And indeed We have created man, and We know what his ownself whispers to him. And We are nearer to him than his jugular vein (by Our Knowledge).*
> And indeed We have created man, and We know what he whispers in his soul, and We are nearer to him than his jugular vein.
> — **Quran 50:16 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 112:4⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَمْ يَكُن لَّهُۥ كُفُوًا أَحَدٌۢ ‎⟫
> *"And there is none co-equal or comparable unto Him." *
> and there is none equal to Him.
> — **Quran 112:4 (inline widget)**

Nothing can remain separate from Allah, but still it has no connection with Allah. All the objects in its existence are both entered and exited at the same time. His being with everything and in everything does not diminish his divinity, and his separation from all things does not remove him from them. As Maulana Ali said, Allah is one, but not in terms of number but in the sense that He has no equal.  What is unique cannot be counted. Saying that Allah is counted is polytheism. Maulana Ali makes it clear that no existence is possible without its existence. He is the only existence and everything else is deception. The radical concept of oneness, which excludes all otherness, in fact states that every creation except Allah is a false God, because they are also apparently one, standing in opposition to the Oneness and Oneness of Allah.

All praise is due to Allah, who is present in the hidden essence of things and whose essence is manifest from the existence of the creatures. The eye that sees cannot bear it, so the eye that does not see it cannot deny its reality, nor can the heart that acknowledges its reality see it. It is the height of the height that no object is higher than it, but it is also so close that no object is nearer than it. Allah has not made the intellect capable of appreciating its attributes, but He has not kept them away from His knowledge.

He says that on the one hand, we cannot even appreciate its attributes, but on the other hand, it is possible to gain knowledge about it.  How is this contradiction possible? Through this paradox we come to another aspect of dhikr which is to remember and recognize. In other words, man is combining the components of knowledge that already exist in his consciousness, but he has forgotten them. Man recognizes what he forgot and therefore knows it again. This does not mean that knowledge is fragmented and we have to put them together to form a picture. Rather, it is like waking up again and becoming enlightened, after the clouds of congenital forgetfulness have been removed.

Maulana Ali in his first sermon says, " ⟪ar-quote:اول الدین معرفتہ⟫(The first of religion is its knowledge)." The first means the former, which can be taken in the sense of the beginning, the foundation. The meaning of knowledge is not only to acquire knowledge, but also to recognize. This shows that Allah has already placed the knowledge of the truth in the consciousness of man. Man recognises this knowledge through the remembrance of Allah and acknowledges the knowledge which he already knew and forgot.  In the same sermon, he says:

⟪ar-quote:فَبَعَثَ فِيهمْ رُسُلَهُ، وَوَاتَرَ إِلَيْهِمْ أَنْبِياءَهُ، لِيَسْتَأْدُوهُمْ مِيثَاقَ فِطْرَتِهِ، وَيُذَكِّرُوهُمْ مَنْسِيَّ نِعْمَتِهِ، وَيَحْتَجُّوا عَلَيْهِمْ بَالتَّبْلِيغِ، وَيُثِيرُوا لَهُمْ دَفَائِنَ الْعُقُولِ، وَيُرُوهُمْ آيَاتِ الْمَقْدِرَةِ⟫ 

"Allah has sent Messengers from among them to take a pledge from them, and to remind them of the blessings which they have forgotten, and to revive them by preaching, and to bring forth for them the hidden treasures of intellect, and to show them the signs of Allah."

These buried treasures are the knowledge that Allaah has placed in the depths of His consciousness and which Allaah testified to at the time of His creation, as He says (interpretation of the meaning):

> ⟪quran 7:172⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَإِذْ أَخَذَ رَبُّكَ مِنۢ بَنِىٓ آدَمَ مِن ظُهُورِهِمْ ذُرِّيَّتَهُمْ وَأَشْهَدَهُمْ عَلَىٰٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ ۖ قَالُوا۟ بَلَىٰ ۛ شَهِدْنَآ ۛ أَن تَقُولُوا۟ يَوْمَ ٱلْقِيَمَةِ إِنَّا كُنَّا عَنْ هَذَا غَفِلِينَ ‎⟫
> *And (remember) when your Lord brought forth from the Children of Adam, from their loins, their seed (or from Adam's loin his offspring) and made them testify as to themselves (saying): "Am I not your Lord?" They said: "Yes! We testify," lest you should say on the Day of Resurrection: "Verily, we have been unaware of this." *
> And when your Lord brought forth from the Children of Adam from their loins, their offspring, and made them testify as to themselves, I am not your Lord, they said, Yes, we testify. Lest you should say on the Day of Resurrection, We were not aware of this.
> — **Quran 7:172 (inline widget)**

These divine realities can also be understood in the sense of the Divine Spirit that Allah breathed into Adam

> ⟪quran 32:9⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ثُمَّ سَوَّىٰهُ وَنَفَخَ فِيهِ مِن رُّوحِهِۦ ۖ وَجَعَلَ لَكُمُ ٱلسَّمْعَ وَٱلْأَبْصَرَ وَٱلْأَفْـِٔدَةَ ۚ قَلِيلًۭا مَّا تَشْكُرُونَ ‎⟫
> *Then He fashioned him in due proportion, and breathed into him the soul (created by Allah for that person), and He gave you hearing (ears), sight (eyes) and hearts. Little is the thanks you give!*
> Then He fashioned him and breathed into him of His spirit, and gave you hearing and sight and hearts. Little thanks do you give!
> — **Quran 32:9 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 2:31⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَعَلَّمَ آدَمَ ٱلْأَسْمَآءَ كُلَّهَا ثُمَّ عَرَضَهُمْ عَلَى ٱلْمَلَٓئِكَةِ فَقَالَ أَنۢبِـُٔونِى بِأَسْمَآءِ هَٓؤُلَآءِ إِن كُنتُمْ صَدِقِينَ ‎⟫
> *And He taught Adam all the names (of everything) , then He showed them to the angels and said, "Tell Me the names of these if you are truthful." *
> And Allah taught Adam all the names, then He presented them to the angels, and said, Tell Me the names of these, if you are truthful.
> — **Quran 2:31 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 30:30⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَأَقِمْ وَجْهَكَ لِلدِّينِ حَنِيفًۭا ۚ فِطْرَتَ ٱللَّهِ ٱلَّتِى فَطَرَ ٱلنَّاسَ عَلَيْهَا ۚ لَا تَبْدِيلَ لِخَلْقِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ ذَلِكَ ٱلدِّينُ ٱلْقَيِّمُ وَلَكِنَّ أَكْثَرَ ٱلنَّاسِ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫
> *So set you (O Muhammad PBUH) your face towards the religion of pure Islamic Monotheism Hanifa (worship none but Allah Alone) Allah's Fitrah (i.e. Allah's Islamic Monotheism), with which He has created mankind. No change let there be in Khalq&shy;illah (i.e. the Religion of Allah Islamic Monotheism), that is the straight religion, but most of men know not. [Tafsir At&shy;Tabarî, Vol 21, Page 41]*
> So set your face upright to the religion on a certain side, according to what Allah has bestowed upon which He has created mankind. There is no alteration of the creation of Allah. This is the right religion, but most of the people do not know.
> — **Quran 30:30 (inline widget)**

This shows that the knowledge of Allah has been placed in the true nature of man, which Allah took from him at the time of creation, which has been mentioned in the previous verse. Imam al-Baqir (a.s.) was asked about the nature of Allah, which means that Allah created the creatures according to the limits of Tawheed (there is no god but Allah) and he testified that Allah is our Lord. This shows that the knowledge of God is the explanation of human nature. That is why, as Maulana Ali said, the knowledge of Allah cannot be hidden from the human intellect.

But although this knowledge has been kept eternal in the human intellect, it has been neglected, which is the antithesis of the remembrance of Allah. This mistake cannot be remedied by any degree of external knowledge. Only when the awareness of remembrance and inner consciousness boils out of the heart and connects with external revelation does this divine knowledge be revealed to the heart and intellect. The treasures of knowledge that were buried in his intellect.

Maulana Ali says that praise is for Allah who is known without seeing. The contradiction of this sentence is further exacerbated by your statement that through objects the Creator appears to the intellect and through objects he is hidden from the eyes. Here is a mention of the veil that was born out of the act of creation. In a way, all creatures are themselves ⟪ar:’حجاب‘⟫ because they are hiding the divine revelations within themselves, and on the other hand, they are bearing witness to the existence of their Creator as their own beings. That is why you say, ⟪ar-quote:لا تحجبہ الحجب⟫ "(Hijab cannot hide it)." The hijab is compelled to reveal its observer because it reveals its own existence to the hijab. And the Master of the Universe says, " ⟪ar-quote:لو کشف الغطاء ما ازدت یقینا!⟫ But it can be seen by the heart which has been purified by the remembrance of Allah and which can see now after being blind."  Then he adds to this contradiction by saying: "The veil between Him and His creation is their own creation, so that there can be a distinction between the Creator and the Creator, the finite and the infinite, and between the Lord and the Creator."

All these creatures, or all the veils that have been created by creation, are examples of the divine attribute of Al-Zahir in that they are apparent, seen, clear and visible. That is, they are expressing the divine reality of ⟪ar:’خالق‘⟫ their existence. That is, Allah is manifesting a part of His hidden treasures as a manifest creation. It is showing the 'outward' side of the world ⟪ar:’الظاہر‘⟫ , and at the same time hiding the inner mystery of Allah ⟪ar:’الباطن‘⟫ in this expression. Therefore, the hijab of the creature is in fact the manifestation of the Creator. So who are these outward hijabs hiding? The Monotheism of Allah! Because this is ⟪ar:’الحق‘⟫ the basis of their essence and essence. And as mentioned earlier, the divine attributes of Allah are the basis of all creation. This proves that the basis of everything is another single truth. The essence of creation is in fact the divine attributes of the Truth.  To associate a creature with Allah is to associate shirk with Him. Therefore, the sight of the Divine Oneness protects us from this shirk. That is why there should always be a distinction between the Creator and the creature, the finite and the infinite, and between the Lord and the Merciful.

The veil of creation protects nature from pantheism, and from reducing the infinite divinity of Allah to the limited forms of man. Likewise, Tanzih (purifying Allah from all attributes) and Tasbeeh (affirmation of natural attributes) are also hijabs, except that they are seen in the light of one another. These transcendence and immanence are veils as long as these two opposing views are seen in the spiritual vision of ⟪ar:’توحید‘⟫ the creature (the manifestation of the manifest) and the non-creature (above all manifestations), in the light of which the two reveal each other. In the same way, unilaterally emphasizing the attribute of Allah's manifestation makes it a veil, because it conceals from us the attribute of Allah's inner self. And in the same way, insisting only on the attribute of His inner self becomes an invisible veil and makes us unable to see the 'appearance' of Allah, which is in the bosom of His universe.  In other words, hijabs are not only created because of creation, but also because of the weakness and limitations of human concepts, and the limitations of the manifestation of divine attributes in them. For this reason, it becomes necessary to deny the attributes of Allah. And through this negation, consciousness is able to understand the divinity and begins to see beyond the veil that it cannot hide.

When Abu Sa'd al-Kharz (a Sufi) was asked, "How did you know God?" So they answered by observing the fact that he connected⟪ar:جَمعُہُ الضِّدَّین⟫ the opposites to each other. Then he recited this verse:

> ⟪quran 57:3⟫
> ⟪ar:‏هُوَ ٱلْأَوَّلُ وَٱلْآخِرُ وَٱلظَّهِرُ وَٱلْبَاطِنُ ۖ وَهُوَ بِكُلِّ شَىْءٍ عَلِيمٌ ‎⟫
> *He is the First (nothing is before Him) and the Last (nothing is after Him), the Most High (nothing is above Him) and the Most Near (nothing is nearer than Him). And He is the All-Knower of every thing.*
> He is the First and the Last, the Outward and the Inward, and He has knowledge of all things.
> — **Quran 57:3 (inline widget)**

Spiritual inspiration enables a person to see seemingly different objects as one object in the light of monotheism. At this deep level of consciousness, the process of reconstruction begins and from it begins the knowledge of the Truth and the heart begins to see Allah through the sight of the truth of faith. Only the facts can be magnificent! Truths that are hidden in the depths of faith. Only the heart which has received the remembrance of Allah can see and understand these facts. Facts that can justify the reality of God.<!-- section 22 (id=3603, raw_sort=22): ذکر اللہ عبادت کی معراج ہے -->Allaah says (interpretation of the meaning):

> ⟪quran 76:25⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱذْكُرِ ٱسْمَ رَبِّكَ بُكْرَةًۭ وَأَصِيلًۭا ‎⟫
> *And remember the Name of your Lord every morning and afternoon [i.e. offering of the Morning (Fajr), Zuhr, and 'Asr prayers].*
> and remember the name of your Lord morning and evening.
> — **Quran 76:25 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 73:8⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱذْكُرِ ٱسْمَ رَبِّكَ وَتَبَتَّلْ إِلَيْهِ تَبْتِيلًۭا ‎⟫
> *And remember the Name of your Lord and devote yourself to Him with a complete devotion.*
> And pronounce the name of your Lord and devote yourselves to Him.
> — **Quran 73:8 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 33:41⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ ٱذْكُرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ ذِكْرًۭا كَثِيرًۭا ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Remember Allah with much remembrance.*
> O you who believe! Remember Allah with much remembrance.
> — **Quran 33:41 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 7:55⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱدْعُوا۟ رَبَّكُمْ تَضَرُّعًۭا وَخُفْيَةً ۚ إِنَّهُۥ لَا يُحِبُّ ٱلْمُعْتَدِينَ ‎⟫
> *Invoke your Lord with humility and in secret.&nbsp;He likes not the aggressors.*
> Pray to your Lord in humility and in secret. He does not love the transgressors.
> — **Quran 7:55 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 7:205⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱذْكُر رَّبَّكَ فِى نَفْسِكَ تَضَرُّعًۭا وَخِيفَةًۭ وَدُونَ ٱلْجَهْرِ مِنَ ٱلْقَوْلِ بِٱلْغُدُوِّ وَٱلْآصَالِ وَلَا تَكُن مِّنَ ٱلْغَفِلِينَ ‎⟫
> *And remember your Lord by your tongue and within yourself, humbly and with fear without loudness in words in the mornings, and in the afternoons and be not of those who are neglectful.*
> And remember your Lord in your heart, humble and fearful. And do not be of the loud voice, morning and evening, and do not be of the heedless.
> — **Quran 7:205 (inline widget)**

All these verses tell us how to remember Allah in your own soul, in humility, in fear, in solitude, in a low voice. But the most important thing is to remember it frequently. The intensity and frequency of the remembrance of the Prophet (s) and Maulana Ali has been mentioned in Surah Al-Muzammil:

> ⟪quran 73:20⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ إِنَّ رَبَّكَ يَعْلَمُ أَنَّكَ تَقُومُ أَدْنَىٰ مِن ثُلُثَىِ ٱلَّيْلِ وَنِصْفَهُۥ وَثُلُثَهُۥ وَطَآئِفَةٌۭ مِّنَ ٱلَّذِينَ مَعَكَ ۚ وَٱللَّهُ يُقَدِّرُ ٱلَّيْلَ وَٱلنَّهَارَ ۚ عَلِمَ أَن لَّن تُحْصُوهُ فَتَابَ عَلَيْكُمْ ۖ فَٱقْرَءُوا۟ مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ ٱلْقُرْآنِ ۚ عَلِمَ أَن سَيَكُونُ مِنكُم مَّرْضَىٰ ۙ وَآخَرُونَ يَضْرِبُونَ فِى ٱلْأَرْضِ يَبْتَغُونَ مِن فَضْلِ ٱللَّهِ ۙ وَآخَرُونَ يُقَتِلُونَ فِى سَبِيلِ ٱللَّهِ ۖ فَٱقْرَءُوا۟ مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنْهُ ۚ وَأَقِيمُوا۟ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ وَآتُوا۟ ٱلزَّكَوٰةَ وَأَقْرِضُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ قَرْضًا حَسَنًۭا ۚ وَمَا تُقَدِّمُوا۟ لِأَنفُسِكُم مِّنْ خَيْرٍۢ تَجِدُوهُ عِندَ ٱللَّهِ هُوَ خَيْرًۭا وَأَعْظَمَ أَجْرًۭا ۚ وَٱسْتَغْفِرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ ۖ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۢ ‎⟫
> *Verily, your Lord knows that you do stand (to pray at night) a little less than two-thirds of the night, or half the night, or a third of the night, and so do a party of those with you, And Allah measures the night and the day. He knows that you are unable to pray the whole night, so He has turned to you (in mercy). So, recite you of the Quran as much as may be easy for you. He knows that there will be some among you sick, others travelling through the land, seeking of Allah's Bounty; yet others fighting in Allah's Cause. So recite as much of the Quran as may be easy (for you), and perform As-Salat (Iqamat-as-Salat) and give Zakat, and lend to Allah a goodly loan, and whatever good you send before you for yourselves, (i.e. Nawafil non-obligatory acts of worship: prayers, charity, fasting, Hajj and 'Umrah, etc.), you will certainly find it with Allah,  better and greater in reward. And seek Forgiveness of Allah. Verily, Allah is Oft-Forgiving, Most-Merciful.*
> your Lord knows that you and those with you stand near two-thirds of the night, and at half-night, and He deems the night and the day. He knows that you cannot recite it, so He has mercy on you. "Some of you will be sick, and there will be some who will travel in the land seeking the bounty of Allah, and some will be those who strive in the way of Allah, so perform the prayer that is easy thereof, and perform the prayer, and pay the poor-rate, and lend to Allah in a goodly manner, and whatever good you send forward for yourselves, it is with Allah." And you will have a better reward and a greater reward, and ask forgiveness of Allah; surely Allah is Forgiving, Merciful.
> — **Quran 73:20 (inline widget)**

In the opening verse of the same sura, Allah exhorts His Messenger to remember:

> ⟪quran 73:8⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱذْكُرِ ٱسْمَ رَبِّكَ وَتَبَتَّلْ إِلَيْهِ تَبْتِيلًۭا ‎⟫
> *And remember the Name of your Lord and devote yourself to Him with a complete devotion.*
> And pronounce the name of your Lord and devote yourselves to Him.
> — **Quran 73:8 (inline widget)**

Here, the word "God" can also mean "Lord" and "God" can also be his name. The next meaning of this verse would be to mention the name of your Lord and come to Him separately from all others. In this sense, devotion to the name of Allah is devotion to Allah Almighty Himself. Allah Himself is the greatest of all linguistic statements and forms, but He is accessible through His names. Names that are not created by man, but which Allah Himself has chosen for Himself. Ignorance of these names is in fact indifference to Allah, as it has been pointed out:

> ⟪quran 58:19⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱسْتَحْوَذَ عَلَيْهِمُ ٱلشَّيْطَنُ فَأَنسَىٰهُمْ ذِكْرَ ٱللَّهِ ۚ أُو۟لَٓئِكَ حِزْبُ ٱلشَّيْطَنِ ۚ أَلَآ إِنَّ حِزْبَ ٱلشَّيْطَنِ هُمُ ٱلْخَسِرُونَ ‎⟫
> *&nbsp;Shaitan (Satan) has overtaken them. So he has made them forget the remembrance of Allah. They are the party of Shaitan (Satan). Verily, it is the party of Shaitan (Satan) that will be the losers!*
> Satan has got the better of them, and he has made them forget the remembrance of Allah. They are Satan's faction. Unquestionably, Satan's party will be the losers.
> — **Quran 58:19 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 63:9⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ لَا تُلْهِكُمْ أَمْوَلُكُمْ وَلَآ أَوْلَدُكُمْ عَن ذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ وَمَن يَفْعَلْ ذَلِكَ فَأُو۟لَٓئِكَ هُمُ ٱلْخَسِرُونَ ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Let not your properties or your children divert you from the remembrance of Allah. And whosoever does that, then they are the losers.*
> O you who believe! Let not your wealth or your children divert you from the remembrance of Allah. And whoever does that, then those! they are the losers.
> — **Quran 63:9 (inline widget)**

The relationship between devotion to Allah and His names is found in Maulana Ali's saying: ⟪ar-quote:من أحب شئی لھج بذکرہ⟫ "He who loves something, mentions it with passion." ⟪ar:لھج⟫It means 'to dedicate', and also to 'repeat over and over again'. And indeed, one should constantly mention the name of Allah with remembrance, heart and tongue, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) said in Du'a' al-Kamil: ⟪ar-quote:لھِجَ بہ لسانِ من ذکرک⟫ "My tongue has dedicated itself to Your remembrance." And he said: ⟪ar-quote:عِج الِّساَنِ بِذِکرِکَ لَھِجاً⟫ "Make my tongue eager for Your remembrance." In another supplication, the Prophet (s) described the remembrance of Allah as an act and said: ⟪ar-quote:یا من اسمہ دواؤٌ و ذکرہ شفاؤٌ⟫ "O him whose name is medicine and whose remembrance is healing."

Here, the name of Allah does not mean a word, or a name like other names, but a cure for the disease of error established at the birth of man. It is the remedy for the negligence that has become his nature. But just as taking medicine cures a disease, and not contemplating it, it is not beneficial to think and contemplate only the names of Allah. It is necessary to mention the names of Allah. Allaah has called the Qur'an a remembrance and said, "Remember the Qur'an often, i.e., recite the Qur'an often." And this hadith of the Messenger of Allah presents the remembrance of Allah as an action. Abdullah bin Basr narrates that a man said to the Messenger of Allah (Sallallahu alaihi wa sallam): "O Messenger of Allah! The laws of Islam are too much for me. So tell me one thing I can catch! He said, "May your tongue always be moist with the remembrance of Allah." This verse of the Qur'an is also worth mentioning:

> ⟪quran 33:41-43⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ ٱذْكُرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ ذِكْرًۭا كَثِيرًۭا ‎ ‏وَسَبِّحُوهُ بُكْرَةًۭ وَأَصِيلًا ‎ ‏هُوَ ٱلَّذِى يُصَلِّى عَلَيْكُمْ وَمَلَٓئِكَتُهُۥ لِيُخْرِجَكُم مِّنَ ٱلظُّلُمَتِ إِلَى ٱلنُّورِۚ وَكَانَ بِٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ رَحِيمًۭا ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Remember Allah with much remembrance. And glorify His Praises morning and afternoon [the early morning (Fajr) and 'Asr prayers]. He it is Who sends Salat (His blessings) on you, and His angels too (ask Allah to bless and forgive you), that He may bring you out from darkness (of disbelief and polytheism) into light (of Belief and Islamic Monotheism). And He is Ever Most Merciful to the believers.*
> O you who believe! Remember Allah much, and glorify Him morning and evening. It is He who sends His mercy upon you, and His angels, that He may bring you out of darkness into the light, and He is Most Merciful to the believers.
> — **Quran 33:41-43 (inline widget)**

In this verse, the remembrance of the believers, and the unity of prayer and the blessings of Allah (coming from darkness to light) are worth considering. Allaah says (interpretation of the meaning):

> ⟪quran 2:152⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَٱذْكُرُونِىٓ أَذْكُرْكُمْ وَٱشْكُرُوا۟ لِى وَلَا تَكْفُرُونِ ‎⟫
> *Therefore remember Me (by praying, glorifying, etc.). I will remember you, and be grateful to Me (for My countless Favours on you) and never be ungrateful to Me.*
> So remember Me, I will remember you, and be grateful to Me, and do not be ungrateful.
> — **Quran 2:152 (inline widget)**

Maulana Ali says in a sermon that whoever mentions Allah, Allah revives his heart and illuminates his inner substance (lip). This word reminds us of the verses of the Qur'an in which it says, "O Awli al-Bab" (those who possess substance).

> ⟪quran 3:190-191⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّ فِى خَلْقِ ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ وَٱخْتِلَفِ ٱلَّيْلِ وَٱلنَّهَارِ لَآيَتٍۢ لِّأُو۟لِى ٱلْأَلْبَبِ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ يَذْكُرُونَ ٱللَّهَ قِيَمًۭا وَقُعُودًۭا وَعَلَىٰ جُنُوبِهِمْ وَيَتَفَكَّرُونَ فِى خَلْقِ ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ رَبَّنَا مَا خَلَقْتَ هَذَا بَطِلًۭا سُبْحَنَكَ فَقِنَا عَذَابَ ٱلنَّارِ ‎⟫
> *Verily! In the creation of the heavens and the earth, and in the alternation of night and day, there are indeed signs for men of understanding. Those who remember Allah (always, and in prayers) standing, sitting, and lying down on their sides, and think deeply about the creation of the heavens and the earth, (saying): "Our Lord! You have not created (all) this without purpose, glory to You! (Exalted be You above all that they associate with You as partners). Give us salvation from the torment of the Fire.*
> in the creation of the heavens and the earth, and in the alternation of night and day, there are signs for men of understanding, those who remember Allah standing, sitting, and lying on their sides, and reflect on the creation of the heavens and the earth, saying: Our Lord! Thou hast not created this for vain; exalted be He above all faults; therefore save us from the chastisement of the Fire.
> — **Quran 3:190-191 (inline widget)**

This verse also clearly shows the relationship between remembrance and thought. The act of dhikr enlivens the heart, which awakens consciousness, which increases the ability to contemplate the verses of Allah (creation and self). When a person mixes love in this thought, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) said, "Whoever loves something, he mentions it with passion." All of this establishes a circle of faith, within which each part strengthens the other. The more a person thinks seriously about the names of Allah, the more he begins to see the beauty of these names, and begins to love Allah. The more a person loves Allah, the more he mentions His names, the more one remembers the names of Allah, the more he understands the secrets hidden in the verses of Allah. That is, thought leads to an increase in remembrance, and remembrance leads to an increase in thought!

Zikr is the pinnacle of all acts of worship, and there are different forms of standing, bowing, prostrating, and silence, humility, fear, and a low voice. All acts of worship require time, time and place, but dhikr can happen at any time, in every house and in any situation, so it is not a separate act like other acts of worship, rather it should be included in a person's daily routine. Imam Ja'far al-Sadiq (a.s.) said, "There is a limit to every action that is reached and it is terminated except the remembrance of Allah." Allah has made certain religious obligations obligatory on man. The one who fulfills these duties reaches their limits. For example, whoever fasts for thirty days in the city of Allah, he has reached his limits. O you who believe! Remember Allah often! My family, Muhammad Baqir (a.s.) used to eat and also engage in the remembrance of Allah while walking.

In this saying, we understand the verse of the Qur'an that distracts those who neither trade nor goods engage in the remembrance of Allah. These are the people who are in a state of prayer (remembrance of Allah) at all times:

> ⟪quran 70:23⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ عَلَىٰ صَلَاتِهِمْ دَآئِمُونَ ‎⟫
> *Those who remain constant in their Salat (prayers);*
> who are steadfast in their prayers.
> — **Quran 70:23 (inline widget)**

Allaah equates prayer with the remembrance of Allaah and says:

> ⟪quran 20:14⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّنِىٓ أَنَا ٱللَّهُ لَآ إِلَهَ إِلَّآ أَنَا۠ فَٱعْبُدْنِى وَأَقِمِ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ لِذِكْرِىٓ ‎⟫
> *"Verily! I am Allah! La ilaha illa Ana (none has the right to be worshipped but I), so worship Me, and perform As&shy;Salat (Iqamat-as-Salat) for My Remembrance.*
> I am God; there is no god but I, so worship Me and establish prayer for My remembrance.
> — **Quran 20:14 (inline widget)**

Maulana Ali says that continuous remembrance of Allah is the food of the soul and the key to worship (Miftah al-Salat).

> ⟪quran 29:45⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱتْلُ مَآ أُوحِىَ إِلَيْكَ مِنَ ٱلْكِتَبِ وَأَقِمِ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ ۖ إِنَّ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ تَنْهَىٰ عَنِ ٱلْفَحْشَآءِ وَٱلْمُنكَرِ ۗ وَلَذِكْرُ ٱللَّهِ أَكْبَرُ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ يَعْلَمُ مَا تَصْنَعُونَ ‎⟫
> *Recite (O Muhammad PBUH) what has been revealed to you of the Book (the Quran), and perform As-Salat (Iqamat&shy;as&shy;Salat). Verily, As-Salat (the prayer) prevents from Al-Fahsha' (i.e. great sins of every kind, unlawful sexual intercourse, etc.) and Al-Munkar (i.e. disbelief, polytheism, and every kind of evil wicked deed, etc.) and the remembering (praising, etc.) of (you by) Allah (in front of the angels) is greater indeed [than your remembering (praising, etc.) Allah in prayers, etc.]. And Allah knows what you do.*
> recite what has been revealed to you of the Book, and be steadfast in prayer. Indeed, prayer prevents indecency and evil, and the remembrance of Allah is greater; and Allah is Aware of what you do.
> — **Quran 29:45 (inline widget)**

In this verse, prayer is described as a precautionary measure. Although prayer is described as a formality and a reasonable, it is also simultaneously unavoidable. They are paid at certain times and cannot be done at certain times. This is expressed in special movements and gestures. But the remembrance of Allah is more than that, because it is the positive substance that revives this prayer, which is free from all limitations and impurities. The virtue of the remembrance of Allah over prayer is the same as the virtue of the soul over the body. The soul does not negate the body, but surrounds it, revives it, and attains wholeness and perfection through it.<!-- section 23 (id=3604, raw_sort=23): ذکر اللہ کی حقیقت -->Now we return to the fruit of the remembrance of Allah and its main purpose, which is realization, the process by which the truth becomes a reality for us. ⟪ar:تَوَحٌُد⟫It is similar to the process of self-integration, which is assimilation of oneself with oneself, and which is different from monotheism (oneness with another). We try to understand the fruit of the remembrance of Allah by its contradictory word, which is heedlessness, forgetfulness, distraction.

Allaah strongly condemns the prayer of hypocrisy and hypocrisy, and says (interpretation of the meaning):

> ⟪quran 107:4-6⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَوَيْلٌۭ لِّلْمُصَلِّينَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ عَن صَلَاتِهِمْ سَاهُونَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ يُرَآءُونَ ‎⟫
> *So woe unto those performers of Salat (prayers) (hypocrites), Who delay their Salat (prayer) from their stated fixed times, Those who do good deeds only to be seen (of men),*
> woe to those who pray who are heedless of their prayers, and who show off.
> — **Quran 107:4-6 (inline widget)**

Similarly, Maulana Ali also forbids mentioning Allah with negligence and hypocrisy. But if the remembrance of Allah is removed from the remembrance, then it becomes a perfect remembrance, in which a person forgets himself. Here again, Maulana Ali has added two contradictory things in his statement that negligence should not be included in the dhikr and that such attention should be established so that a person becomes oblivious to himself and ⟪ar:’الفنا فی الذکر‘⟫ a state of self-consciousness is created. He says:

Do not mention Allaah carelessly, nor forget Him in your distraction, rather remember Him in full. A remembrance in which there is harmony between your heart and your tongue, and what you conceal is consistent with what you show. But you will never be able to remember it with the truth until you are heedless of your own soul in this remembrance!

This quote of yours is the essence of Sufism. This quote of yours refers to all the places from which perfect sincerity is produced. The second name of Sufism is Sadiq and Ikhlas. On the one hand, dhikr invigorates the heart, which creates sincerity, and on the other hand, sincerity is the virtue that brings perfection and perfection in dhikr. In this perfect place, the word of the tongue is completely in harmony with the intention of the heart, and there is not the slightest difference between the word and the intention. This harmony between the tongue and the heart means that the divine reality released on the tongue becomes the echo of the glorification of the heart, the heart which is the mirror of nature and where all spiritual morals are produced.

When the soul becomes completely pure and pure, and becomes one with the utterances of the intellect and the tongue, it becomes transparent to the spiritual standards (nature) embedded within it, and begins to see the treasures buried within it. These are the standards that sparkle in the heart by the remembrance of Allah, and then manifest themselves in the form of actions. Without these moral and spiritual standards, the apparent act of dhikr is negligent and unpopular. And the ignorant is the one who does not strive to be sincere and turns away from the Great Jihad, and refrains from fulfilling the commands of Allah.

Maulana Ali's quote opens the door for us to the reality of dhikr through which we can move towards the truth. To mention this highest standard, the annihilation of the self (self-neglect) is required. In order to see affiliation, it is necessary for a person to remove the veil of his self that is between the truth and himself. The beginning of knowledge is the self-effacing and its extremity is the annihilation of the self. It is as if the reality of dhikr demands a revolutionary negligence. This shows that man moves from perfection to reality of the latter, from human perfection to divine reality (Al-Haqq). The first stage is the elimination of hypocrisy, and the pursuit of sincerity, honesty, and integrity that produces human perfection. In this category, a person's own identity remains. This harmony of intention and action is called perfection. But this is mentioned through the human being himself and is therefore of a lower rank. In reality, a person's self-identity does not survive because he has become oblivious to himself. In this category, ⟪ar:’ذاکر‘⟫ the focus shifts completely away from ⟪ar:’مذکور‘⟫ the one being mentioned. The reality of dhikr becomes one with the truth. At this time, it can be said inwardly that the one who mentions the truth is Allah Himself, and it is apparently being issued on the tongue of man. At this time, the existence of man is a deception that is erased by self-mention.

In the light of this, we now return to the hadith of the Prophet (peace and blessings of Allaah be upon him) that Allah says, "My servant does not cease to be close to Me through his Nawafil until I love him." Now we know that by Nawafil you mean the remembrance of Allah. It is worth noting here that Allah is the root of every action of Zakir. Allah sees and hears the deeds of those whom He loves. And Allah does not change Himself in order to enter into a person's intentions and actions, rather He becomes one with his intention and action. In other words, the divine realities become obscured by the Zakir's soul, which makes him see beyond the suspicion of his outward existence, and he begins to understand the inner realities of the verses of the Qur'an, as he says:

> ⟪quran 37:96⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ‎⟫
> *"While Allah has created you and what you make!" *
> God has created you and what you make.
> — **Quran 37:96 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 8:17⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَلَمْ تَقْتُلُوهُمْ وَلَكِنَّ ٱللَّهَ قَتَلَهُمْ ۚ وَمَا رَمَيْتَ إِذْ رَمَيْتَ وَلَكِنَّ ٱللَّهَ رَمَىٰ ۚ وَلِيُبْلِىَ ٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ مِنْهُ بَلَآءً حَسَنًا ۚ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ سَمِيعٌ عَلِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *You killed them not, but Allah killed them. And you (Muhammad PBUH) threw not when you did throw but Allah threw, that He might test the believers by a fair trial from Him. Verily, Allah is All-Hearer, All-Knower.*
> It was not you who killed them, but it was God who killed them. And you did not throw your handful when you threw, but it was God who threw, and that He might bestow His grace on the believers. God is All-hearing, All-knowing.
> — **Quran 8:17 (inline widget)**

This was the point of the remembrance of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and Maulana Ali that in a battle, an arrow pierced his ankle. He said to the people, "When I am in a state of prostration during prayer, remove this arrow." This was done when he started the prayer and went into prostration. When he finished the prayer, he asked, "Did you take out the arrow?" It's as if you didn't even realize it. It is the highest point of mention that the physical existence of man (the feelings related to him) does not remain.

And as the Messenger of Allah said, "Kindness means to worship Allah as you see Him, and if you do not see, He sees you." The Arabic text of this hadith is such that if we pause in the middle of the phrase "in the name of ta'ri'ah", its meaning is completely changed to such that if you do not see it, you can see it. Only Allah can see the sight of Allah, not the servant. The true manifestation of Allah cannot be attained as long as any of the creatures remain in the sight of Nabda. In the story of Moses

> ⟪quran 7:143⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَمَّا جَآءَ مُوسَىٰ لِمِيقَتِنَا وَكَلَّمَهُۥ رَبُّهُۥ قَالَ رَبِّ أَرِنِىٓ أَنظُرْ إِلَيْكَ ۚ قَالَ لَن تَرَىٰنِى وَلَكِنِ ٱنظُرْ إِلَى ٱلْجَبَلِ فَإِنِ ٱسْتَقَرَّ مَكَانَهُۥ فَسَوْفَ تَرَىٰنِى ۚ فَلَمَّا تَجَلَّىٰ رَبُّهُۥ لِلْجَبَلِ جَعَلَهُۥ دَكًّۭا وَخَرَّ مُوسَىٰ صَعِقًۭا ۚ فَلَمَّآ أَفَاقَ قَالَ سُبْحَنَكَ تُبْتُ إِلَيْكَ وَأَنَا۠ أَوَّلُ ٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ ‎⟫
> *And when Musa (Moses) came at the time and place appointed by Us, and his Lord spoke to him, he said: "O my Lord! Show me (Yourself), that I may look upon You." Allah said: "You cannot see Me, but look upon the mountain if it stands still in its place then you shall see Me." So when his Lord appeared to the mountain, He made it collapse to dust, and Musa (Moses) fell down unconscious. Then when he recovered his senses he said: "Glory be to You, I turn to You in repentance and I am the first of the believers." *
> And when Moses came to Our appointed time, and his Lord spoke to them, he said, "My Lord, show me that I may look at You." He said, "You do not see Me, but if it stays still, then You will see Me." Then when his Lord showed light to the mountain, He made it to pieces. Then when he regained consciousness, he said, "Glory be to You! I repent to You, and I am the first of the believers."
> — **Quran 7:143 (inline widget)**

The reflection of Al-Haqq's brilliance made Moses unconscious. God did not shine on Moses, but He shone on the mountain, which Moses could not bear.

Once, one of the companions of the Prophet Abu al-Darda saw that Ali was lying in a garden in Medina and his body was completely motionless and lifeless. He went to Hazrat Fatima's house to refresh her. She said, "My husband Ali has not passed away, but he must have fainted for fear of God." They often have this condition. Fear here means the knowledge of God's greatness. Allah mentions the fear of this perfection in the Qur'an as follows:

> ⟪quran 79:40-41⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَأَمَّا مَنْ خَافَ مَقَامَ رَبِّهِۦ وَنَهَى ٱلنَّفْسَ عَنِ ٱلْهَوَىٰ ‎ ‏فَإِنَّ ٱلْجَنَّةَ هِىَ ٱلْمَأْوَىٰ ‎⟫
> *But as for him who feared standing before his Lord, and restrained himself from impure evil desires, and lusts. Verily, Paradise will be his abode.*
> But as for him who fears to stand before his Lord, and restrain himself from lust, his abode is Paradise.
> — **Quran 79:40-41 (inline widget)**

Although every fear is usually terrifying, this fear of God is not terrifying but beautiful. This fear gives a person the power of attraction in truth. As it is often said in Sufism, when a person is afraid of the creature, he runs away from it, but when he is afraid of Allah, he runs towards it, as the Qur'an says:

> ⟪quran 9:118⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَعَلَى ٱلثَّلَثَةِ ٱلَّذِينَ خُلِّفُوا۟ حَتَّىٰٓ إِذَا ضَاقَتْ عَلَيْهِمُ ٱلْأَرْضُ بِمَا رَحُبَتْ وَضَاقَتْ عَلَيْهِمْ أَنفُسُهُمْ وَظَنُّوٓا۟ أَن لَّا مَلْجَأَ مِنَ ٱللَّهِ إِلَّآ إِلَيْهِ ثُمَّ تَابَ عَلَيْهِمْ لِيَتُوبُوٓا۟ ۚ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ هُوَ ٱلتَّوَّابُ ٱلرَّحِيمُ ‎⟫
> *And (He did forgive also) the three [who did not join the Tabuk expedition (whom the Prophet PBUH)] left (i.e. he did not give his judgement in their case, and their case was suspended for Allah's Decision) till for them the earth, vast as it is, was straitened and their ownselves were straitened to them, and they perceived that there is no fleeing from Allah,  and no refuge but with Him. Then, He accepted their repentance, that they might repent (unto Him). Verily, Allah is the One Who accepts repentance, Most Merciful.*
