> and to the three whose case was deferred, until when the earth, vast as it was, became straitened for them, and their souls became straitened for them, and they realized that there was no refuge from Allah, so He turned to them of His mercy, so that they might repent; surely Allah is the Acceptor of Repentance, the Merciful.
> — **Quran 9:118 (inline widget)**

This quote of Maulana Ali is an indication of his spiritual love and the connection of his consciousness with the truth, which is why, as Maulana Fatima (a.s.) said, he often falls into such a state.

Surely, Allah has a drink for His saints. When they drink it, they become intoxicated, and when they are intoxicated, they are delighted, and when they are delighted, they are blessed, and when they are blessed, they are dissolved, and when they are dissolved, they are free, and when they are free, they are pure. When they seek, they seek, and when they seek, they find (wujdu), and when they find it, they reach it, and when they arrive, they become one with Him in such a way that there is no distinction between them and their beloved.

The Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings of Allaah be upon him) said, "There have come upon them times of knowledge of perfect monotheism that no angel or prophet can bear." This feeling of monotheism is the fruit of all acts of worship, which is the sharpest of all intoxications. Zakir is going to drink this wine. In the initial stages, it seems that the servant is drinking the wine of the remembrance of the names of Allah and the servant is remembering Allah, but in the extreme degrees, Allah Himself drinks the wine of the name of His servant and begins to mention it. And this happens when a person has destroyed his soul in the remembrance of Allah. Maulana Ali says that the remembrance of Allah is not a way of speaking, nor is it a way of thinking. ⟪ar:’مذکور‘⟫ It is first released and ⟪ar:’ذاکر‘⟫ re-released (⟪ar:اول من المذکور و ثانی من الذاکر⟫).

That is, Allah is the first to remembrance, and the remembrance of man is a reflection of the remembrance of Allah, and it is the result of this divine remembrance. Allaah says (interpretation of the meaning): "Remember Me, and I will remember you." Now, if we delve deeper into the dhikr, then the command of Allah (swt) revealed by the word "Joe" ⟪ar:’کُن‘⟫ from which the whole existence was created, can also be seen in the light of dhikr. Allah took the name of the possibility and called upon it, which made it exist from the depths of the earth. Allah was the remembrance of the creation and the creation became His remembrance. The Qur'an asks us:

> ⟪quran 76:1⟫
> ⟪ar:‏هَلْ أَتَىٰ عَلَى ٱلْإِنسَنِ حِينٌۭ مِّنَ ٱلدَّهْرِ لَمْ يَكُن شَيْـًۭٔا مَّذْكُورًا ‎⟫
> *Has there not been over man a period of time, when he was nothing to be mentioned?*
> man must have come upon a time when there was no mention of it
> — **Quran 76:1 (inline widget)**

Here, man is called something that Allah has created into being. And its demise indicates that there was a time when there was no mention of it. That is, Allah did not command him to come from decay. At that time, man was known, but only God knew. This means that the remembrance of Allah for man predates the existence of man, and the mention of the formless Allah is more than man. Man mentions Allah by His names, whereas Allah mentions man by the word of a kun. But the word was not for a moment that it came into play and then faded. Rather, this word will continue to resonate in the human soul until the Day of Judgment as a witness to the divinity of Allah Almighty. Through this word, Allah breathed into the soul of existence

Hazrat Kamil asked Amir al-Mu'minin, "What is the truth?" He said: "Al-Haqeeqah is the name of exposing the glory of Allah, without any hints." In the light of the light of the known, the name of the annihilation of al-Mahoum (about whom it is to be feared) is Haqiqah. The name of the total connection with the attribute of monotheism is al-Haqiqa. It is a light emanating from the dawn of eternity, whose rays shine on the temple of monotheism.

By "temple", he refers to Allah in the place of monotheism. The names that give life to the soul and provide sustenance to it. The soul is the manifestation of the names where Allah manifests Himself in a certain way. Ibn al-'Arabi writes in his book Futuhat al-Makkiyah that all praise is due to Him who created things from scratch and negated them, and brought them into existence through the attention of His words. As a result of the attention of the Divine Word of God to possible objects, the attributes of this world come into being. That is, the spirit of possibilities is breathed into existence which is related to the body. The heart inside this body is the name of Allah who is giving it life. Every slave has a name that is derived from his master. So the slave becomes the flesh of the master, and the master becomes the heart of the slave.

This example reminds us of the saying of Amir al-Mu'minin that remembrance burns for hearts. The name (of Allah) that comes from above is reflected in the name that resonates in the heart. And this reflection occurs when the rust of the heart is cleared by the burning of the remembrance of Allah. It is the connection of an outer light with an inner light which represents the Qur'anic verse of light (Noor Ali Noor).

Now the question arises: what is the difference between the divine names, which are the origin of everything, and the names mentioned in the Qur'an? On the one hand, all creation is the Book of Allah, and all appearances are the words of this book, but on the other hand, there are special names mentioned in the Qur'an that we have been asked to glorify. Why is that? One of the answers to this is given in the Qur'an:

> ⟪quran 17:110⟫
> ⟪ar:‏قُلِ ٱدْعُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ أَوِ ٱدْعُوا۟ ٱلرَّحْمَنَ ۖ أَيًّۭا مَّا تَدْعُوا۟ فَلَهُ ٱلْأَسْمَآءُ ٱلْحُسْنَىٰ ۚ وَلَا تَجْهَرْ بِصَلَاتِكَ وَلَا تُخَافِتْ بِهَا وَٱبْتَغِ بَيْنَ ذَلِكَ سَبِيلًۭا ‎⟫
> *Say (O Muhammad PBUH): "Invoke Allah or invoke the Most Beneficent (Allah), by whatever name you invoke Him (it is the same), for to Him belong the Best Names. And offer your Salat (prayer) neither aloud nor in a low voice, but follow a way between.*
> Say, 'Call upon Allah, or call upon the Most Merciful.' Whichever name you invoke, to Him belong the Most Beautiful Names. And do not recite in your prayer in a low voice, nor in a low voice, but seek a way in between.
> — **Quran 17:110 (inline widget)**

In this verse, Allah Himself is admonishing the believers to mention the names that have been revealed in the Qur'an. All these names are completely different from the names of idols.

> ⟪quran 53:23⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنْ هِىَ إِلَّآ أَسْمَآءٌۭ سَمَّيْتُمُوهَآ أَنتُمْ وَآبَآؤُكُم مَّآ أَنزَلَ ٱللَّهُ بِهَا مِن سُلْطَنٍ ۚ إِن يَتَّبِعُونَ إِلَّا ٱلظَّنَّ وَمَا تَهْوَى ٱلْأَنفُسُ ۖ وَلَقَدْ جَآءَهُم مِّن رَّبِّهِمُ ٱلْهُدَىٰٓ ‎⟫
> *They are but names which you have named, you and your fathers, for which Allah has sent down no authority. They follow but a guess and that which they themselves desire, whereas there has surely come to them the Guidance from their Lord!*
> are naught but names which ye have invented, ye and your fathers, for which Allah has sent down no authority; they follow nothing but conjecture and desire, whereas there has come to them the guidance from their Lord.
> — **Quran 53:23 (inline widget)**

The names of idols are similar to the names of worldly appearances that are self-explanatory, or signs that have nothing to do with the actual appearance. But God's names are indirectly related to His appearance, and they are the reality of the substance He created. Therefore, these names have the power to not only inform but also have the power to transform. They have the ability to reveal the greatness and reality of Allah in the heart and intellect of man. For this reason, the existence of Allah is inevitable, because no existence is outside the scope of His existence. However, rust on the heart hides the presence of Allah, even though the heart itself is a creation of Allah.

Therefore, it is necessary to purify the heart from within through the remembrance of Allah so that the external substance can be unveiled for it. The divine names of Allah are the pinnacle of appearances, which take all the manifestations into their enclosure and they themselves are above it.  This internal and external substance can be likened to light and shadow. Both are manifestations of the same essence, but there is no relation between the two (light and shadow). As Ibn al-'Arabi said, the existence of the truth is a fixed light and all creation is the shadow of the light that follows it.

Maulana Ali says in one of his prayers, "I call you by all the names that You have chosen for Yourself." The fact that Allah Himself has named Himself is evident in the greatness and power of these names. And he said, "You will never be able to mention Him until you forget yourselves in the remembrance of Him." The question arises, what is meant by forgetting one's self and being oblivious of it? It is impossible for a conscious person to be oblivious to his own existence during his remembrance. If a person tries to forget himself, his effort will not allow him to be oblivious to himself. So it is understood that being oblivious to oneself here means paying complete attention to the names of Allah, so that there is no space or space left in the soul, soul, intellect and existence where the remembrance of Allah is not present, so that the soul can make its place in that space. And this ability to perish is obtained by the grace of Allah when a person strives to remove the dirt of rust from his heart. The rust that deprives us of the vision of Allah's Oneness which has no parallel. Allaah says to His Prophet, "We will teach you in such a way that you will never speak." Why wouldn't it be forgotten? For We will cleanse your pure heart from all rust and impurities.

> ⟪quran 87:6-7⟫
> ⟪ar:‏سَنُقْرِئُكَ فَلَا تَنسَىٰٓ ‎ ‏إِلَّا مَا شَآءَ ٱللَّهُ ۚ إِنَّهُۥ يَعْلَمُ ٱلْجَهْرَ وَمَا يَخْفَىٰ ‎⟫
> *We shall make you to recite (the Quran), so you (O Muhammad (Peace be upon him)) shall not forget (it), Except what Allah, may will, He knows what is apparent and what is hidden.*
> assuredly We shall make thee recite, and thou shalt not forget, save whom Allah wills; verily He knoweth what is manifest and what is hidden.
> — **Quran 87:6-7 (inline widget)**

And he said, "Remember your Lord when he forgets:

> ⟪quran 18:24⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِلَّآ أَن يَشَآءَ ٱللَّهُ ۚ وَٱذْكُر رَّبَّكَ إِذَا نَسِيتَ وَقُلْ عَسَىٰٓ أَن يَهْدِيَنِ رَبِّى لِأَقْرَبَ مِنْ هَذَا رَشَدًۭا ‎⟫
> *Except (with the saying), "If Allah will!" And remember your Lord when you forget and say: "It may be that my Lord guides me unto a nearer way of truth than this." *
> Except that Allah wills, and remember your Lord when he forgets, and say, Perhaps my Lord will guide me to a better way than this.
> — **Quran 18:24 (inline widget)**

That is, when a person forgets everything that is not God, then he is able to remember God. If Allah is in the palace of affirmation, then man is in the palace of negation in contrast to Him. When this negation (creature) is negated, then there is complete affirmation of Allah, just as multiplying negation by negation produces affirmation.

The Creator of the Universe says, "I am the death of death!" Rumi has described Ali's sayings in his book al-Masnawi as follows: He said, "I have taken up the sword for the sake of Allah, I am a servant of Allah, and I am not subject to the commands of my body." I am the lion of God, not the lion of my desires! My deeds are a witness to my religion. In war, I am the sword of Allah which is carried by the hand of Allah. I have removed the burden of my soul from my path. I have forgotten all other than Allah. God is my sun and I am His reflection. I'm a wise man! I am the veil between Allah and His creation. I am full of pearls of Oneness like a sword adorned with jewels. I do not kill people in war, but I give them life in the Hereafter!

Allah's movement towards His servant can only be possible after denying His existence. This negation is the nothingness from which Allah Almighty created existence. That is, Allah created man out of nothing, and now man has to destroy himself and find Allah. Man is denying his existence by denying the substance that never existed (for the substance of human existence is exhausted), and by this negation he is acknowledging what has always been. As he said:

> ⟪quran 55:26-27⟫
> ⟪ar:‏كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْهَا فَانٍۢ ‎ ‏وَيَبْقَىٰ وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو ٱلْجَلَلِ وَٱلْإِكْرَامِ ‎⟫
> *Whatsoever is on it (the earth) will perish. And the Face of your Lord full of Majesty and Honour will abide forever.*
> whosoever is on the earth will perish, and there will remain the Countenance of your Lord, the Most Majestic and the Most Majestic.
> — **Quran 55:26-27 (inline widget)**

Every creature has two sides, or 'faces'. One is the divine aspect which is the reality of everything and the other is the mortal aspect which is imperishable. Therefore, the face of Allah, which is immortal, is not only the divine reality, but the reality that exists in everything. Allaah says (interpretation of the meaning):

> ⟪quran 28:88⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَدْعُ مَعَ ٱللَّهِ إِلَهًا آخَرَ ۘ لَآ إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ ۚ كُلُّ شَىْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُۥ ۚ لَهُ ٱلْحُكْمُ وَإِلَيْهِ تُرْجَعُونَ ‎⟫
> *And invoke not any other ilah (god) along with Allah, La ilaha illa Huwa (none has the right to be worshipped but He). Everything will perish save His Face. His is the Decision, and to Him you (all) shall be returned.*
> And do not invoke any other god along with Allah; there is no God except Him; all things will perish except His Face; His is the command, and it is to Him that you will be returned.
> — **Quran 28:88 (inline widget)**

Ghazali writes that it is not that objects are killed when they reach a particular place or time. Rather, they are in a state of perdition all the time. This is because everything except Allah is perfect in itself. Through the face of God, he is getting survival from the Almighty, which we see in the form of existence. His existence is not from Him Himself, but from the Face of God. Therefore, the face of Allah is the reality and everything else is deception.  Then he writes about the Sufis: "There is no power left in them except the remembrance of Allah, and they do not have the power to remember themselves." When a person reaches this place, he is in the place of annihilation and he is in the place of survival. But mortality also perishes, because the soul is heedless of itself, and neglects its own annihilation. Because if he has a sense of his own annihilation, he is aware of himself.

Al-Qashayri writes that anyone who has not tasted the loneliness of annihilation will not be able to receive the sustenance of the remembrance of Allah. Here, loneliness refers to the closeness of the self to the self, which manifests itself in the form of self-praise, desires, and ego. And this closeness cannot be removed without the remembrance of Allah. This is the reality of the dhikr which the Lord encapsulates in this short sentence that you should forget your self in the remembrance of Allah. Allaah says (interpretation of the meaning):

> ⟪quran 2:198⟫
> ⟪ar:‏لَيْسَ عَلَيْكُمْ جُنَاحٌ أَن تَبْتَغُوا۟ فَضْلًۭا مِّن رَّبِّكُمْ ۚ فَإِذَآ أَفَضْتُم مِّنْ عَرَفَتٍۢ فَٱذْكُرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ عِندَ ٱلْمَشْعَرِ ٱلْحَرَامِ ۖ وَٱذْكُرُوهُ كَمَا هَدَىٰكُمْ وَإِن كُنتُم مِّن قَبْلِهِۦ لَمِنَ ٱلضَّآلِّينَ ‎⟫
> *There is no sin on you if you seek the Bounty of your Lord (during pilgrimage by trading, etc.). Then when you leave 'Arafat, remember Allah (by glorifying His Praises, i.e. prayers and invocations, etc.) at the Mash'ar-il-Haram. And remember Him (by invoking Allah for all good, etc.) as He has guided you, and verily, you were, before, of those who were astray.*
> it is no sin upon you to seek the bounty of your Lord. Then, when you return from 'Arafat, remember Allah at the Sacred Place, and remember Him as He has made known to you, and before that you were of the astray.
> — **Quran 2:198 (inline widget)**

Here, guidance refers to elevation in the level of remembrance. The first is the mention of language, which is related to the self. Then there is the mention of the heart, which is related to worship, then there is the mention of the mysteries, which are related to the insight of worship, and then there is the mention of the soul, which is related to worship.

The first ⟪ar:’ذکر السان‘⟫ is that which relates to the self, and then ⟪ar:’ذکر القلب‘⟫ that which relates to the acts of worship that release the grace of Allah.  Then ⟪ar:’ذکر السر‘⟫ there is the secret, which is related to the sight of the worship from which the truths of the divine attributes are revealed, then ⟪ar:’ذکر الروح‘⟫ there is the contemplation of the essence in the light emanating from the sight, then ⟪ar:’ذکر الکھفی‘⟫ there is the hidden, which is related to the beauty of the origin in which the duality exists, and finally the mention of the original, which is related to the true vision which is related to the end of duality is born. Maulana Ali says:

Do not abandon dhikr because you do not feel the presence of Allah in it, because it is better for you not to find Him in your remembrance than for you to forget Him. He will lead you away from negligence to the Prophet, and from there to the dhikr in which everything except what is mentioned disappears. And it is not difficult for Allah to do so.

Ibn al-'Ajba writes in his book Hakam that the more a person is destroyed in the name of Allah, the more he errs in the knowledge of the 'original'. He writes, "The name of Allah is the joy of my heart and it is the coolness of my eyes." Any caste is named, and true happiness always comes from the essence of any thing, not its name.  Imam Ja'far al-Sadiq (a.s.) said:

The name of Allah is separate from His Essence, and everything on which His name appears is a creation, so it is separate from Allah. Everything that is described is a creature, and the Creator cannot be described within the limits of the name of his creation. There are ninety-nine names of God. If the name and the caste were one, each name would be one God. But Allah is the One to whom His names point, and they are separate from Him and His creation.

Each name refers to a caste on the one hand and identifies that caste, while on the other hand, the name also has its own identity. For example, Rahim, Karim, and Sattar identify Allah, but these names also have an identity of their own, which is separate from Rahim, Karim, and Karim from Sattar. The separation of these names from each other indicates their limitation. Although they are real in themselves, they become superstitious and miraculous in the sight of Allah, and their status before Allah becomes an 'imagined reality'. The real reality of all names goes back to the Self, which is Allah. That is, if we look at it from one point of view, there is a difference between the name and the caste, but in the second respect the two are the same. In one sense, the name is nothing but only a divine attribute of the caste, while in the second sense, the name is a name that is spoken through words. For example, Rahim has an origin which is mercy, and there is an origin of Karim which is karma. So Rahim is the name of Mercy (caste), and Karim is the name of Karam (caste). In this case, both the name and the caste are the same.

The attributes disappear into the caste because they become one with the caste, and they do not exist of their own, and this is the reality of monotheism. After this knowledge, the word of sincerity no longer exists because all the gods have merged into the essence of Allah and have disappeared. The meaning of this word is: there is no reality except the real reality (self). From this point of view, only ⟪ar:’اللہ‘⟫ one remains, because Allah is the One who has no equal, and no one can know Him except Allah.

The Messenger of Allah (s.a.w.a.) is an example of a perfect human being. Maulana Ali says, "We are the most beautiful names of Allah." ⟪ar:ھو علامۃ العظمی و آیاتہ الکبری⟫ The Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings of Allaah be upon him) said: "Whoever sees me has seen the truth." So the Messenger of Allah, Ali and the Imams (a.s.) are the ones who manifested these divine attributes to human beings in the physicality of human beings. These beings are the mirrors in which the divine attributes are reflected. The brighter the light of the truth is upon them, the brighter the reflection will be in this perfect man.

In the first sermon of Nahj al-Balagha, Maulana Ali says: "The perfection of sincerity is to purify it from all attributes, because every attribute bears witness to its own attributes." So whoever describes the attribute of Allah has taken it as the attribute of Allah, and whoever thinks it is a pair, he has created a duality, and whoever has created a duality has divided it into parts, and whoever divides it into parts, he is ignorant of it.

Maulana Ali's statement here that purifying Allah from His attributes is monotheism, does not mean that these divine attributes do not exist, but the purpose is to deny the notion that these attributes are autonomous and external, and are attached to the truth separately. Or that these attributes exist outside of Allah, or that the attributes are separate from the real self. Allah is the One whose attributes have no limit. What is being denied here is that the reality of any attribute of Allah cannot be captured in the human imagination and lexicon. If these divine attributes are not separate from the Essence, and if Allah's Essence is eternal and unlimited, then it is proved that the attributes are also infinite. When the self cannot be understood, the attributes cannot be understood.

In one sense, it is to admit the attribute, and in the other sense, to deny it. The acknowledgment that attributes are not separate from the self, and the denial that these attributes cannot be incorporated into our thoughts and concepts. This is the relationship between the human soul and the truth. Man himself is desolate and has no existence, but on the other hand, he is not separated from the truth, while he becomes oblivious to himself in his worship.  When man ceases to exist, then the existence of Allah remains. Although there is a great deal of contradiction in this, it is the fact that the sense of the perfect existence of the truth is connected with the feeling of the non-existence of the self.

The Prophet (peace and blessings of Allaah be upon him) said, "Laylat al-Mi'raj, I have learned the true meaning of the names, and I have seen them return to an object and an entity." Masmi was what I saw, and my own existence was mine. For my journey was in me, and was pointing to me, and through it I came to know that I am a pure slave who has not the slightest trace of divinity.

Similarly, when Maulana Ali describes his greatness in his sermons, he is actually describing the greatness of Allah, which is being revealed through him. They are the embodiment of Allah's greatness, and His greatness is the highest standard of self-denial. Someone said to Imam Ja'far al-Sadiq (a.s.), "You are arrogant!" He said, "I am not arrogant, for greatness is only a punishment for Allah." I have completely cleansed the field of my self from arrogance. It has been replaced by the greatness of God. As long as the selfish arrogance exists, the existence of the Divine Greatness (in this place) is impossible, and when there is pride through the existence of the Divine Greatness. At this point, the divine attributes, on the mirror of the self, which has been transparently made transparent by divine realities, shine more strongly and faster. And this burning was created when I cleansed the dust of ego and selfish desires⟪ar:ھوی⟫ from the mirror of my heart.

Now let us return to the hadith of Qudsi, that my servant moves towards my closeness through my obligatory duties, which are dearer to me the most, and does not stop receiving my closeness through Nawafil until I love him. And when I begin to love him, I become his hearing with which he hears, his sight with which he sees, his hands with which he holds, and his feet with which he walks.

Let us now consider the contradiction of this hadith. On the one hand, the most beloved act of a person in the sight of Allah is duties, but on the other hand, the Nawafil of the servant is the reason for his closeness to Allah, due to which Allah begins to love this servant. A love that is embedded in the senses of the person and his powers, which reflects monotheism.  This contradiction can be removed from the notion that when Allah loves His obligatory duties, He is loving something that is separate from His essence. But when Allah loves His servant, the servant who has become oblivious of himself in his remembrance of Him, is manifold because that servant has become the manifestation of Allah because he has become one with Allah. So at that time, the love of the servant of Allah becomes the love of Allah's self. God wants to know Himself, so He created this world. When a person denies his self in the remembrance of Allah and the knowledge of Allah, then the command of Allah to know himself is fulfilled.

Maulana Ali says, "It is raining from me, and no bird can fly to me!" It rains from you because you have become one with the source of this knowledge. Allaah says (interpretation of the meaning):

> ⟪quran 76:5-6⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّ ٱلْأَبْرَارَ يَشْرَبُونَ مِن كَأْسٍۢ كَانَ مِزَاجُهَا كَافُورًا ‎ ‏عَيْنًۭا يَشْرَبُ بِهَا عِبَادُ ٱللَّهِ يُفَجِّرُونَهَا تَفْجِيرًۭا ‎⟫
> *Verily, the Abrar (pious, who fear Allah and avoid evil), shall drink a cup (of wine) mixed with water from a spring in Paradise called Kafur. A spring wherefrom the slaves of Allah will drink, causing it to gush forth abundantly.*
> the righteous will drink a cup of wine wherein is a spring of camphor, a fountain from which the servants of Allah will drink, causing it to gush forth.
> — **Quran 76:5-6 (inline widget)**

This camphor wine is in fact the essence of Allah. These people will increase the source of this wine because it is the wine of camphor itself, and there is no duality in it and in this wine. The remembrance of Allah not only removes the dust of the heart and gives it life, but also erases the name and trace of duality by the grace of the mentioned one. He purifies the heart from all kinds of shirk and establishes the principle of monotheism. To understand the reality of this is to negate all other apparent facts.

On the one hand, a person knows Allah through the fact that it is not possible to know Him, because He is beyond the veil of the universe, and on the other hand, in the remembrance of Allah, when a person becomes oblivious of himself, the distinction between the Creator and the creature disappears. At that time, the soul of the person does not change with anything else, rather that state of self becomes a state of decay. Its existence vanishes and only consciousness remains, which does not belong to anything, and does not belong to any entity. At that time, the person reaches the position of Arif Billah (attaining knowledge through Allah), otherwise he remains in the position of (knowledge of Allah). As Maulana Ali said, "Know Allah through Allah! The purpose of the remembrance of Allah is not only to make a person forget everything except Allah, but also to understand that there is nothing but Allah, as Ali (a.s.) said: "When the heart is enlightened by the remembrance of Allah, then the state of seeing after being blind and hearing after being deaf is created." Wherever he looks, he sees the face of God.

> ⟪quran 2:115⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلِلَّهِ ٱلْمَشْرِقُ وَٱلْمَغْرِبُ ۚ فَأَيْنَمَا تُوَلُّوا۟ فَثَمَّ وَجْهُ ٱللَّهِ ۚ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ وَسِعٌ عَلِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *And to Allah belong the east and the west, so wherever you turn yourselves or your faces there is the Face of Allah (and He is High above, over His Throne). Surely! Allah is All-Sufficient for His creatures' needs, All-Knowing.*
To God belong > the East and the West. Whichever way you turn, there is the Face of God. God is All-embracing, All-knowing.
> — **Quran 2:115 (inline widget)**

> ⟪quran 24:41⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَلَمْ تَرَ أَنَّ ٱللَّهَ يُسَبِّحُ لَهُۥ مَن فِى ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ وَٱلطَّيْرُ صَٓفَّتٍۢ ۖ كُلٌّۭ قَدْ عَلِمَ صَلَاتَهُۥ وَتَسْبِيحَهُۥ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ عَلِيمٌۢ بِمَا يَفْعَلُونَ ‎⟫
> *See you not (O Muhammad PBUH) that Allah, He it is Whom glorify whosoever is in the heavens and the earth, and the birds with wings out-spread (in their flight). Of each one He (Allah) knows indeed his Salat (prayer) and his glorification, [or everyone knows his Salat (prayer) and his glorification], and Allah is All-Aware of what they do.*
> do you not see that all those who are in the heavens and the earth, and the birds with outspread wings, glorify Allah? Each one knows its prayer and its glorification, and Allah knows what they do.
> — **Quran 24:41 (inline widget)**

In his sermons, Amir al-Mu'minin says: "I am the sign of Allah Almighty! I know the secrets of God! I'm the limit of all limits! I am a companion of the rays of God's divine glory! I am the first, I am the last, I am the outward, I am the inside! I am the face of God! I am the mirror of God, His pen and His tablet! I am the one who is called Alijah in the Gospels! I am the one in whose possession are the mysteries of the Messenger of Allah!

Although these words create the concept of shirk for the outward worshipper, the people of the inner self understand the true meaning of these words. Only if we first say that I am a sign of Allah Almighty! If you understand it, everyone else will automatically understand. In this sermon, Maulana Ali is identifying himself with the knowledge of Allah, not with his own knowledge of Allah. The knowledge that Allah has about Himself is not the knowledge that man has about Allah. Knowledge, knowledge and knowledge become one when they reach the place of this great knowledge, just as knowledge and existence become one when they reach the pinnacle of consciousness.  At this point, the scholar becomes self-aware, and knowledge is the consciousness that the truth has about itself. And consciousness has access to this knowledge when it destroys every particle of its existence in Allah. One has to forget oneself to remember God. In order to become the knowledge of Allah, everything has to be what Allah Himself is.  At that time, man himself becomes a ray of divine greatness. All mysteries ⟪ar:’السر‘⟫ are hidden in the Ultimate Secret, which is the essence and essence of Allah, which encompasses all the Names within Him. That is why you say that I am the first, I am the last, I am the outward, I am the inner.

Then you call yourself the face of God. This quote of yours can be understood in the light of the fact that you compare yourself to a mirror. When a person looks in the mirror, the mirror ceases to exist. All the attention of the viewer is on the face seen in the mirror. He doesn't even realize the existence of the mirror. That is, the mirror loses its identity. On the contrary, when the focus is on the mirror, one cannot see the inside of it. So the mirror is identified with the form that the 'I' is seeing. At this time, both the mirror and the shape become one, even though they are two separate objects at the same time. As long as a person's attention is on the mirror, he is wearing a veil for the face, but as soon as he looks at the face, the veil rises and reveals his obedience. Neglecting the existence of the mirror is the opposite of the annihilation of man, and focusing on the image in the mirror is the opposite of the remembrance of Allah.

Here again, we see a contradiction. Wali Allah, who knows that they are the opposite of annihilation and destruction before the divinity of Allah, are the ones who correctly interpret the name and attributes of Allah. The attributes that belong to God are not theirs. This is the reason why these saints and Safyan represent the beautiful names of Allah. The light of these attributes shines through them because they have burned the mirror of their heart with the remembrance of Allah, and they have erased all stains of egoism. Physicality cannot stop them from reflecting this light. These are the beings whose hearts are living in heaven while their bodies are working in this world. Even while living in this world, their lives have been destroyed, as Allah has said:

> ⟪quran 29:64⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَمَا هَذِهِ ٱلْحَيَوٰةُ ٱلدُّنْيَآ إِلَّا لَهْوٌۭ وَلَعِبٌۭ ۚ وَإِنَّ ٱلدَّارَ ٱلْآخِرَةَ لَهِىَ ٱلْحَيَوَانُ ۚ لَوْ كَانُوا۟ يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫
> *And this life of the world is only amusement and play! Verily, the home of the Hereafter, that is the life indeed (i.e. the eternal life that will never end), if they but knew*
> And the life of this world is naught but a sport and a pastime; and the life of the Hereafter, if they but knew.
> — **Quran 29:64 (inline widget)**

Therefore, their instincts are always associated with divine realities. When Maulana Ali was struck by the sword of Ibn Muljam, he instinctively said: "I have succeeded in swearing by the Lord of the Ka'bah." At the moment of his death, there was nothing but the remembrance of Allah. There was no god but Allah on his tongue. You died on the same miracle on which you lived your life. On the teachings of the Messenger of Allah who said, "The most mysterious death is when you die in a state where your tongue is moist with the remembrance of Allah."<!-- section 24 (id=5722, raw_sort=24): The Spirit Of The Intellect -->Our purpose is to outline some of the key dimensions of the spiritual ethos of Maulana Ali, with particular stress on its intellectual aspects. Additionally, we will demonstrate the pivotal role played by the intellect (*al-Aql*) in the elaboration and assimilation of Maulana Ali's spiritual teachings. One of our key aims here, is to show something of the '**spirit of the intellect**' in the worldview of Maulana Ali. A spirit that not only "comprises" the activities of the rational mind, but "surpasses" it, encompassing domains not nowadays associated with the intellect; domains such as moral behavior and aesthetic sensibility. We also hope to demonstrate the manner in which this spiritual view of the intellect is directly related to the Qur'anic concept of the spirit (*al-Ruh*), and to explore some of the fruits of engaging deeply with this unifying spirit proper to the intellect.

It may be useful at the outset to clarify our preference for the word 'intellect' rather than 'reason' to translate the word *Aql*. What we wish to evoke here is the original meaning of the Latin word *intellectus.*Intellect is that, which is capable of a direct contemplative vision of transcendent realities. Reason on the other hand, is of an indirect, discursive nature, that is related to discourses or modes of discourse. Reason works with logic, and arrives at only the mental concepts of those realities. But through intellect, one is able to contemplate or 'see' the Absolute, whereas with reason, one can only think about it.

It is important to stress three factors which are inherent to the spirit of the intellectual perspective being considered here. These are the centrality of revelation, the harmony between revelation and the intellect, and the distinction between the intellect (conceived as the principle of the articulation of consciousness) and reason

To begin with the first, one must assert at the outset that everything about Maulana Ali's life and his teachings is centred on the Quranic revelation and its embodiment in the Prophet's conduct. Indeed, both the thought and life of Maulana Ali can be read as a kind of spiritual commentary, a *Taweel*, on the sacred text. On the doctrinal plane, it can be asserted with confidence that Maulana Ali was one who had an 'innate aptitude' for performing the task of *tawil*. On the existential plane also, his life can be read as a dramatic unfolding of the inner meaning of the revealed text, from his birth in the most holy shrine of the Kaaba to his martyrdom in the mosque of Kufa. Maulana Ali's refusal to stop short at the superficial surface of things, be it religious, ethics, politics, manifested an unflinching fidelity to the sacred substance of the religion. A fidelity which entailed not only intellectual penetration inwardly, but also combative resistance outwardly. The saying of the Prophet (PBUH) is of considerable importance in this connection: Ali will  fight for the taweel of the Quran as I fought for its tanzil.

As mentioned earlier, Maulana Ali's short caliphate was dominated by bloody civil wars. It can well be argued that all three of these wars were indeed fought for the sake of the correct interpretation and application of the Quran; the clarification of its fundamental message (*tawheed*); and the realization of this oneness on all spiritual and social levels. This claim is substantiated in a graphic manner by Maulana Ali's response to a bedouin who, just as the battle of the Camel (*al-Jamal*) was about to begin, came to him and said, 'O Commander of the Faithful! Do you say that Allah is one?' Those present remonstrated with the bedouin, telling him that this was neither the time nor the place for such questions. Maulana Ali however, intervened: 'Leave him for surely what the bedouin wishes is what we wish for the people.'

We can begin our reflections on the spirituality of Maulana Ali by considering his response to the bedouin. A response which relates to the principle of right intention taking priority over outward action, whatever that action may be. For Maulana Ali, the most fundamental intention motivating his every action has been knowledge of the true nature of the ultimate reality. Whether religious in the ordinary sense, or military as in the present context. What Maulana 'wishes for the people' then, is this knowledge, which must lie at the very heart of all concerns, motivations and actions, whether on the battlefield or the prayer rug. Thus, there is no time or place where this question—What do you mean by saying Allah is one?' is irrelevant, or out of place. It was for the sake of the correct knowledge of the divine, that Maulana Ali was fighting in the first place. Also, in fulfilment of the prophecy of the Prophet just mentioned.

On the very field of battle, then, Maulana Ali gives a discourse on the meaning of divine oneness. The very first part of Maulana Ali's reply contains a key to the understanding of his whole spiritual ethos. He refutes the notion of Allah's oneness being in any way a 'numerical' or 'countable' oneness. He tells the bedouin that it is not permissible to say 'one' while having in mind any numerical conception, for 'that which has no second does not enter into the category of numbers' .

'That which has no second' is not just a divinity to which no other partner can be ascribed. Instead, it is that reality which has no 'otherness'. The Real, al-Haqq which is both transcendent and immanent, beyond all 'things', and manifested by all 'things', at once inaccessible and inalienable. In these few words, Maulana Ali creates a shift of consciousness (for those who have 'ears to hear'), from the dogmatic notion of one God versus many gods; to the mystical apprehension of the one and only Reality, in the face of which everything else is but an appearance. All things become perceived as so many outward phenomena which call out to be deciphered. They appear as many signs (ayat) pointing to that of which they are manifestations. Retracing these appearances back to their source and origin is the literal meaning of Tawil: returning back to the *Awwal*(the First). On one hand, the 'Real' is described as being the beginning and end of all things, the apparent and the hidden; there is nothing in being but this one Reality.

Surah Al-Hadid { 57:3 } · Surah Al-Hadid ·  · { 57:3 }
Surah Al-Hadid ·  · { 57:3 }
He is the first, the last, the noon, and the inward, and He knows everything.
He is the First and the Last, the Outward and the Inward. And He is the All-Knower of every thing. 3

On the other hand, apparent multiplicity is to be 'brought back' to real oneness. As Allah says.....

Surah Al-Faslat ( 41:53 } · Surah Al-Faslat ·  · { 41:53 }
Surah Al-Faslat ·  · { 41:53 }
We will show them Our sign in the horizons and in themselves until it becomes clear to them that it is the right 53
We will show them Our Signs in the universe, and in their ownselves, until it becomes manifest to them that this is the truth.  53

In one saying attributed to Maulana Ali, there is a reference to the Prophet as the first of those who were taught by Allah the science of *tawil*. And the prophet then taught Maulana Ali. According to the Prophet, 'Truly, Ali is with the Qur an, and the Qur'an is with Ali.' In another famous saying, Maulana Ali claimed to be able to load seventy camels with the pages of the commentary on Surah AlFateha. And Maulana Ali's cousin, Ibn Abbas, claims to have learnt the science of interpretation from Ali.

In this connection, the following saying of Maulana Ali is of fundamental importance: 'Quran consists of a book inscribed between two covers; it speaks not with a tongue, it cannot do without an interpreter (⟪ar:لا بُدَّا مِنَ التَّرجُمٰن⟫).' This exchange between revelation and the intellect is further underlined in the saying, 'The prophet of a man is the interpreter of his intellect (⟪ar:رَاسُ الرَّجَل تَرجُمان عَقلِہ⟫). Elsewhere, we find an explicit correspondence between the intellect and the 'inner' messenger. The intellect is 'the messenger of the Real'.

Thus, Maulana Ali's teachings, which express his spiritual ethos, should be read essentially as creative interpretations of the Quranic revelation. They initiate a movement from the letters of the revelation to its spirit; and from the spirit of the revelation to the spirit of the Revealer.

Letters of revelation -> Spirit of Revelation -> Revealer (al-Haqq)

It can be thought of as a process of 'retracing', or going back to the source, the origin, the beginning, *al-awwal*, which will be accomplished in the measure, that the spirit of the intellect is enlivened within the interpreter. But the Revealer remains inevitability concealed (as the essence of the divine Reality), at the very same time as being revealed through the revelation. The divine Reality in itself, is too great to be described in words. Only the forms of its manifestations are susceptible to revelation. This dialectical interplay between the form and the formless, the evident and the hidden, the revealed and the concealed, and all such antinomies lie at the root of the paradoxical mode of expression, for which Maulana Ali is renowned.

Indeed, one of the most striking aspects of Maulana Ali's perspective is the way in which it reveals the hollowness of many of the false or excessively polarized dichotomies that later came to characterize, or be imposed upon Islamic thought. This dichotomy between intellect and revelation is found in various polarized ramifications, such as reason versus faith, convention (*sunna*) versus nature (*tabi'a*), imitation (*taqlid*) versus verification (*tahqiq*), piety (*taqwa*) versus inquiry (*tahqiq*), and so on. However in Maulana Ali's ethos, intellect and revelation, rather than being regarded as mutually exclusive, are complementary and, at the highest level, indeed inseparable, as truth being one. While it is clear that the human intellect cannot in any way be equated with divine revelation, the spirit animating the intellect is not restricted by human limitations. It is this spirit which perceives and grasps the divine quality of revelation.

The divine spirit articulating the form, and infusing the content of revelation must be understandable to some degree by human consciousness. If that didn't happen, revelation would be nothing more than various rules and regulations for the will, rather than a source of creative inspiration for the intellect. It cannot be too heavily stressed that divine revelation, presupposes a creative engagement with all the resources of the intellect, instead of cutting short the operations of reason and imposing some unintelligible decree. And this is what the Quran itself repeatedly calls for.

The revealed text is silent and 'speaks' only through the 'interpreter', the intellect. This view of the relationship between intellect and revelation rigorously excludes all literalism and superficiality. It excludes all attempts to confine meaning within a flat, unilateral reading. On the contrary, such a view seeks the very opposite. Rather than 'enclose' meaning, the tendency generated here helps to 'dis-close' it. To open up the inner horizons of multiple levels of meaning hidden in the text. This multi-function significance is plumbed in accordance with the depth and penetration of the intellect of the 'interpreter'. This 'prophetic' intellect, rejoins the source of revelation itself. For it is this 'inner prophet', or inmost degree of consciousness, which is the ultimate basis on which one is able to confirm as true the verses of the outer revelation. It 'validates' them experientially, and not just affirm them dogmatically. It is thus that Maulana Ali says, in the first sermon of the Nahjul Balagha, that one of the purposes of revelation, of the 'sending forth of prophets' by Allah to mankind, was 'to unearth for them the buried treasures of the intellects  (⟪ar:دفائن العقول⟫)' .

This saying constitutes one of the keys of the spiritual ethos being considered here, that the intellect is not stifled by revelation; rather, it is enlivened by it. Revelation is a loud and clear call to the spiritual depths of the intellect. It cultivates and brings to fruition the seeds of consciousness planted therein by Allah. The spirit of one's intellect, then, cannot be alien to that which descends as revelation from Allah. On the contrary, it must be fundamentally similar to it. It is for precisely this reason, that one can have absolute certainty that the revelation indeed comes from the Absolute. It is not so much a question of setting up a dichotomy between intellect or revelation, but of seeing the intellect 'as' revelation, or at least as one mode of revelation. It (intellect) is the God-given means by which the individual comes to discern, affirm and plumb the divine 'revelations' outside himself (both those of 'signs' (ayats) of scripture and those constituted by the 'signs' (ayat) of the natural world). If the human intellect can perceive and recognize revelation, it is on account of the fact that both are rooted in the same ultimate source. Prophetic revelation awakens and brings to life the depths of human intellect. It does not replace or displace the intellect. From this perspective, the revealed text is not to be seen as some extraneous source opposed to the intelligence, but rather as the objective, outward expression of the very principles that the intellect itself yields to the 'inner prophet'. Understanding by 'intellect' then does not mean simply the faculty of reasoning, but the source of consciousness articulating the human spirit.

The intellect contains unsuspected depths or 'buried treasures' — and is thus far from being exhausted by its surface operations, or the cognitions and reasonings proper to its purely mental dimension. These considerations take us once again to the relationship between intellect and reason. Just as there can be no contradiction whatsoever between **revelation**and **intellect**, likewise one must avoid setting up a false dichotomy between **reason**and **intellect**. Instead, reason should be perceived as one of the modes of the intellect. Reason no more contradicts intellect, than intellect contradicts revelation. Reason is a mode of the intellect but is not to be equated with it roughly. Similarly, one cannot reduce the universal objectivity of revelation to the subjective specificities of any one individual's intellect, or to his or her own 'private' revelation. To equate reason with intellect would be tantamount to denying the existence of the 'buried treasures' of the intellect, those dimensions that transcend rationality and are initially, 'buried' beneath, and thus hidden from, the rational surface of the intellect. The revelation constituted by the intellect is embedded within the creation of the human being. And it is this intellect, which most critically defines the human being as such.

Instead of competing the intellect against revelation, each is to be seen in the light of the other. The substance of revelation cannot be engaged except through the intellect on one hand, and the 'buried treasures' of the intellect cannot be disclosed except through revelation on the other. This understanding of the intellect brings us close to what Maulana Ali refers to as the 'heart', that inner most mode of perception which is capable of 'seeing' Allah. It is the 'heart' that can 'see' Allah, not using eyesight but the spiritual insight which is generated by the 'true principles of faith' (*haqaiq Al-Iman*). As Maulana Ali puts it, in response to the questioner asking whether he had 'seen' his Lord, 'Eyes see Him not through sight's observation, but hearts see Him through the true principles and beliefs of faith. '

To return to the relationship between the intellect and reason, one can say that between the spiritual depths of the intellect and its own rational surface there is both continuity and discontinuity. The aspect of continuity is manifested in the evident fact that all thinking begins with concepts conveying intelligible meaning. Thought is initially concerned with ideas that are rationally discernible, and these must bear some relation to the realities they express. But there is also discontinuity between the spiritual and the rational aspects of the intellect, in that reason stops short at the ideas 'de-fined'—the Arabic word for definition, *hadd*expresses both the sense of a conceptual definition and that of a limitation, a boundary. To go beyond the limits imposed by the rational act of definition, something more than reason is necessary; and this 'something more' is that which makes the ethos we are considering a spiritual one, not a rationalistic one. It is certainly 'rational' in the sense that the form of the ethos is indeed susceptible to the scrutiny of reason, but it is not 'rationalistic' inasmuch as its essence is not predicated on reason alone.

Now Maulana Ali frequently hints, in highly allusive terms, at the mysteries and the marvels (the unearthed treasures of the intellect), that he has directly witnessed by the eye of his purified heart. He also indirectly alludes to this supra-rational mode of awareness through the bewildering use of apophatic (*knowledge of God obtained through negation*) discourse and paradoxical utterances, which are abundantly found in the works attributed to him. It seems that, in this ethos, the higher the truth the deeper is the paradox. The incommensurability between the reality in itself and the human conceptions that are made of it, is effectively evoked by this creative use of paradox. Each human conception of reality needs to be 'deconstructed' first in order to then 'reconstruct'. Maulana Ali's paradoxes feed directly into modes of spiritual intuition, contemplation and realization of that which reason, on its own account, is incapable of attaining. It is this intuition and contemplation which 're-members' or 'reconstructs', the spiritual realities that transcend the categories of reason. The value of the paradoxes, antinomies (*a contradiction between two beliefs or conclusions that are in themselves reasonable*), apophasis and negation is entirely predicated on the various positive realities which the intellect can plumb, and thus become aware of its own hidden depths. The resulting consciousness does not negate reason so much as build it, and thereby reveal the limits of the sphere of operation proper to reason. It reveals that reason alone cannot 'comprehend' the higher realities, nor express them fully, no matter how indispensable it may be in initiating the cognitive movement towards those realities.

Thus, when Maulana Ali negates the possibility of human conceptions encompassing the divine Reality, what is being negated is the limitation which is the inescapable corollary (*forming a proposition that follows from one already proved*) of all such conceptions, and not the positive content, the *ma'na* or spiritual meaning of the conception itself. This conception is a necessary starting point for a process of assimilation that engages a deeper level of awareness than that 'defined' by the mind, and which therefore extends far beyond the domain of speculative thought. In this light, the negation of the limitations of human conception should be seen as the introduction to an absolute affirmation. The affirmation of the Absolute, which has no limitation. The spiritual negation of conceptual limitation is of an upward, 'constructive' order, not of a nihilistic (*rejecting all religious and moral principles in the belief that life is meaningless*) deconstructive one. Nowhere is this style of discourse more apparent than in the famous opening lines of the first sermon of the Nahj al-balagha:

Praise be to God, whose praise those who speak cannot deliver, whose graces those who count cannot number, whose rightful due those who strive cannot render; He who cannot be grasped by aspirations, nor fathomed by profound intuitions; He whose attribute has no binding limitation, no existing description, no time appointed, no term extended.

---

---

---

The divine attributes (sifa) cannot be confined to a definition (*laysa li sifatihee Haddun Mahdud*), and yet it is affirmed as real. It is described (*mawsuf*) by the very words of the Quranic revelation, even though it has no 'description'. For example, Allah is described as having attributes such as, He is the Merciful, the Compassionate, the Almighty, and so on. But Maulana Ali affirms that these very attributes cannot be defined, bounded, or described. The paradox is further sharpened when Maulana Ali speaks of the perfection of *ikhlas*. It is the 'rendering sincere', or the purification of one's devotion to Allah, and conception of Allah. It is to divest (*nafy*) Allah of all attributes. So, on one hand the attributes are affirmed, and on the other they are to be negated. The rational mind can only think of Allah in terms of the attributes, verbally expressed in the Quran. Yet here, Maulana Ali appears to negate these same attributes, thereby depriving the mind of any convenient conceptual handle by which to grasp the nature of the divine Reality. This simultaneous affirmation, and negation of the attributes, raises an apparently irresolvable contradiction. But in doing so, it enhances receptivity to a deeper mode of knowing. This style of discourse is designed to awaken a latent awareness, inscribed in the heart or the depths of the intellect. This awareness then invites the seeker to "dive" into the depths of the knowledge that is 'buried' in the intellect. This very shock of the apparent contradiction, precipitates a leap of consciousness from the formal activity of reason, to the super-rational contemplation of the spirit.

Consider the words spoken by Maulana Ali immediately after affirming that his heart had indeed witnessed Allah, not by means of outward vision but through 'the realities of faith': My Lord is not described in terms of dimension (⟪ar:بُعْد⟫), nor motion (⟪ar:حرکۃ⟫), nor rest (⟪ar:سکون⟫) nor through coming or going. He is subtle in subtlety but not described by subtlety. He is magnificent in magnificence but not described by magnificence. He is great in greatness but not described by greatness.

The attributes are again affirmed and denied. Allah possesses these attributes, but is not reducible to them. We can begin to think of Allah in terms of these categories, but we cannot reduce Him to our limited conceptions. The attributes surely afford something to the mind by which the divine nature can be understood. But this understanding is fragmentary, and never exhaustive. It therefore needs to be negated, so that a fuller understanding may be gained. The initial conceptual orientation to the divine Reality needs to be both negated and sublimated. It needs to be negated as being a mental conception, while the positive content of the conception needs to be elevated to a high rank through spiritual intuition. Only then can the two-dimensional 'portrait' defined by reason, be given the third dimension of depth. But this third dimension emerges only after the insufficiency of the rational depiction is clearly understood. Paradox produces this cognitive shock, which reveals the pretension of reason in its effort to disclose the nature of the Absolute.

One sees in Maulana Ali's discourses a repeated combination of affirmation and denial, which mirrors the negation and affirmation found in the first testimony of Islam: *La ilaha*, 'No Allah', being the negation (*nafy*); then *Illa Allah*, 'except Allah' coming as the affirmation (*Isbaat*). This helps one to see that the perfection of *ikhlas*, as described by Maulana Ali, is gained by the negation of the attributes 'in order to' affirm the infinitude of the divine Reality. Thus, each of the attributes is to be 'negated', but only insofar as it is conceived by the limited mind. Therefore negation is necessary, because at the mental level each attribute 'excludes' not only the other attributes, but also the object of attribution itself (the divine Essence). For any concep to develop in the mind, defined ideas are required. And where there are definitions, there are limits, which result in exclusions. However, the reality of the attribute is unlimited by virtue of its absolute identity with the Essence. The attribute that has been 'negated' is paradoxically affirmed as being nothing 'but' Allah: *illa Allah*. Thus, one can place each of the negated attributes in the place of the negation (*nafy*) of the first testimony, and arrive at such formulations as: *La Rahmana illa'Llah*, 'There is no All-Compassionate except Allah'; *La Raheema illa'Llah*, 'There is No All-Merciful except Allah'.

In this respect, the apparent negation of the attributes not only becomes an affirmation of their true identity, but it also disconnects any restrictive association with the poverty of mental conceptions. The attributes are not super-imposed upon the Essence, but are in fact absolutely one with it. The attributes are differentiable from the essence, only in conception and not in existence. The Essence does indeed comprise all the mentioned attributes such as greatness, subtlety, and so on, but it is also infinitely more than the sum of these attributes. These attributes are infinite, only within and as the Essence. Maulana Ali's explanation of this paradox here, can be seen in fact as a commentary of the Quranic verse:

Surah Al-Mu'minun (23:91) · Surah Al-Mu'minun ·  · { 23:91 }
Surah Al-Mu'minun ·  · { 23:91 }
Praise God for what they describe 91
Glorified be Allah above all that they attribute to Him! 91

The infinitude of Allah, requires the negation of all that the mind can conceive through reason on the human plane. But it does not negate all that the heart can 'see' through spiritual vision. This very negation on the plane of reason calls out to something deeper. This in turn, can only be understood in the light of spiritual practice, which is always assumed as the reflective, devotional or contemplative context for the hearers of Maulana Ali's sermons and discourses. The heart, which is the symbolic seat of the contemplative intelligence, calls out to be 'polished', and this is precisely what the 'remembrance of Allah' does. This is why the rememberance of Allah (*Zikr Allah*) according to Maulana Ali, is the 'most excellent form of worship'.

Interestingly, even at the level of practice there is a further paradox. Because the 'reality of the remembrance' is not attained until 'you forget yourself' in your remembrance of Allah. It is not just the rational mind and its concepts that are to be negated or 'deconstructed'. Instead, it is the individual 'soul' itself (as the locus of all cognition, rational or supra-rational), that is to be negated or 'deconstrcuted'. This final denouement, or annihilation (*fana)*, is the ultimate form of paradox.

In Maulana Ali's perspective, the intellect must be seen, first and foremost as a spiritual faculty. And the spirit must be appreciated as not only the source of the intellect, but also the source of life. Without the intellect the spirit is reduced to an unconscious existence. Conversely, without the spirit, the intellect tends towards lifeless thoughts. And this is why the Quran, describing the creation of man states, that Allah 'breathing' His spirit into Adam AS:

Surah Al-Sajjdah (32:7-9) · Surah Al-Sajjdah ·  · { 32:7-9 }
Surah Al-Sajjdah ·  · { 32:7-9 }
He who made all things good, He created him, and He began the creation of man from clay2 7 Then He made his seed 5 of his descendants2 from the waters of humiliation2 8 Then He leveled it and breathed into it of His Spirit6 and He made for you hearing and seeing and hearing for you, but little do you give thanks.
Who made everything He has created good, and He began the creation of man from clay. 7 Then He made his offspring from semen of worthless water. 8 Then He fashioned him in due proportion, and **breathed**into him the soul, and He gave you hearing, sight and hearts. Little is the thanks you give! 9

The following lines from the first sermon is one of the many passages in which this infusion of the divine spirit into man is commented upon by Maulana Ali:

Then Allah (may He be glorified), gathered up a quantity of dust, from some hard earth and some soft, some sweet earth and some salty, and poured water onto it until it was pure, then kneaded into it some moisture until it stuck together. He then fashioned from this, a form with curves and joints, limbs and parts. He compacted it until it held tightly together. He solidified it until it became as sounding clay, assigning to it a measured duration and a known consummation. Then He breathed into it of His spirit, and it stood up as a human being, endowed with intellectual powers with which to reflect, thoughts by which to conduct himself, limbs to put to service, instruments at his disposal, and knowledge with which to discern between the true and the false.

In other words, it is the 'in-spiration' (literally, the 'in-breathing' and the insertion of the spirit) of the breath of Allah's spirit, that produces consciousness and life. Death, on the contrary, is the 'ex-piration', or the departure of the spirit. Life, in the absence of the intention to be true to one's spirit, is a kind of death. It is through this spirit that inanimate unconscious matter is brought to life and given awareness of itself. It not only generates knowledge of other forms, but it also generates knowledge of the self. This intimate intertwining between the gift of life, and the capacity to know (existence which is conscious, and knowledge which is existential), is one of the foundations of any truly 'spiritual' perspective. It is not a question of contrasting the spirit with the body, but of realizing that the infusion of the spirit 'into' the body brings the body to life. It is for this reason that 'spiritual' knowledge enlivens the hearts!

Surah Al-Anfaal ( 8:24 } · Surah Al-Anqal ·  · { 8:24 }
Surah Al-Anqal ·  · { 8:24 }
O you who have believed, respond to Allah and to the Messenger if he calls you to what He greets you, and know that Allah brings a barrier between a man and his heart, and to Him you will be gathered.
O you who believe! Answer Allah and His messenger when he calls you to that which will give you life, and know that Allah comes in between a person and his heart. And verily to Him you shall be gathered. 24

According to Maulana Ali, one of the most important aspects of this 'call' from Allah to human beings is, to 'remind' them of the buried treasures of the intellect

Existence is the bestowal of the conscious spirit on the body. Hence the *Aql*or intellect, which is the principle of articulation for the spirit, is not merely a mental faculty, it is the constitution of our true life. Mental faculty is just one mode of operation of the intellect, but by no means the only one. According to the sayings of Maulana Ali, the '*aql*' is multi-faceted, comprising aspects that in our times are rarely associated with intelligence.

Being 'spiritual', then means being true to one's intellect (to the treasures buried deep within it), and not just to the rational functions operating on its surface. For Maulana Ali, the 'true intellectual' (*al- Aqil*) is the one who not only 'thinks' correctly but also 'acts' ethically, and at the deepest level seeks to 'realize' the ultimate Reality. The intellectual is defined by him, as 'one who puts all things in their proper place'. And because this is the very definition of justice also, only the true intellectual can therefore be fully 'just'. Only the only one who has the ability to see things as they 'truly are', is able to put them in their right place. Therefore, thought, action and realization, are all concern of the true intellectual - the *aqil*. Correct thinking, impeccable virtue, and authentic being are inseprably tied up with the intellect, in this spiritual ethos being considered here. These aspects of the ethos become clearer in the light of Maulana's discourse to Kumayl, to which we now turn our attention.

*Verses referenced in this topic (curated linkage from KAHSKOLE. TopicAyats — 7 of 7 not already cited above):*

> ⟪quran 8:24⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ ٱسْتَجِيبُوا۟ لِلَّهِ وَلِلرَّسُولِ إِذَا دَعَاكُمْ لِمَا يُحْيِيكُمْ ۖ وَٱعْلَمُوٓا۟ أَنَّ ٱللَّهَ يَحُولُ بَيْنَ ٱلْمَرْءِ وَقَلْبِهِۦ وَأَنَّهُۥٓ إِلَيْهِ تُحْشَرُونَ ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Answer Allah (by obeying Him) and (His) Messenger when he (PBUH) calls you to that which will give you life, and know that Allah comes in between a person and his heart (i.e. He prevents an evil person to decide anything). And verily to Him you shall (all) be gathered.*
> O you who believe! Obey Allah and the Messenger when He calls you to that matter in which you live, and know that Allah stands as a barrier between a man and his heart, and that to Him you will be gathered.
> — **Quran 8:24 (TopicAyats)**

> ⟪quran 23:91⟫
> ⟪ar:‏مَا ٱتَّخَذَ ٱللَّهُ مِن وَلَدٍۢ وَمَا كَانَ مَعَهُۥ مِنْ إِلَهٍ ۚ إِذًۭا لَّذَهَبَ كُلُّ إِلَهٍۭ بِمَا خَلَقَ وَلَعَلَا بَعْضُهُمْ عَلَىٰ بَعْضٍۢ ۚ سُبْحَنَ ٱللَّهِ عَمَّا يَصِفُونَ ‎⟫
> *No son (or offspring or children) did Allah beget, nor is there any ilah (god) along with Him; (if there had been many gods), behold, each god would have taken away what he had created, and some would have tried to overcome others! Glorified be Allah above all that they attribute to Him!*
> Allah has not begotten a son, nor is there any god besides Him; if there were, each god would have taken away what he had created, and some of them would have risen above others. Glory be to Allah, that which they describe.
